10132{_}1756{_}And the people themselves, do they attempt to understand it--to follow out my instructions?"
10132{_}1757{_}The starosta spread out his thin hands in deprecation.
10132{_}1758{_}He cringed a little as he stood.
10132{_}1759{_}He had Jewish blood in his veins, which, while it raised him above his fellows in Osterno, carried with it the usual tendency to cringe.
10132{_}1760{_}It is in the blood; it is part of what the people who stood without Pilate's palace took upon themselves and upon their children.
10132{_}1761{_}"Your Excellency," he said, "knows what they are.
10132{_}1762{_}It is slow.
10132{_}1763{_}They make no progress.
10132{_}1764{_}For them one disease is as another.
10132{_}1765{_}'Bog dal e Bog vzial,' they say.
10132{_}1766{_}'God gave and God took!'"
10132{_}1767{_}He paused, his black eyes flashing from one face to the other.
10132{_}1768{_}"Only the Moscow doctor, Excellency," he said significantly, "can manage them."
10132{_}1769{_}Paul shrugged his shoulders.
10132{_}1770{_}He rose from his seat, glancing at Steinmetz, who was looking on in silence, with his queer, mocking smile.
10132{_}1771{_}"I will go with you now," he said.
10132{_}1772{_}"It is late enough already."
10132{_}1773{_}The starosta bowed very low, but he said nothing.
10132{_}1774{_}Paul went to a cupboard and took from it an old fur coat, dragged at the seams, stained about the cuffs a dull brown--doctors know the color.
10132{_}1775{_}Such stains have hanged a man before now, for they are the marks of blood.
10132{_}1776{_}Paul put on this coat.
10132{_}1777{_}He took a long, soft silken scarf such as Russians wear in winter, and wrapped it round his throat, quite concealing the lower part of his face.
10132{_}1778{_}He crammed a fur cap down over his ears.
10132{_}1779{_}"Come," he said.
10132{_}1780{_}Karl Steinmetz accompanied them down stairs, carrying a lamp in one hand.
10132{_}1781{_}He closed the door behind them, but did not lock it.
10132{_}1782{_}Then he went upstairs again to the quiet little room, where he sat down in a deep chair.
10132{_}1783{_}He looked at the open door of the cupboard from which Paul Alexis had taken his simple disguise, with a large, tolerant humor.
10132{_}1784{_}"El Senor Don Quixote de la Mancha," he said sleepily.
10132{_}1785{_}It is said that to a doctor nothing is shocking and nothing is disgusting.
10132{_}1786{_}But doctors are, after all, only men of stomach like the rest of us, and it is to be presumed that what nauseates one will nauseate the other.
10132{_}1787{_}When the starosta unceremoniously threw open the door of the miserable cabin belonging to Vasilli Tula, Paul gave a little gasp.
10132{_}1788{_}The foul air pouring out of the noisome den was such that it seemed impossible that human lungs could assimilate it.
10132{_}1789{_}This Vasilli Tula was a notorious drunkard, a discontent, a braggart.
10132{_}1790{_}The Nihilist propaganda had in the early days of that mistaken mission reached him and unsettled his discontented mind.
10132{_}1791{_}Misfortune seemed to pursue him.
10132{_}1792{_}In higher grades of life than his there are men who, like Tula, make a profession of misfortune.
10132{_}1793{_}Paul stumbled down two steps.
10132{_}1794{_}The cottage was dark.
10132{_}1795{_}The starosta had apparently trodden on a chicken, which screamed shrilly and fluttered about in the dark with that complete abandon which belongs to chickens, sheep, and some women.
10132{_}1796{_}"Have you no light?"
10132{_}1797{_}cried the starosta.
10132{_}1798{_}Paul retreated to the top step, where he had a short-lived struggle with a well-grown calf which had been living in the room with the family, and evinced a very creditable desire for fresh air.
10132{_}1799{_}"Yes, yes, we have a little petroleum," said a voice.
10132{_}1800{_}"But we have no matches."
10132{_}1801{_}The starosta struck a light.
10132{_}1802{_}"I have brought the Moscow doctor to see you."
10132{_}1803{_}"The Moscow doctor!"
10132{_}1804{_}cried several voices.
10132{_}1805{_}"Sbogom--sbogom!
10132{_}1806{_}God be with you!"
10132{_}1807{_}In the dim light the whole of the floor seemed to get up and shake itself.
10132{_}1808{_}There were at least seven persons sleeping in the hut.
10132{_}1809{_}Two of them did not get up.
10132{_}1810{_}One was dead.
10132{_}1811{_}The other was dying of cholera.
10132{_}1812{_}A heavily built man reached down from the top of the brick stove a cheap tin paraffin lamp, which he handed to the starosta.
10132{_}1813{_}By the light of this Paul came again into the hut.
10132{_}1814{_}The floor was filthy, as may be imagined, for beasts and human beings lived here together.
10132{_}1815{_}The man--Vasilli Tula--threw himself down on his knees, clawing at Paul's coat with great unwashed hands, whining out a tale of sorrow and misfortune.
10132{_}1816{_}In a moment they were all on their knees, clinging to him, crying to him for help: Tula himself, a wild-looking Slav of fifty or thereabouts; his wife, haggard, emaciated, horrible to look upon, for she was toothless and almost blind; two women and a loutish boy of sixteen.
10132{_}1817{_}Paul pushed his way, not unkindly, toward the corner where the two motionless forms lay half concealed by a mass of ragged sheepskin.
10132{_}1818{_}"Here," he said, "this woman is dead.
10132{_}1819{_}Take her out.
10132{_}1820{_}When will you learn to be clean?
10132{_}1821{_}This boy may live--with care.
10132{_}1822{_}Bring the light closer, little mother.
10132{_}1823{_}So, it is well.
10132{_}1824{_}He will live.
10132{_}1825{_}Come, don't sit crying.
10132{_}1826{_}Take all these rags out and burn them.
10132{_}1827{_}All of you go out.
10132{_}1828{_}It is a fine night.
10132{_}1829{_}You are better in the cart-shed than here.
10132{_}1830{_}Here, you, Tula, go round with the starosta to his store.
10132{_}1831{_}He will give you clean blankets."
10132{_}1832{_}They obeyed him blindly.
10132{_}1833{_}Tula and one of the young women (his daughters) dragged the dead body, which was that of a very old woman, out into the night.
10132{_}1834{_}The starosta had retired to the door-way when the lamp was lighted, his courage having failed him.
10132{_}1835{_}The air was foul with the reek of smoke and filth and infection.
10132{_}1836{_}"Come, Vasilli Tula," the village elder said, with suspicious eagerness.
10132{_}1837{_}"Come with me, I will give you what the good doctor says.
10132{_}1838{_}Though you owe me money, and you never try to pay me."
10132{_}1839{_}But Tula was kissing and mumbling over the hem of Paul's coat.
10132{_}1840{_}Paul took no notice of him.
10132{_}1841{_}"We are starving, Excellency," the man was saying.
10132{_}1842{_}"I can get no work.
10132{_}1843{_}I had to sell my horse in the winter, and I cannot plough my little piece of land.
10132{_}1844{_}The Government will not help us.
10132{_}1845{_}The Prince--curse him!--does nothing for us.
10132{_}1846{_}He lives in Petersburg, where he spends all his money, and has food and wine more than he wants.
10132{_}1847{_}The Count Stepan Lanovitch used to assist us--God be with him!
10132{_}1848{_}But he has been sent to Siberia because he helped the peasants.
10132{_}1849{_}He was like you; he was a great barin, a great noble, and yet he helped the peasants."
10132{_}1850{_}Paul turned round sharply and shook the man off.
10132{_}1851{_}"Go," he said, "with the starosta and get what I tell you.
10132{_}1852{_}A great, strong fellow like you has no business on his knees to any man!
10132{_}1853{_}I will not help you unless you help yourself.
10132{_}1854{_}You are a lazy good-for-nothing.
10132{_}1855{_}Get out!"
10132{_}1856{_}He pushed him out of the hut, and kicked after him a few rags of clothing which were lying about on the floor, all filthy and slimy.
10132{_}1857{_}"Good God!"
10132{_}1858{_}muttered he under his breath, in English, "that a place like this should exist beneath the very walls of Osterno!"
10132{_}1859{_}From hut to hut he went all through that night on his mission of mercy--without enthusiasm, without high-flown notions respecting mankind, but with the simple sense of duty that was his.
10132{_}1860{_}These people were his things--his dumb and driven beasts.
10132{_}1861{_}In his heart there may have existed a grudge against the Almighty for placing him in a position which was not only intensely disagreeable, but also somewhat ridiculous.
10132{_}1862{_}For he did not dare to tell his friends of these things.
10132{_}1863{_}He had spoken of them to no man except Karl Steinmetz, who was in a sense his dependent.
10132{_}1864{_}English public school and university had instilled into him the intensely British feeling of shame respecting good works.
10132{_}1865{_}He could take chaff as well as any man, for he was grave by habit, and a grave man receives the most chaff most good-humoredly.
10132{_}1866{_}But he had a nervous dread of being found out.
10132{_}1867{_}He had made a sort of religion of suppressing the fact that he was a prince; the holy of holies of this cult was the fact that he was a prince who sought to do good to his neighbor--a prince in whom one might repose trust.
10132{_}1868{_}This was not the first time by any number that he had gone down into his own village insisting in a rough-and-ready way on cleanliness and purity.
10132{_}1869{_}"The Moscow doctor"--the peasants would say in the kabak over their vodka and their tea--"the Moscow doctor comes in and kicks our beds out of the door.
10132{_}1870{_}He comes in and throws our furniture into the street But afterward he gives us new beds and new furniture."
10132{_}1871{_}It was a joke that always obtained in the kabak.
10132{_}1872{_}It flavored the vodka, and with that fiery poison served to raise a laugh.
10132{_}1873{_}The Moscow doctor was looked upon in Osterno and in many neighboring villages as second only to God.
10132{_}1874{_}In fact, many of the peasants placed him before their Creator.
10132{_}1875{_}They were stupid, vodka-soddened, hapless men.
10132{_}1876{_}The Moscow doctor they could see for themselves.
10132{_}1877{_}He came in, a very tangible thing of flesh and blood, built on a large and manly scale; he took them by the shoulders and bundled them out of their own houses, kicking their bedding after them.
10132{_}1878{_}He scolded them, he rated them and abused them.
10132{_}1879{_}He brought them food and medicine.
10132{_}1880{_}He understood the diseases which from time to time swept over their villages.
10132{_}1881{_}No cold was too intense for him to brave should they be in distress.
10132{_}1882{_}He asked no money, and he gave none.
10132{_}1883{_}But they lived on his charity, and they were wise enough to know it.
10132{_}1884{_}What wonder if these poor wretches loved the man whom they could see and hear above the God who manifested himself to them in no way!
10132{_}1885{_}The orthodox priests of their villages had no money to spend on their parishioners.
10132{_}1886{_}On the contrary, they asked for money to keep the churches in repair.
10132{_}1887{_}What wonder, then, if these poor ignorant, helpless peasants would listen to no priest; for the priest could not explain to them why it was that God sent a four-month-long winter which cut them off from the rest of the world behind impassable barriers of snow; that God sent them droughts in the summer so that there was no crop of rye; that God scourged them with dread and horrible disease!
10132{_}1888{_}It is almost impossible for us to realize, in these days of a lamentably cheap press and a cheaper literature, the mental condition of men and women who have no education, no newspaper, no news of the world, no communication with the universe.
10132{_}1889{_}To them the mystery of the Moscow doctor was as incomprehensible as to us is the Deity.
10132{_}1890{_}They were so near to the animals that Paul could not succeed in teaching them that disease and death followed on the heels of dirt and neglect.
10132{_}1891{_}They were too ignorant to reason, too low down the animal scale to comprehend things which some of the dumb animals undoubtedly recognize.
10132{_}1892{_}Paul Alexis, half Russian, half English, understood these people very thoroughly.
10132{_}1893{_}He took advantage of their ignorance, their simplicity, their unfathomable superstition.
10132{_}1894{_}He governed as no other could have ruled them, by fear and kindness at once.
10132{_}1895{_}He mastered them by his vitality, the wholesome strength of his nature, his infinite superiority.
10132{_}1896{_}He avoided the terrible mistake of the Nihilists by treating them as children to whom education must be given little by little instead of throwing down before them a mass of dangerous knowledge which their minds, unaccustomed to such strong food, are incapable of digesting.
10132{_}1897{_}A British coldness of blood damped as it were the Russian quixotism which would desire to see result follow upon action--to see the world make quicker progress than its Creator has decreed.
10132{_}1898{_}With very unsatisfactory material Paul was setting in motion a great rock which will roll down into the ages unconnected with his name, clearing a path through a very thick forest of ignorance and tyranny.
10132{_}1899{_}CHAPTER XI   CATRINA  The man who carries a deceit, however innocent, with him through life is apt to be somewhat handicapped in that unfair competition.
10132{_}1900{_}He is like a ship at sea with a "sprung" mainmast.
10132{_}1901{_}A side breeze may arise at any moment which throws him all aback and upon his beam-ends.
10132{_}1902{_}He runs illegitimate risks, which are things much given to dragging at a man's mind, handicapping his thoughts.
10132{_}1903{_}Paul suffered in this way.
10132{_}1904{_}It was a distinct burthen to him to play a double part, although each was innocent enough in itself.
10132{_}1905{_}At school, and later on at the 'Varsity, he had consistently and steadily suppressed a truth from friend and foe alike--namely, that he was in his own country a prince.
10132{_}1906{_}No great crime on the face of it; but a constant suppression of a very small truth is as burdensome as any suggestion of falsehood.
10132{_}1907{_}It makes one afraid of contemptible foes, and doubtful of the value of one's own friendship.
10132{_}1908{_}Paul was a simple-minded man.
10132{_}1909{_}He was not afraid of the Russian Government.
10132{_}1910{_}Indeed, he cultivated a fine contempt for that august body.
10132{_}1911{_}But he was distinctly afraid of being found out, for that discovery could only mean an incontinent cessation of the good work which rendered his life happy.
10132{_}1912{_}The fear of being deprived of this interest in existence should certainly have been lessened, if not quite allayed, by the fact that a greater interest had been brought into his life in the pleasant form of a prospective wife.
10132{_}1913{_}When he was in London with Etta Sydney Bamborough he did not, however, forget Osterno.
10132{_}1914{_}He only longed for the time when he could take Etta freely into his confidence and engage her interest in the object of his ambition--namely, to make the huge Osterno estate into that lump of leaven which might in time leaven the whole of the empire.
10132{_}1915{_}That a man is capable of sustaining two absorbing interests at once is a matter of every-day illustration.
10132{_}1916{_}Are we not surrounded by men who do their work well in life, and love their wives well at home, without allowing the one to interfere with the other?
10132{_}1917{_}That women are capable of the same seems exceedingly probable.
10132{_}1918{_}But we are a race of sheep who run after each other, guided for the moment by a catchword which will not bear investigation, or an erroneous deduction set in alliterative verse which clings to the mind and sways it.
10132{_}1919{_}Thus we all think that woman's whole existence is, and is only capable of, love, because a poet, in the trickiness of his trade, once said so.
10132{_}1920{_}Now, Paul held a different opinion.
10132{_}1921{_}He thought that Etta could manage to love him well, as she said she did, and yet take an interest in that which was in reality the object of his life.
10132{_}1922{_}He intended to take the earliest opportunity of telling her all about the work he was endeavoring to carry out at Osterno, and the knowledge that he was withholding something from her was a constant burden to an upright and honest nature.
10132{_}1923{_}"I think," he said one morning to Steinmetz, "that I will write and tell Mrs. Sydney Bamborough all about this place."
10132{_}1924{_}"I should not do that," replied Steinmetz with a leisurely promptitude.
10132{_}1925{_}They were alone in a great smoking-room of which the walls were hung all round with hunting trophies.
10132{_}1926{_}Paul was smoking a post-prandial cigar.
10132{_}1927{_}Steinmetz reflected gravely over a pipe.
10132{_}1928{_}They were both reading Russian newspapers--periodicals chiefly remarkable for that which they leave unsaid.
10132{_}1929{_}"Why not?"
10132{_}1930{_}asked Paul.
10132{_}1931{_}"On principle.
10132{_}1932{_}Never tell a woman that which is not interesting enough to magnify into a secret."
10132{_}1933{_}Paul turned over his newspaper.
10132{_}1934{_}He began reading again.
10132{_}1935{_}Then, suddenly, he looked up.
10132{_}1936{_}"We are engaged to be married," he observed pointedly.
10132{_}1937{_}Steinmetz took his pipe from his lips slowly and imperturbably.
10132{_}1938{_}He was a man to whom it was no satisfaction to impart news.
10132{_}1939{_}He either knew it before or did not take much interest in the matter.
10132{_}1940{_}"That makes it worse," he said.
10132{_}1941{_}"A woman only conceals what is bad about her husband.
10132{_}1942{_}If she knows anything that is likely to make other women think that their husbands are inferior, she will tell it."
10132{_}1943{_}Paul laughed.
10132{_}1944{_}"But this is not good," he argued.
10132{_}1945{_}"We have kept it so confoundedly quiet that I am beginning to feel as if it is a crime."
10132{_}1946{_}Steinmetz uncrossed his legs, crossed them again, and then spoke after mature reflection:  "As I understand the law of libel, a man is punished, not for telling a lie, but for telling either the truth or a lie with malicious intent.
10132{_}1947{_}I imagine the Almighty will take the intent into consideration, if human justice finds it expedient to do so!"
10132{_}1948{_}Paul shrugged his shoulders.
10132{_}1949{_}Argument was not his strong point, and, like most men who cannot argue, he was almost impervious to the arguments of others.
10132{_}1950{_}He recognized the necessity for secrecy--the absolute need of a thousand little secretive precautions and disguises which were intensely disagreeable to him.
10132{_}1951{_}But he also grumbled at them freely, and whenever he made such objection Karl Steinmetz grew uneasy, as if the question which he disposed of with facile philosophy or humorous resignation had behind it a possibility and an importance of which he was fully aware.
10132{_}1952{_}It was on these rare occasions that he might have conveyed to a keen observer the impression that he was playing a very dangerous game with a smiling countenance.
10132{_}1953{_}"All that we do," pursued Steinmetz, "is to bow to a lamentable necessity for deceit.
10132{_}1954{_}I have bowed to it all my life.
10132{_}1955{_}It has been my trade, perhaps.
10132{_}1956{_}It is not our fault that we are placed in charge of four or five thousand human beings who are no more capable of helping themselves than are sheep.
10132{_}1957{_}It is not our fault that the forefathers of these sheep cut down the forests and omitted to plant more, so that the flocks with whom we have to deal have no fuel.
10132{_}1958{_}It is not our fault that a most terrific winter annually renders the land unproductive for four months.
10132{_}1959{_}It is not our fault that the government to which we are forced to bow--the Czar whose name lifts our hats from our heads--it is not our fault that progress and education are taboo, and that all who endeavor to forward the cause of humanity are promptly put away in a safe place where they are at liberty to forward their own salvation and nothing else.
10132{_}1960{_}Nothing is our fault, mein lieber, in this country.
10132{_}1961{_}We have to make the best of adverse circumstances.
10132{_}1962{_}We are not breaking any human law, and in doing nothing we should be breaking a divine command."
10132{_}1963{_}Paul flicked the ash off his cigar.
10132{_}1964{_}He had heard all this before.
10132{_}1965{_}Karl Steinmetz's words were usually more remarkable for solid thoughtfulness than for brilliancy of conception or any great novelty of expression.
10132{_}1966{_}"Oh!"
10132{_}1967{_}said Paul quietly, "I am not going to leave off.
10132{_}1968{_}You need not fear that.
10132{_}1969{_}Only I shall have to tell my wife.
10132{_}1970{_}Surely a woman could help us in a thousand ways.
10132{_}1971{_}There is such a lot that only a woman understands."
10132{_}1972{_}"Yes!"
10132{_}1973{_}grunted Steinmetz; "and only the right sort of woman."
10132{_}1974{_}Paul looked up sharply.
10132{_}1975{_}"You must leave that to me," he said.
10132{_}1976{_}"My very dear friend, I leave every thing to you."
10132{_}1977{_}Paul smiled.
10132{_}1978{_}There was no positive proof that this was not strictly true.
10132{_}1979{_}There was no saying that Karl Steinmetz did not leave every thing to every-body.
10132{_}1980{_}But wise people thought differently.
10132{_}1981{_}"You don't know Etta," he said, half shyly.
10132{_}1982{_}"She is full of sympathy and pity for these people."
10132{_}1983{_}Steinmetz bowed gravely.
10132{_}1984{_}"I have no doubt of it."
10132{_}1985{_}"And yet you say that she must not be told."
10132{_}1986{_}"Certainly not.
10132{_}1987{_}A secret is considerably strained if it be divided between two people.
10132{_}1988{_}Stretching it to three will probably break it.
10132{_}1989{_}You can tell her when you are married.
10132{_}1990{_}Does she consent to live in Osterno?"
10132{_}1991{_}"Oh, yes.
10132{_}1992{_}I think so."
10132{_}1993{_}"Um--m!"
10132{_}1994{_}"What did you say?"
10132{_}1995{_}"Um--m," repeated Steinmetz, and the conversation somewhat naturally showed signs of collapse.
10132{_}1996{_}At this moment the door was opened, and a servant in bright livery, with powdered wig, silk stockings, and a countenance which might have been of wood, brought in a letter on a silver tray.
10132{_}1997{_}Paul took the square envelope and turned it over, displaying as he did so a coronet in black and gold on the corner, like a stamp.
10132{_}1998{_}Karl Steinmetz saw the coronet.
10132{_}1999{_}He never took his quiet, unobtrusive glance from Paul's face while he opened the letter and read it.
10132{_}2000{_}"A fresh difficulty," said Paul, throwing the note across to his companion.
10132{_}2001{_}Steinmetz looked grave while he unfolded the thick stationery.
10132{_}2002{_}"Dear Paul [the letter ran]: I hear you are at Osterno and that the Moscow doctor is in your country.
10132{_}2003{_}We are in great distress at Thors--cholera, I fear.
10132{_}2004{_}The fame of your doctor has spread to my people, and they are clamoring for him.
10132{_}2005{_}Can you bring or send him over?
10132{_}2006{_}You know your room here is always in readiness.
10132{_}2007{_}Come soon with the great doctor, and also Herr Steinmetz.
10132{_}2008{_}In doing so you will give more than pleasure to your old friend,"  Catrina Lanovitch.
10132{_}2009{_}"P.S.
10132{_}2010{_}Mother is afraid to go out of doors for fear of infection.
10132{_}2011{_}She thinks she has a little cold."
10132{_}2012{_}Steinmetz folded the letter very carefully, pressing the seam of it reflectively with his stout forefinger and thumb.
10132{_}2013{_}"I always think of the lie first," he said.
10132{_}2014{_}"It's my nature or my misfortune.
10132{_}2015{_}We can easily write and say that the Moscow doctor has left."
10132{_}2016{_}He paused, scratching his brow pensively with his curved forefinger.
10132{_}2017{_}It is to be feared that he was seeking not so much the truth as the most convenient perversion of the same.
10132{_}2018{_}"But then," he went on, "by doing that we leave these poor devils to die in their--styes.
10132{_}2019{_}Catrina cannot manage them.
10132{_}2020{_}They are worse than our people."
10132{_}2021{_}"Whatever is the best lie to tell," burst in Paul--"as we seem to live in an atmosphere of them--I must go to Thors; that is quite certain."
10132{_}2022{_}"There is no must in the case," put in Steinmetz quietly, as a parenthesis.
10132{_}2023{_}"No man is compelled to throw himself in the way of infection.
10132{_}2024{_}But I know you will go, whatever I say."
10132{_}2025{_}"I suppose I shall," admitted Paul.
10132{_}2026{_}"And Catrina will find you out at once."
10132{_}2027{_}"Why?"
10132{_}2028{_}Steinmetz drew in his feet.
10132{_}2029{_}He leant forward and knocked his pipe on one of the logs that lay ready to light in the great open fire-place.
10132{_}2030{_}"Because she loves you," he said shortly.
10132{_}2031{_}"There is no coming the Moscow doctor over her, mien lieber."
10132{_}2032{_}Paul laughed rather awkwardly.
10132{_}2033{_}He was one of the few men--daily growing fewer--who hold that a woman's love is not a thing to be tossed lightly about in conversation.
10132{_}2034{_}"Then--" he began, speaking rather quickly, as if afraid that Steinmetz was going to say more.
10132{_}2035{_}"If," he amended, "you think she will find out, she must not see me, that is all."
10132{_}2036{_}Steinmetz reflected again.
10132{_}2037{_}He was unusually grave over this matter.
10132{_}2038{_}One would scarcely have taken this stout German for a person of any sentiment whatever.
10132{_}2039{_}Nevertheless he would have liked Paul to marry Catrina Lanovitch in preference to Etta Sydney Bamborough, merely because he thought that the former loved him, while he felt sure that the latter did not.
10132{_}2040{_}So much for the sentimental point of view--a starting-point, by the way, which usually makes all the difference in a man's life.
10132{_}2041{_}For a man needs to be loved as much as a woman needs it.
10132{_}2042{_}From the practical point of view, Karl Steinmetz knew too much about Etta to place entire reliance on the goodness of her motives.
10132{_}2043{_}He keenly suspected that she was marrying Paul for his money--for the position he could give her in the world.
10132{_}2044{_}"We must be careful," he said.
10132{_}2045{_}"We must place clearly before ourselves the risks that we are running before we come to any decision.
10132{_}2046{_}For you the risk is simply that of unofficial banishment.
10132{_}2047{_}They can hardly send you to Siberia because you are half an Englishman; and that impertinent country has a habit of getting up and shouting when her sons are interfered with.
10132{_}2048{_}But they can easily make Russia impossible for you.
10132{_}2049{_}They can do you more harm than you think.
10132{_}2050{_}They can do these poor devils of peasants of yours more harm than we can comfortably contemplate.
10132{_}2051{_}As for me," he paused and shrugged his great shoulders, "it means Siberia.
10132{_}2052{_}Already I am a suspect--a persona non grata."
10132{_}2053{_}"I do not see how we can refuse to help Catrina," said Paul, in a voice which Steinmetz seemed to know, for he suddenly gave in.
10132{_}2054{_}"As you will," he said.
10132{_}2055{_}He sat up, and, drawing a small table toward him, took up a pen reflectively.
10132{_}2056{_}Paul watched him in silence.
10132{_}2057{_}When the letter was finished, Steinmetz read it aloud:  "My Dear Catrina:  "The Moscow doctor and your obedient servant will be (D.V.)
10132{_}2058{_}in Thors by seven o'clock to-night.
10132{_}2059{_}We propose spending about an hour in the village, if you will kindly advise the starosta to be ready for us.
10132{_}2060{_}As our time is limited, and we are much needed in Osterno, we shall have to deprive ourselves of the pleasure of calling at the castle.
10132{_}2061{_}The prince sends kind remembrances, and proposes riding over to Thors to avail himself of your proffered hospitality in a day or two.
10132{_}2062{_}With salutations to the countess,  "Your old friend,  "Karl Steinmetz."
10132{_}2063{_}Steinmetz waited with the letter in his hand for Paul's approval.
10132{_}2064{_}"You see," he explained, "you are notoriously indifferent to the welfare of the peasants.
10132{_}2065{_}It would be unnatural if you suddenly displayed so much interest as to induce you to go to Thors on a mission of charity."
10132{_}2066{_}Paul nodded.
10132{_}2067{_}"All right," he said.
10132{_}2068{_}"Yes, I see; though I confess I sometimes forget what the deuce I _am_ supposed to be."
10132{_}2069{_}Steinmetz laughed pleasantly as he folded the letter.
10132{_}2070{_}He rose and went to the door.
10132{_}2071{_}"I will send it off," he said.
10132{_}2072{_}He paused on the threshold and looked back gravely.
10132{_}2073{_}"Do not forget," he added, "that Catrina Lanovitch loves you."
10132{_}2074{_}CHAPTER XII   AT THORS  Below the windows of a long, low, stone house, in its architecture remarkably like a fortified farm--below these deep-embrasured windows the river Oster mumbled softly.
10132{_}2075{_}One of the windows was wide open, and with the voice of the water a wonderful music rolled out to mingle and lose itself in the hum of the pine-woods.
10132{_}2076{_}The room was a small one; beneath the artistic wall-paper one detected the outline of square-hewn stones.
10132{_}2077{_}There were women's things lying about; there were flowers in a bowl on a low, strong table.
10132{_}2078{_}There were a few good engravings on the wall; deep-curtained windows, low chairs, a sofa, a fan.
10132{_}2079{_}But it was not a womanly room.
10132{_}2080{_}The music filling it, vibrating back from the grim stone walls, was not womanly music.
10132{_}2081{_}It was more than manly.
10132{_}2082{_}It was not earthly, but almost divine.
10132{_}2083{_}It happened to be Grieg, with the halting beat of a disabled, perhaps a broken, heart in it, as that master's music usually has.
10132{_}2084{_}The girl was alone in the room.
10132{_}2085{_}The presence of any one would have silenced something that was throbbing at the back of the chords.
10132{_}2086{_}Quite suddenly she stopped.
10132{_}2087{_}She knew how to play the quaint last notes.
10132{_}2088{_}She knew something that no master had ever taught her.
10132{_}2089{_}She swung round on the stool and faced the light.
10132{_}2090{_}It was afternoon--an autumn afternoon in Russia--and the pink light made the very best of a face which was not beautiful at all, never could be beautiful--a face about which even the owner, a woman, could have no possible illusion.
10132{_}2091{_}It was broad and powerful, with eyes too far apart, forehead too broad and low, jaw too heavy, mouth too determined.
10132{_}2092{_}The eyes were almond-shaped, and slightly sloping downward and inward--deep, passionate blue eyes set in a Mongolian head.
10132{_}2093{_}It was the face of a woman who could, morally speaking, make mincemeat of nine young men out of ten.
10132{_}2094{_}But she could not have made one out of the number love her.
10132{_}2095{_}For it has been decreed that women shall win love--except in some happy exceptions--by beauty only.
10132{_}2096{_}The same unwritten law has it that a man's appearance does not matter--a law much appreciated by some of us, and duly canonized by not a few.
10132{_}2097{_}The girl was evidently listening.
10132{_}2098{_}She glanced at a little golden clock on the mantel-piece, and then at the open window.
10132{_}2099{_}She rose--she was short, and somewhat broadly built--and went to the window.
10132{_}2100{_}"He will be back," she said to herself, "in a few minutes now."
10132{_}2101{_}She raised her hand to her forehead, and pressed back her hair with a little movement of impatience, expressive, perhaps, of a great suspense.
10132{_}2102{_}She stood idly drumming on the window-sill for a few moments; then, with a quick little sigh, she went back to the piano.
10132{_}2103{_}As she moved she gave a jerk of the head from time to time, as schoolgirls who have too much hair are wont to do.
10132{_}2104{_}The reason of this nervous movement was a wondrous plait of gold reaching far below her waist.
10132{_}2105{_}Catrina Lanovitch almost worshipped her own hair.
10132{_}2106{_}She knew without any doubt that not one woman in ten thousand could rival her in this feminine glory--knew it as indubitably as she knew that she was plain.
10132{_}2107{_}The latter fact she faced with an unflinching, cold conviction which was not feminine at all.
10132{_}2108{_}She did not say that she was hideous, for the sake of hearing a contradiction or a series of saving clauses.
10132{_}2109{_}She never spoke of it to any one.
10132{_}2110{_}She had grown up with it, and as it was beyond doubt, so was it outside discussion.
10132{_}2111{_}All her femininity seemed to be concentrated, all her vanity centred, on her hair.
10132{_}2112{_}It was her one pride, perhaps her one hope.
10132{_}2113{_}Women have been loved for their voices.
10132{_}2114{_}Catrina's voice was musical enough, but it was deep and strong.
10132{_}2115{_}It was passionate, tender if she wished, fascinating; but it was not lovable.
10132{_}2116{_}If the voice may win love, why not the hair?
10132{_}2117{_}Catrina despised all men but one--that one she worshipped.
10132{_}2118{_}She lived night and day with one great desire, beside which heaven and hell were mere words.
10132{_}2119{_}Neither the hope of the one nor the fear of the other in any way touched or affected her desire.
10132{_}2120{_}She wanted to make Paul Alexis love her; and, womanlike, she clung to the one womanly charm that was hers--the wonderful golden hair.
10132{_}2121{_}Pathetic, aye, pathetic--with a grin behind the pathos, as there ever is.
10132{_}2122{_}She sat down at the piano, and her strong, small hands tore the heart out of each wire.
10132{_}2123{_}There are some people who get farther into a piano than others, making the wires speak as with a voice.
10132{_}2124{_}Catrina Lanovitch had this trick.
10132{_}2125{_}She only played a Russian people-song--a simple lay such as one may hear issuing from the door of any kabak on a summer evening.
10132{_}2126{_}But she infused a true Russian soul into it--the soul that is cursed with a fatal power of dumb and patient endurance.
10132{_}2127{_}She did not sway from side to side as do some people who lose themselves in the intoxication of music.
10132{_}2128{_}But she sat quite upright, her sturdy, square shoulders motionless.
10132{_}2129{_}Her strange eyes were fixed with the stillness of distant contemplation.
10132{_}2130{_}Suddenly she stopped and leaped to her feet.
10132{_}2131{_}She did not go to the window, but stood listening beside the piano.
10132{_}2132{_}The beat of a horse's hoofs on the narrow road was distinctly audible, hollow and sodden as is the sound of a wooden road.
10132{_}2133{_}It came nearer and nearer, and a certain unsteadiness indicated that the horse was tired.
10132{_}2134{_}"I thought he might have come," she whispered, and she sat down breathlessly.
10132{_}2135{_}When the servant came into the room a few minutes later Catrina was at the piano.
10132{_}2136{_}"A letter, mademoiselle," said the maid.
10132{_}2137{_}"Lay it on the table," answered Catrina, without looking round.
10132{_}2138{_}She was playing the closing bars of a nocturne.
10132{_}2139{_}She rose slowly, turned, and seized the letter as a starving man seizes food.
10132{_}2140{_}There was something almost wolf-like in her eyes.
10132{_}2141{_}"Steinmetz," she exclaimed, reading the address.
10132{_}2142{_}"Steinmetz.
10132{_}2143{_}Oh!
10132{_}2144{_}why won't he write to me?"
10132{_}2145{_}She tore open the letter, read it, and stood holding it in her hand, looking out over the trackless pine-woods with absorbed, speculative eyes.
10132{_}2146{_}The sun had just set.
10132{_}2147{_}The farthest ridge of pine-trees stood out like the teeth of a saw in black relief on the rosy sky.
10132{_}2148{_}Catrina Lanovitch watched the rosiness fade into pearly gray.
10132{_}2149{_}"Madame the Countess awaits mademoiselle for tea," said the maid's voice suddenly, in the gloom of the door-way.
10132{_}2150{_}"I will come."
10132{_}2151{_}The village of Thors--twenty miles farther down the river Oster, twenty miles nearer to the junction of that river with the Volga--was little more than a hamlet in the days of which we write.
10132{_}2152{_}Some day, perhaps, the three hundred souls of Thors may increase and multiply--some day when Russia is attacked by the railway fever.
10132{_}2153{_}For Thors is on the Chorno-Ziom--the belt of black and fertile soil that runs right across the vast empire.
10132{_}2154{_}Karl Steinmetz, a dogged watcher of the Wandering Jew--the deathless scoffer at our Lord's agony, who shall never die, who shall leave cholera in his track wherever he may wander--Karl Steinmetz knew that the Oster was in itself a Wandering Jew.
10132{_}2155{_}This river meandered through the lonesome country, bearing cholera germs within its waters.
10132{_}2156{_}Whenever Osterno had cholera it sent it down the river to Thors, and so on to the Volga.
10132{_}2157{_}Thors lay groaning under the scourge, and the Countess Lanovitch shut herself within her stone walls, shivering with fear, begging her daughter to return to Petersburg.
10132{_}2158{_}It was nearly dark when Karl Steinmetz and the Moscow doctor rode into the little village, to find the starosta, a simple Russian farmer, awaiting them outside the kabak.
10132{_}2159{_}Steinmetz knew the man, and immediately took command of the situation with that unquestioned sense of authority which in Russia places the barin on much the same footing as that taken by the Anglo-Indian in our eastern empire.
10132{_}2160{_}"Now, starosta," he said, "we have only an hour to spend in Thors.
10132{_}2161{_}This is the Moscow doctor.
10132{_}2162{_}If you listen to what he tells you, you will soon have no sickness in the village.
10132{_}2163{_}The worst houses first--and quickly.
10132{_}2164{_}You need not be afraid, but if you do not care to come in, you may stay outside."
10132{_}2165{_}As they walked down the straggling village-street the Moscow doctor told the starosta in no measured terms, as was his wont, wherein lay the heart of the sickness.
10132{_}2166{_}Here, as in Osterno, dirt and neglect were at the base of all the trouble.
10132{_}2167{_}Here, as in the larger village, the houses were more like the abode of four-footed beasts than the dwellings of human beings.
10132{_}2168{_}The starosta prudently remained outside the first house to which he introduced the visitors.
10132{_}2169{_}Paul went fearlessly in, while Steinmetz stood in the door-way, holding open the door.
10132{_}2170{_}As he was standing there he perceived a flickering light approaching him.
10132{_}2171{_}The light was evidently that of an ordinary hand-lantern, and from the swinging motion it was easy to divine that it was being carried by some one who was walking quickly.
10132{_}2172{_}"Who is this?"
10132{_}2173{_}asked Steinmetz.
10132{_}2174{_}"It is likely to be the Countess Catrina, Excellency."
10132{_}2175{_}Steinmetz glanced back into the cottage, which was dark save for the light of a single petroleum lamp.
10132{_}2176{_}Paul's huge form could be dimly distinguished bending over a heap of humanity and foul clothing in a corner.
10132{_}2177{_}"Does she visit the cottages?"
10132{_}2178{_}asked Steinmetz sharply.
10132{_}2179{_}"She does, God be with her!
10132{_}2180{_}She has no fear.
10132{_}2181{_}She is an angel.
10132{_}2182{_}Without her we should all be dead."
10132{_}2183{_}"She won't visit this, if I can help it," muttered Steinmetz.
10132{_}2184{_}The light flickered along the road toward them.
10132{_}2185{_}In the course of a few minutes it fell on the stricken cottage, on the starosta standing in the road, on Steinmetz in the door-way.
10132{_}2186{_}"Herr Steinmetz, is that you?"
10132{_}2187{_}asked a voice, deep and musical, in the darkness.
10132{_}2188{_}"Zum Befehl," answered Steinmetz, without moving.
10132{_}2189{_}Catrina came up to him.
10132{_}2190{_}She was clad in a long dark cloak, a dark hat, and wore no gloves.
10132{_}2191{_}She brought with her a clean aromatic odor of disinfectants.
10132{_}2192{_}She carried the lantern herself, while behind her walked a man-servant in livery, with a large basket in either hand.

10132{_}2194{_}"It is not much that we can do," answered Steinmetz, taking the small outstretched hand within his large soft grasp; "but that little you may always count upon."
10132{_}2195{_}"I know," she said gravely.

10132{_}2198{_}he asked, speaking in German, as they always did together.
10132{_}2199{_}She shrugged her shoulders.
10132{_}2200{_}"Oh!"
10132{_}2201{_}she answered indifferently, "I am well, of course.
10132{_}2202{_}I always am.
10132{_}2203{_}I have the strength of a horse.
10132{_}2204{_}Of course I have been troubled about these poor people.
10132{_}2205{_}It has been terrible.
10132{_}2206{_}They are worse than children.

10132{_}2209{_}They are not like the Jews.
10132{_}2210{_}It seems unjust.
10132{_}2211{_}I have been very busy, in my small way.

10132{_}2216{_}Steinmetz did not move.

10132{_}2231{_}"I may be able to help."
10132{_}2232{_}Steinmetz shook his head.
10132{_}2233{_}"Better not!"
10132{_}2234{_}he said.
10132{_}2235{_}"Besides, your life is too precious to these poor people to run unnecessary risks."
10132{_}2236{_}She gave a strange, bitter laugh.
10132{_}2237{_}"And what about you?"
10132{_}2238{_}she said.

10132{_}2240{_}"You never hear of Paul going into any of the cottages," snapped Steinmetz sharply.
10132{_}2241{_}"For me it is different.

10132{_}2243{_}"No," she answered slowly; "and it is quite right.

10132{_}2246{_}"He is well, thank you."

10132{_}2253{_}After him came a shower of clothes and bedding.

10132{_}2255{_}exclaimed Steinmetz, spluttering.

10132{_}2259{_}But Catrina had slipped past him.

10132{_}2262{_}he cried.

10132{_}2264{_}She was just over the threshold.

10132{_}2268{_}Almost immediately she gave a mocking laugh.
10132{_}2269{_}"Paul!"
10132{_}2270{_}she said.
10132{_}2271{_}CHAPTER XIII   UNMASKED  For a moment there was silence in the hovel, broken only by the wail of the dying man in the corner.
10132{_}2272{_}Paul and Catrina faced each other--she white and suddenly breathless, he half frowning.
10132{_}2273{_}But he did not meet her eyes.
10132{_}2274{_}"Paul," she said again, with a lingering touch on the name.

10132{_}2276{_}"Paul, what did you do this for?
10132{_}2277{_}Why are you here?
10132{_}2278{_}Oh, why are you in this wretched place?"
10132{_}2279{_}"Because you sent for me," he answered quietly.
10132{_}2280{_}"Come, let us go out.
10132{_}2281{_}I have finished here.
10132{_}2282{_}That man will die.
10132{_}2283{_}There is nothing more to be done for him.
10132{_}2284{_}You must not stay in here."
10132{_}2285{_}She gave a short laugh as she followed him.
10132{_}2286{_}He had to stoop low to pass through the door-way.
10132{_}2287{_}Then he turned and held out his hand, for fear she should trip over the high threshold.
10132{_}2288{_}She nodded her thanks, but refused the proffered assistance.
10132{_}2289{_}Steinmetz lingered behind to give some last instructions, leaving Paul and Catrina to walk on down the narrow street alone.
10132{_}2290{_}The moon was just rising--a great yellow moon such as only Russia knows--the land of the silver night.
10132{_}2291{_}"How long have you been doing this?"
10132{_}2292{_}asked Catrina suddenly.
10132{_}2293{_}She did not look toward him, but straight in front of her.
10132{_}2294{_}"For some years now," he replied simply.
10132{_}2295{_}He lingered.
10132{_}2296{_}He was waiting for Steinmetz, who always rose to such emergencies, who understood secrets and how to secure them when they seemed already lost.
10132{_}2297{_}He did not quite understand what was to be done with Catrina--how she was to be silenced.
10132{_}2298{_}She had found him out with such startling rapidity that he felt disposed to admit her right to dictate her own terms.
10132{_}2299{_}On a straight road this man was fearless and quick, but he had no taste or capacity for crooked ways.
10132{_}2300{_}Catrina walked on in silence.
10132{_}2301{_}She was not looking at the matter from his point of view at all.
10132{_}2302{_}"Of course," she said at length, "of course, Paul, I admire you for it immensely.
10132{_}2303{_}It is just like you to go and do the thing quietly and say nothing about it; but--oh, you must go away from here.
10132{_}2304{_}I--I--it is too horrible to think of your running such risks.
10132{_}2305{_}Rather let them all die like flies than that.
10132{_}2306{_}You mustn't do it.
10132{_}2307{_}You mustn't."
10132{_}2308{_}She spoke in English hurriedly, with a little break in her voice which he did not understand.
10132{_}2309{_}"With ordinary precautions the risk is very small," he said practically.
10132{_}2310{_}"Yes.
10132{_}2311{_}But do you take ordinary precautions?
10132{_}2312{_}Are you sure you are all right now?"
10132{_}2313{_}She stopped.
10132{_}2314{_}They were quite alone in the one silent street of the stricken village.
10132{_}2315{_}She looked up into his face.
10132{_}2316{_}Her hands were running over the breast of the tattered coat he wore.
10132{_}2317{_}It was lamentably obvious, even to him, that she loved him.
10132{_}2318{_}In her anxiety she either did not know what she was doing, or she did not care whether he knew or not.
10132{_}2319{_}She merely gave sway to the maternal instinct which is in the love of all women.
10132{_}2320{_}She felt his hands; she reached up and touched his face.
10132{_}2321{_}"Are you sure--are you sure you have not taken it?"
10132{_}2322{_}she whispered.
10132{_}2323{_}He walked on, almost roughly.
10132{_}2324{_}"Oh, yes; quite," he said.
10132{_}2325{_}"I will not allow you to go into any more houses in Thors.
10132{_}2326{_}I cannot--I will not!
10132{_}2327{_}Oh, Paul, you don't know.
10132{_}2328{_}If you do, I will tell them all who you are, and--and the Government will stop you."
10132{_}2329{_}"What would be the good of that?"
10132{_}2330{_}said Paul awkwardly.
10132{_}2331{_}"Your father cared for his peasants, and was content to run risks for them.
10132{_}2332{_}I suppose you care about them, too, as you go into their houses."
10132{_}2333{_}"Yes; but--"  She paused, gave a strange little reckless laugh, and was silent.
10132{_}2334{_}Heaven forbid that we should say that she wanted him to know that she loved him.
10132{_}2335{_}Chivalry bids us believe that women guard the secret of their love inviolate from the world.
10132{_}2336{_}But what was Catrina to do?
10132{_}2337{_}Men are in the habit of forgetting that plain women are women at all.
10132{_}2338{_}Surely some of them may be excused for reminding us at times that they also are capable of loving--that they also desire to be loved.
10132{_}2339{_}Happy is the man who loves and is loved of a plain woman; for she will take her own lack of beauty into consideration, and give him more than most beautiful women have it in their power to give.
10132{_}2340{_}"Of course," Catrina went on, with a sudden anger which surprised herself, "I cannot stop you from doing this at Osterno, though I think it is wicked; but I can prevent you from doing it here, and I certainly shall!"
10132{_}2341{_}Paul shrugged his shoulders.
10132{_}2342{_}"As you like," he said.
10132{_}2343{_}"I thought you cared more about the peasants."
10132{_}2344{_}"I do not care a jot about the peasants," she answered passionately, "as compared--It is you I am thinking about, not them.
10132{_}2345{_}I think you are selfish, and cruel to your friends."
10132{_}2346{_}"My friends have never shown that they are consumed with anxiety on my account."
10132{_}2347{_}"That is mere prevarication.
10132{_}2348{_}Leave that to Herr Steinmetz and such men, whose business it is; you don't do it well.
10132{_}2349{_}Your friends may feel a lot that they do not show."
10132{_}2350{_}She spoke the words shortly and sharply.
10132{_}2351{_}Surreptitious good is so rare, that when it is found out it very naturally gets mixed up with secret evil, and the perpetrator of the hidden good deed feels guilty of a crime.
10132{_}2352{_}Paul was in this lamentable position, which he proceeded to further aggravate by seeking to excuse himself.
10132{_}2353{_}"I did it after mature consideration.
10132{_}2354{_}I tried paying another man, but he shirked his work and showed the white feather; so Steinmetz and I concluded that there was nothing to be done but do our dirty work ourselves."
10132{_}2355{_}"Which, being translated, means that you do it."
10132{_}2356{_}"Pardon me.
10132{_}2357{_}Steinmetz does his share."
10132{_}2358{_}Catrina Lanovitch was essentially a woman, despite her somewhat masculine frame.
10132{_}2359{_}She settled Karl Steinmetz's account with a sniff of contempt.
10132{_}2360{_}"And that is why you have been so fond of Osterno the last two years?"
10132{_}2361{_}she asked innocently.
10132{_}2362{_}"Yes," he answered, falling into the trap.
10132{_}2363{_}Catrina winced.
10132{_}2364{_}One does not wince the less because the pain is expected.
10132{_}2365{_}The girl had the Slav instinct of self-martyrdom, which makes Russians so very different from the pleasure-loving nations of Europe.
10132{_}2366{_}"Only that?"
10132{_}2367{_}she enquired.
10132{_}2368{_}Paul glanced down at her.
10132{_}2369{_}"Yes," he answered quietly.
10132{_}2370{_}They walked on in silence for a few moments.
10132{_}2371{_}Paul seemed tacitly to have given up the idea of visiting any more of the stricken cottages.
10132{_}2372{_}They were going toward the long old house, which was called the castle more by courtesy than by right.
10132{_}2373{_}"How long are you going to stay in Osterno?"
10132{_}2374{_}asked Catrina at length.
10132{_}2375{_}"About a fortnight; I cannot stay longer.
10132{_}2376{_}I am going to be married."
10132{_}2377{_}Catrina stopped dead.
10132{_}2378{_}She stood for a moment looking at the ground with a sort of wonder in her eyes, not pleasant to see.
10132{_}2379{_}It was the look of one who, having fallen from a great height, is not quite sure whether it means death or not.
10132{_}2380{_}Then she walked on.
10132{_}2381{_}"I congratulate you," she said.
10132{_}2382{_}"I only hope she will make you happy.
10132{_}2383{_}She is--beautiful, I suppose?"
10132{_}2384{_}"Yes," answered Paul simply.
10132{_}2385{_}The girl nodded her head.
10132{_}2386{_}"What is her name?"
10132{_}2387{_}"Etta Sydney Bamborough."
10132{_}2388{_}Catrina had evidently never heard the name before.
10132{_}2389{_}It conveyed nothing to her.
10132{_}2390{_}Womanlike, she went back to her first question.
10132{_}2391{_}"What is she like?"
10132{_}2392{_}Paul hesitated.
10132{_}2393{_}"Tall, I suppose?"
10132{_}2394{_}suggested the stunted woman at his side.
10132{_}2395{_}"Yes."
10132{_}2396{_}"And graceful?"
10132{_}2397{_}"Yes."
