10132{_}4396{_}She played her part before the crowd of bowing servants with that forgetfulness of mere bodily fatigue which is expected of princesses and other great ladies.
10132{_}4397{_}She swept up the broad staircase, leaning on Paul's arm, with a carriage, a presence, a dazzling wealth of beauty, which did not fail to impress the onlookers.
10132{_}4398{_}Whatever Etta may have failed to bring to Paul Howard Alexis as a wife, she made him a matchless princess.
10132{_}4399{_}He led her straight through the drawing-room to the suite of rooms which were hers.
10132{_}4400{_}These consisted of an ante-room, a small drawing-room, and her private apartments beyond.
10132{_}4401{_}Paul stopped in the drawing-room, looking round with a simple satisfaction in all that had been done by his orders for Etta's comfort.
10132{_}4402{_}"These," he said, "are your rooms."
10132{_}4403{_}He was no adept at turning a neat phrase--at reeling off a pretty honeymoon welcome.
10132{_}4404{_}Perhaps he expected her to express delight, to come to him, possibly, and kiss him, as some women would have done.
10132{_}4405{_}She looked round critically.
10132{_}4406{_}"Yes," she said, "they are very nice."
10132{_}4407{_}She crossed the room and drew aside the curtain that covered the double-latticed windows.
10132{_}4408{_}The room was so warm that there was no rime on the panes.
10132{_}4409{_}She gave a little shudder, and he went to her side, putting his strong, quiet arm around her.
10132{_}4410{_}Below them, stretching away beneath the brilliant moonlight, lay the country that was his inheritance, an estate as large as a large English county.
10132{_}4411{_}Immediately beneath them, at the foot of the great rock upon which the castle was built, nestled the village of Osterno--straggling, squalid.
10132{_}4412{_}"Oh!"
10132{_}4413{_}she said dully, "this is Siberia; this is terrible!"
10132{_}4414{_}It had never presented itself to him in that light, the wonderful stretch of country over which they were looking.
10132{_}4415{_}"It is not so bad," he said, "in the daylight."
10132{_}4416{_}And that was all; for he had no persuasive tongue.
10132{_}4417{_}"That is the village," he went on, after a little pause.
10132{_}4418{_}"Those are the people who look to us to help them in their fight against terrible odds.
10132{_}4419{_}I hoped--that you would be interested in them."
10132{_}4420{_}She looked down curiously at the little wooden huts, half-buried in the snow; the smoking chimneys; the twinkling, curtainless windows.
10132{_}4421{_}"What do you expect me to do?"
10132{_}4422{_}she asked in a queer voice.
10132{_}4423{_}He looked at her in a sort of wonderment.
10132{_}4424{_}Perhaps it seemed to him that a woman should have no need to ask such a question.
10132{_}4425{_}"It is a long story," he said; "I will tell you about it another time.
10132{_}4426{_}You are tired now, after your journey."
10132{_}4427{_}His arm slipped from her waist.
10132{_}4428{_}They stood side by side.
10132{_}4429{_}And both were conscious of a feeling of difference.
10132{_}4430{_}They were not the same as they had been in London.
10132{_}4431{_}The atmosphere of Russia seemed to have had some subtle effect upon them.
10132{_}4432{_}Etta turned and sat slowly down on a low chair before the fire.
10132{_}4433{_}She had thrown her furs aside, and they lay in a luxurious heap on the floor.
10132{_}4434{_}The maids, hearing that the prince and princess were together, waited silently in the next room behind the closed door.
10132{_}4435{_}"I think I had better hear it now," said Etta.
10132{_}4436{_}"But you are tired," protested her husband.
10132{_}4437{_}"You had better rest until dinner-time."
10132{_}4438{_}"No; I am not tired."
10132{_}4439{_}He came toward her and stood with one elbow on the mantel-piece, looking down at her--a quiet, strong man, who had already forgotten his feat of endurance of a few hours earlier.
10132{_}4440{_}"These people," he said, "would die of starvation and cold and sickness if we did not help them.
10132{_}4441{_}It is simply impossible for them in the few months that they can work the land to cultivate it so as to yield any more than their taxes.
10132{_}4442{_}They are overtaxed, and no one cares.
10132{_}4443{_}The army must be kept up and a huge Civil Service, and no one cares what happens to the peasants.
10132{_}4444{_}Some day the peasants _must_ turn, but not yet.
10132{_}4445{_}It is a question for all Russian land-owners to face, and nobody faces it.
10132{_}4446{_}If any one tries to improve the condition of his peasants--they were happier a thousand times as serfs--the bureaucrats of Petersburg mark him down and he is forced to leave the country.
10132{_}4447{_}The whole fabric of this Government is rotten, but every-one, except the peasants, would suffer by its fall, and therefore it stands."
10132{_}4448{_}Etta was staring into the fire.
10132{_}4449{_}It was impossible to say whether she heard with comprehension or not.
10132{_}4450{_}Paul went on:  "There is nothing left, therefore, but to go and do good by stealth.
10132{_}4451{_}I studied medicine with that view.
10132{_}4452{_}Steinmetz has scraped and economized the working of the estate for the same purpose.
10132{_}4453{_}The Government will not allow us to have a doctor; they prevent us from organizing relief and education on anything like an adequate scale.
10132{_}4454{_}They do it all by underhand means.
10132{_}4455{_}They have not the pluck to oppose us openly!
10132{_}4456{_}For years we have been doing what we can.
10132{_}4457{_}We have almost eradicated cholera.
10132{_}4458{_}They do not die of starvation now.
10132{_}4459{_}And they are learning--very slowly, but still they are learning.
10132{_}4460{_}We--I--thought you might be interested in your people; you might want to help."
10132{_}4461{_}She gave a short little nod.
10132{_}4462{_}There was a suggestion of suspense in her whole being and attitude, as if she were waiting to hear something which she knew could not be avoided.
10132{_}4463{_}"A few years ago," he went on, "a gigantic scheme was set on foot.
10132{_}4464{_}I told you a little about it--the Charity League."
10132{_}4465{_}Her lips moved, but no sound came from them, so she nodded a second time.
10132{_}4466{_}A tiny carriage-clock on the mantel-piece struck seven, and she looked up in a startled way, as if the sound had frightened her.
10132{_}4467{_}The castle was quite still.
10132{_}4468{_}Silence seemed to brood over the old walls.
10132{_}4469{_}"That fell through," he went on, "as I told you.
10132{_}4470{_}It was betrayed.
10132{_}4471{_}Stepan Lanovitch was banished.
10132{_}4472{_}He has escaped, however; Steinmetz has seen him.
10132{_}4473{_}He succeeded in destroying some of the papers before the place was searched after the robbery--one paper in particular.
10132{_}4474{_}If he had not destroyed that, I should have been banished.
10132{_}4475{_}I was one of the leaders of the Charity League.
10132{_}4476{_}Steinmetz and I got the thing up.
10132{_}4477{_}It would have been for the happiness of millions of peasants if it had not been betrayed.
10132{_}4478{_}In time--we shall find out who did it."
10132{_}4479{_}He paused.
10132{_}4480{_}He did not say what he would do when he had found out.
10132{_}4481{_}Etta was staring into the fire.
10132{_}4482{_}Her lips were dry.
10132{_}4483{_}She hardly seemed to be breathing.
10132{_}4484{_}"It is possible," he went on in his strong, quiet, inexorable voice, "that Stepan Lanovitch knows now."
10132{_}4485{_}Etta did not move.
10132{_}4486{_}She was staring into the fire--staring--staring.
10132{_}4487{_}Then she slowly fainted, rolling from the low chair to the fur hearth-rug.
10132{_}4488{_}Paul picked her up like a child and carried her to the bedroom, where the maids were waiting to dress her.
10132{_}4489{_}"Here," he said, "your mistress has fainted from the fatigue of the journey."
10132{_}4490{_}And, with his practised medical knowledge, he himself tended her.
10132{_}4491{_}CHAPTER XXV   OSTERNO  "Always gay; always gay!"
10132{_}4492{_}laughed Steinmetz, rubbing his broad hands together and looking down into the face of Maggie, who was busy at the breakfast-table.
10132{_}4493{_}"Yes," answered the girl, glancing toward Paul, leaning against the window reading his letters.
10132{_}4494{_}"Yes, always gay.
10132{_}4495{_}Why not?"
10132{_}4496{_}Karl Steinmetz saw the glance.
10132{_}4497{_}It was one of the little daily incidents that one sees and half forgets.
10132{_}4498{_}He only half forgot it.
10132{_}4499{_}"Why not, indeed?"
10132{_}4500{_}he answered.
10132{_}4501{_}"And you will be glad to hear that Ivanovitch is as ready as yourself this morning to treat the matter as a joke.
10132{_}4502{_}He is none the worse for his freezing, and all the better for his experience.
10132{_}4503{_}You have added another friend, my dear young lady, to a list which is, doubtless, a very long one."
10132{_}4504{_}"He is a nice man," answered Maggie.
10132{_}4505{_}"How is it," she asked, after a little pause, "that there are more men in the lower classes whom one can call nice than among their betters?"
10132{_}4506{_}Paul paused between two letters, hearing the question.
10132{_}4507{_}He looked up as if interested in the answer, but did not join in the conversation.
10132{_}4508{_}"Because dealing with animals and with nature is more conducive to niceness than too much trafficking with human beings," replied Steinmetz promptly.
10132{_}4509{_}"I suppose that is it," said Maggie, lifting the tea-pot lid and looking in.
10132{_}4510{_}"At all events, it is the sort of answer one might expect from you.
10132{_}4511{_}You are always hard on human nature."
10132{_}4512{_}"I take it as I find it," replied Steinmetz, with a laugh, "but I do not worry about it like some people.
10132{_}4513{_}Now, Paul would like to alter the course of the world."
10132{_}4514{_}As he spoke he half turned toward Paul, as if suggesting that he should give an opinion, and this little action had the effect of putting a stop to the conversation.
10132{_}4515{_}Maggie had plenty to say to Steinmetz, but toward Paul her mental attitude was different.
10132{_}4516{_}She was probably unaware of this little fact.
10132{_}4517{_}"There," she said, after a pause, "I have obeyed Etta's instructions.
10132{_}4518{_}She does not want us to begin, I suppose?"
10132{_}4519{_}"No," replied Paul.
10132{_}4520{_}"She will be down in a minute."
10132{_}4521{_}"I hope the princess is not overtired," said Steinmetz, with a certain formal politeness which seemed to accompany any mention of Etta's name.
10132{_}4522{_}"Not at all, thank you," replied Etta herself, coming into the room at that moment.
10132{_}4523{_}She looked fresh and self-confident.
10132{_}4524{_}"On the contrary, I am full of energy and eagerness to explore the castle.
10132{_}4525{_}One naturally takes an interest in one's baronial halls."
10132{_}4526{_}With this she walked slowly across to the window.
10132{_}4527{_}She stood there looking out, and every one in the room was watching.
10132{_}4528{_}On looking for the first time on the same view, a few moments earlier, Maggie had uttered a little cry of surprise, and had then remained silent.
10132{_}4529{_}Etta looked out of the window and said nothing.
10132{_}4530{_}It was a most singular out-look--weird, uncouth, prehistoric, as some parts of the earth still are.
10132{_}4531{_}The castle was built on the edge of a perpendicular cliff.
10132{_}4532{_}On this side it was impregnable.
10132{_}4533{_}Any object dropped from the breakfast-room window would fall a clear two hundred feet to the brawling Oster River.
10132{_}4534{_}The rock was black, and shining like the topmost crags of an Alpine mountain where snow and ice have polished the bare stone.
10132{_}4535{_}Beyond and across the river lay the boundless steppe--a sheet of virgin snow.
10132{_}4536{_}Etta stood looking over this to the far horizon, where the white snow and the gray sky softly merged into one.
10132{_}4537{_}Her first remark was characteristic, as first and last remarks usually are.
10132{_}4538{_}"And as far as you can see is yours?"
10132{_}4539{_}she asked.
10132{_}4540{_}"Yes," answered Paul simply, with that calm which only comes with hereditary possession.
10132{_}4541{_}The observation attracted Steinmetz's attention.
10132{_}4542{_}He went to another window, and looked across the waste critically.
10132{_}4543{_}"Four times as far as we can see is his," he said.
10132{_}4544{_}Etta looked out slowly and comprehensively, absorbing it all like a long, sweet drink.
10132{_}4545{_}There was no hereditary calmness in her sense of possession.
10132{_}4546{_}"And where is Thors?"
10132{_}4547{_}she asked.
10132{_}4548{_}Paul stretched out his arm, pointing with a lean, steady finger:  "It lies out there," he answered.
10132{_}4549{_}Another of the little incidents that are only half forgotten.
10132{_}4550{_}Some of the persons assembled in that room remembered the pointing finger long afterward.
10132{_}4551{_}"It makes one feel very small," said Etta, turning to the breakfast-table--"at no time a pleasant sensation.
10132{_}4552{_}Do you know," she said, after a little pause, "I think it probable that I shall become very fond of Osterno, but I wish it was nearer to civilization."
10132{_}4553{_}Paul looked pleased.
10132{_}4554{_}Steinmetz had a queer expression on his face.
10132{_}4555{_}Maggie murmured something about one's surroundings making but little difference to one's happiness, and the subject was wisely shelved.
10132{_}4556{_}After breakfast Steinmetz withdrew.
10132{_}4557{_}"Now," said Paul, "shall I show you the old place, you and Maggie?"
10132{_}4558{_}Etta signified her readiness, but Maggie said that she had letters to write, that Etta could show her the castle another time, when the men were out shooting, perhaps.
10132{_}4559{_}"But," said Etta, "I shall do it horribly badly.
10132{_}4560{_}They are not my ancestors, you know.
10132{_}4561{_}I shall attach the stories to the wrong people, and locate the ghost in the wrong room.
10132{_}4562{_}You will be wise to take Paul's guidance."
10132{_}4563{_}"No, thank you," replied Maggie, quite firmly and frankly.
10132{_}4564{_}"I feel inclined to write; and the feeling is rare, so I must take advantage of it."
10132{_}4565{_}The girl looked at her cousin with something in her honest blue eyes that almost amounted to wonder.
10132{_}4566{_}Etta was always surprising her.
10132{_}4567{_}There was a whole gamut of feeling, an octave of callow, half-formed girlish instincts, of which Etta seemed to be deprived.
10132{_}4568{_}If she had ever had them, no trace was left of their whilom presence.
10132{_}4569{_}At first Maggie had flatly refused to come to Russia.
10132{_}4570{_}When Paul pressed her to do so, she accepted with a sort of wonder.
10132{_}4571{_}There was something which she did not understand.
10132{_}4572{_}The same instinct made her refuse now to accompany Paul and Etta over their new home.
10132{_}4573{_}Again Etta pressed her, showing her lack of some feeling which Maggie indefinitely knew she ought to have had.
10132{_}4574{_}This time Paul made no sign.
10132{_}4575{_}He added no word to Etta's persuasions, but stood gravely looking at his wife.
10132{_}4576{_}When the door had closed behind them, Maggie stood for some minutes by the window looking out over the snow-clad plain, the rugged, broken rocks beneath her.
10132{_}4577{_}Then she turned to the writing-table.
10132{_}4578{_}She resolutely took pen and paper, but the least thing seemed to distract her attention--the coronet on the note-paper cost her five minutes of far-off reflection.
10132{_}4579{_}She took up the pen again, and wrote "Dear Mother."
10132{_}4580{_}The room grew darker.
10132{_}4581{_}Maggie looked up.
10132{_}4582{_}The snow had begun again.
10132{_}4583{_}It was driving past the window with a silent, purposeful monotony.
10132{_}4584{_}The girl drew the writing-case toward her.
10132{_}4585{_}She examined the pen critically and dipped it into the ink.
10132{_}4586{_}But she added nothing to the two words already written.
10132{_}4587{_}The castle of Osterno is almost unique in the particular that one roof covers the ancient and the modern buildings.
10132{_}4588{_}The vast reception-rooms, worthy of the name of state-rooms, adjoin the small stone-built apartments of the fortress which Paul's ancestors held against the Tartars.
10132{_}4589{_}This grimmer side of the building Paul reserved to the last for reasons of his own, and Etta's manifest delight in the grandeur of the more modern apartments fully rewarded him.
10132{_}4590{_}Here, again, that side of her character manifested itself which has already been shown.
10132{_}4591{_}She was dazzled and exhilarated by the splendor of it all, and the immediate effect was a feeling of affection toward the man to whom this belonged; who was in act, if not in word, laying it at her feet.
10132{_}4592{_}When they passed from the lofty rooms to the dimmer passages of the old castle Etta's spirits visibly dropped, her interest slackened.
10132{_}4593{_}He told her of tragedies enacted in by-gone times--such ancient tales of violent death and broken hearts as attach themselves to gray stone walls and dungeon keeps.
10132{_}4594{_}She only half listened, for her mind was busy with the splendors they had left behind, with the purposes to which such splendors could be turned.
10132{_}4595{_}And the sum total of her thoughts was gratified vanity.
10132{_}4596{_}Her bright presence awakened the gloom of ages within the dimly lit historic rooms.
10132{_}4597{_}Her laugh sounded strangely light and frivolous and shallow in the silence of the ages which had brooded within these walls since the days of Tamerlane.
10132{_}4598{_}It was perhaps the greatest tragedy of the Alexis family, this beautiful tragedy that walked by the side of Paul.
10132{_}4599{_}"I am glad your grandfather brought French architects here and built the modern side," she said.
10132{_}4600{_}"These rooms are, of course, very interesting, but gloomy--horribly gloomy, Paul.
10132{_}4601{_}There is a smell of ghosts and dulness."
10132{_}4602{_}"All the same, I like these rooms," answered Paul.
10132{_}4603{_}"Steinmetz and I used to live entirely on this side of the house.
10132{_}4604{_}This is the smoking-room.
10132{_}4605{_}We shot those bears, and all the deer.
10132{_}4606{_}That is a wolf's head.
10132{_}4607{_}He killed a keeper before I finished him off."
10132{_}4608{_}Etta looked at her husband with a curious little smile.
10132{_}4609{_}She sometimes felt proud of him, despite the ever present knowledge that, intellectually speaking, she was his superior.
10132{_}4610{_}There was something strong and simple and manly in a sort of mediaeval way that pleased her in this big husband of hers.
10132{_}4611{_}"And how did you finish him off?"
10132{_}4612{_}she asked.
10132{_}4613{_}"I choked him.
10132{_}4614{_}That bear knocked me down, but Steinmetz shot him.
10132{_}4615{_}We were four days out in the open after that elk.
10132{_}4616{_}This is a lynx--a queer face--rather like De Chauxville; the dogs killed him."
10132{_}4617{_}"But why do you not paper the room," asked Etta, with a shiver, "instead of this gloomy panelling?
10132{_}4618{_}It is so mysterious and creepy.
10132{_}4619{_}Quite suggestive of secret passages."
10132{_}4620{_}"There are no secret passages," answered Paul.
10132{_}4621{_}"But there is a room behind here.
10132{_}4622{_}This is the door.
10132{_}4623{_}I will show it to you presently.
10132{_}4624{_}I have things in there I want to show you.
10132{_}4625{_}I keep all my medicines and appliances in there.
10132{_}4626{_}It is our secret surgery and office.
10132{_}4627{_}In that room the Charity League was organized."
10132{_}4628{_}Etta turned away suddenly and went to the narrow window, where she sat on a low window-seat, looking down into the snow-clad depths.
10132{_}4629{_}"I did not know you were a doctor," she said.
10132{_}4630{_}"I doctor the peasants," replied Paul, "in a rough-and-ready way.
10132{_}4631{_}I took my degree on purpose.
10132{_}4632{_}But, of course, they do not know that it is I; they think I am a doctor from Moscow.
10132{_}4633{_}I put on an old coat, and wear a scarf, so that they cannot see my face.
10132{_}4634{_}I only go to them at night.
10132{_}4635{_}It would never do for the Government to know that we attempt to do good to the peasants.
10132{_}4636{_}We have to keep it a secret even from the people themselves.
10132{_}4637{_}And they hate us.
10132{_}4638{_}They groan and hoot when we drive through the village.
10132{_}4639{_}But they never attempt to do us any harm; they are too much afraid of us."
10132{_}4640{_}When Etta rose and came toward him her face was colorless.
10132{_}4641{_}"Let me see this room," she said.
10132{_}4642{_}He opened the door and followed her into the apartment, which has already been described.
10132{_}4643{_}Here he told further somewhat bald details of the work he had attempted to do.
10132{_}4644{_}It is to be feared that he made neither an interesting nor a romantic story of it.
10132{_}4645{_}There were too many details--too much statistic, and no thrilling realism whatever.
10132{_}4646{_}The experiences of a youthful curate in Bethnal Green would have made high tragedy beside the tale that this man told his wife of the land upon which God has assuredly laid His curse--Aceldama, the field of blood.
10132{_}4647{_}Etta listened, and despite herself she became interested.
10132{_}4648{_}She was sitting in a chair usually occupied by Steinmetz.
10132{_}4649{_}There was a faint aroma of tobacco-smoke.
10132{_}4650{_}The atmosphere of the room was manly and energetic.
10132{_}4651{_}Paul showed her his simple stores of medicine--the old coat saturated with disinfectants which had become the recognized outward sign of the Moscow doctor.
10132{_}4652{_}"And do other people, other noblemen, try to do this sort of thing too?"
10132{_}4653{_}asked Etta at length.
10132{_}4654{_}"Catrina Lanovitch does," replied Paul.
10132{_}4655{_}"What?
10132{_}4656{_}The girl with the hair?"
10132{_}4657{_}"Yes," answered Paul.
10132{_}4658{_}He had never noticed Catrina's hair.
10132{_}4659{_}Etta's appraising eye had seen more in one second than Paul had perceived in twenty years.
10132{_}4660{_}"Yes," he answered.
10132{_}4661{_}"But, of course, she is handicapped."
10132{_}4662{_}"By her appearance?"
10132{_}4663{_}"No; by her circumstances.
10132{_}4664{_}Her name is sufficient to handicap her every moment in this country.
10132{_}4665{_}But she does a great deal.
10132{_}4666{_}She--she found me out, confound her!"
10132{_}4667{_}Etta had risen; she was looking curiously at the cupboard where Paul's infected clothes were hanging.
10132{_}4668{_}He had forbidden her to go near it.
10132{_}4669{_}She turned and looked at him.
10132{_}4670{_}"Found you out!
10132{_}4671{_}How?"
10132{_}4672{_}she asked, with a queer smile.
10132{_}4673{_}"Saw through my disguise."
10132{_}4674{_}"Yes--she would do that!"
10132{_}4675{_}said Etta aloud to herself.
10132{_}4676{_}"What is this door?"
10132{_}4677{_}she asked, after a pause.
10132{_}4678{_}"It leads to an inner room," replied Paul, "where Steinmetz usually works."
10132{_}4679{_}He passed in front of her and opened the door.
10132{_}4680{_}As he was doing so Etta went on in the train of her thoughts:  "So Catrina knows?"
10132{_}4681{_}"Yes."
10132{_}4682{_}"And no one else?"
10132{_}4683{_}Paul made no answer; for he had passed on into the smaller room, where Steinmetz was seated at a writing-table.
10132{_}4684{_}"Except, of course, Herr Steinmetz?"
10132{_}4685{_}Etta went on interrogatively.
10132{_}4686{_}"Madame," said the German, looking up with his pleasant smile, "I know _every thing_."
10132{_}4687{_}And he went on writing.
10132{_}4688{_}CHAPTER XXVI   BLOODHOUNDS  The table d'hote of the Hotel de Moscou at Tver had just begun.
10132{_}4689{_}The soup had been removed; the diners were engaged in igniting their first cigarette at the candles placed between each pair of them for that purpose.
10132{_}4690{_}By nature the modern Russian is a dignified and somewhat reserved gentleman.
10132{_}4691{_}By circumstance he has been schooled into a state of guarded unsociability.
10132{_}4692{_}If there is a seat at a public table conveniently removed from those occupied by earlier arrivals the new-comer invariably takes it.
10132{_}4693{_}In Russia one converses--as in Scotland one jokes--with difficulty.
10132{_}4694{_}A Russian table d'hote is therefore any thing but hilarious in its tendency.
10132{_}4695{_}A certain number of grave-faced gentlemen and a few broad-jowled ladies are visibly constrained by the force of circumstance to dine at the same table and hour, et voila tout.
10132{_}4696{_}There is no pretence that any more sociable and neighborly motive has brought them together.
10132{_}4697{_}Indeed, they each suspect the other of being a German, or a Nihilist, or, worse still, a Government servant.
10132{_}4698{_}They therefore sit as far apart as possible, and smoke cigarettes between and during the courses with that self-centred absorption which would be rude, if it were not entirely satisfactory, to the average Briton.
10132{_}4699{_}The ladies, of course, have the same easy method of showing a desire for silence and reflection in a country where nurses carrying infants usually smoke in the streets, and where a dainty confectioner's assistant places her cigarette between her lips in order to leave her hands free for the service of her customers.
10132{_}4700{_}The table d'hote of the Hotel de Moscou at Tver was no exception to the general rule.
10132{_}4701{_}In Russia, by the way, there are no exceptions to general rules.
10132{_}4702{_}The personal habits of the native of Cronstadt differ in no way from those of the Czar's subject living in Petropavlovsk, eight thousand miles away.
10132{_}4703{_}Around the long table of the host were seated, at respectable intervals, a dozen or more gentlemen, who gazed stolidly at each other from time to time, while the host himself smiled broadly upon them all from that end of the room where the lift and the smell of cooking exercise their calling--the one to spoil the appetite, the other to pander to it when spoilt.
10132{_}4704{_}Of these dozen gentlemen we have only to deal with one--a man of broad, high forehead, of colorless eyes, of a mask-like face, who consumed what was put before him with as little noise as possible.
10132{_}4705{_}Known in Paris as "Ce bon Vassili," this traveller.
10132{_}4706{_}But in Paris one does not always use the word bon in its English sense of "good."
10132{_}4707{_}M. Vassili was evidently desirous of attracting as little attention as circumstances would allow.
10132{_}4708{_}He was obviously doing his best to look like one who travelled in the interest of braid or buttons.
10132{_}4709{_}Moreover, when Claude de Chauxville entered the table d'hote room, he concealed whatever surprise he may have felt behind a cloud of cigarette smoke.
10132{_}4710{_}Through the same blue haze he met the Frenchman's eye, a moment later, without the faintest twinkle of recognition.
10132{_}4711{_}These two worthies went through the weird courses provided by a cook professing a knowledge of French _cuisine_ without taking any compromising notice of each other.
10132{_}4712{_}When the meal was over Vassili inscribed the number of his bedroom in large figures on the label of his bottle of St. Emilion--after the manner of wise commercial-travellers in continental hotels.
10132{_}4713{_}He subsequently turned the bottle round so that Claude de Chauxville could scarcely fail to read the number, and with a vague and general bow he left the room.
10132{_}4714{_}In his apartment the genial Vassili threw more wood into the stove, drew forward the two regulation arm-chairs, and lighted all the candles provided.
10132{_}4715{_}He then rang the bell and ordered liqueurs.
10132{_}4716{_}There was evidently something in the nature of an entertainment about to take place in apartment No.
10132{_}4717{_}44 of the Hotel de Moscou.
10132{_}4718{_}Before long a discreet knock announced the arrival of the expected visitor.
10132{_}4719{_}"Entrez!"
10132{_}4720{_}cried Vassili; and De Chauxville stood before him, with a smile which in French is called crane.
10132{_}4721{_}"A pleasure," said Vassili, behind his wooden face, "that I did not anticipate in Tver."
10132{_}4722{_}"And consequently one that carries its own mitigation.
10132{_}4723{_}An unanticipated pleasure, mon ami, is always inopportune.
10132{_}4724{_}I make no doubt that you were sorry to see me."
10132{_}4725{_}"On the contrary.
10132{_}4726{_}Will you sit?"
10132{_}4727{_}"I can hardly believe," went on De Chauxville, taking the proffered chair, "that my appearance was opportune--on the principle, ha!
10132{_}4728{_}ha!
10132{_}4729{_}that a flower growing out of place is a weed.
10132{_}4730{_}Gentlemen of the--eh--Home Office prefer, I know, to travel quietly!"
10132{_}4731{_}He spread out his expressive hands as if smoothing the path of M. Vassili through this stony world.
10132{_}4732{_}"Incognito," he added guilelessly.
10132{_}4733{_}"One does not publish one's name from the housetops," replied the Russian, with a glimmer of pride in his eyes, "especially if it happen to be not quite obscure; but between friends, my dear baron--between friends."
10132{_}4734{_}"Yes.
10132{_}4735{_}Then what are you doing in Tver?"
10132{_}4736{_}enquired De Chauxville, with engaging frankness.
10132{_}4737{_}"Ah, that is a long story.
10132{_}4738{_}But I will tell you--never fear--I will tell you on the usual terms."
10132{_}4739{_}"Viz?"
10132{_}4740{_}enquired the Frenchman, lighting a cigarette.
10132{_}4741{_}Vassili accepted the match with a bow, and did likewise.
10132{_}4742{_}He blew a guileless cloud of smoke toward the dingy ceiling.
10132{_}4743{_}"Exchange, my dear baron, exchange."
10132{_}4744{_}"Oh, certainly," replied De Chauxville, who knew that Vassili was in all probability fully informed as to his movements past and prospective.
10132{_}4745{_}"I am going to visit some old friends in this Government--the Lanovitches, at Thors."
10132{_}4746{_}"Ah!"
10132{_}4747{_}"You know them?"
10132{_}4748{_}Vassili raised his shoulders and made a little gesture with his cigarette, as much as to say, "Why ask?"
10132{_}4749{_}De Chauxville looked at his companion keenly.
10132{_}4750{_}He was wondering whether this man knew that he--Claude de Chauxville--loved Etta Howard Alexis, and consequently hated her husband.
10132{_}4751{_}He was wondering how much or how little this impenetrable individual knew and suspected.
10132{_}4752{_}"I have always said," observed Vassili suddenly, "that for unmitigated impertinence give me a diplomatist."
10132{_}4753{_}"Ah!
10132{_}4754{_}And what would you desire that I should, for the same commodity, give you now?"
10132{_}4755{_}"A woman."
10132{_}4756{_}There was a short silence in the room while these two birds of a feather reflected.
10132{_}4757{_}Suddenly Vassili tapped himself on the chest with his forefinger.
10132{_}4758{_}"It was I," he said, "who crushed that very dangerous movement--the Charity League."
10132{_}4759{_}"I know it."
10132{_}4760{_}"A movement, my dear baron, to educate the moujik, if you please.
10132{_}4761{_}To feed him and clothe him, and teach him--to be discontented with his lot.
10132{_}4762{_}To raise him up and make a man of him.
10132{_}4763{_}Pah!
10132{_}4764{_}He is a beast.
10132{_}4765{_}Let him be treated as such.
10132{_}4766{_}Let him work.
10132{_}4767{_}If he will not work, let him starve and die."
10132{_}4768{_}"The man who cannot contribute toward the support of those above him in life is superfluous," said De Chauxville glibly.
10132{_}4769{_}"Precisely.
10132{_}4770{_}Now, my dear baron, listen to me!"
10132{_}4771{_}The genial Vassili leaned forward and tapped with one finger on the knee of De Chauxville, as if knocking at the door of his attention.
10132{_}4772{_}"I am all ears, mon bon monsieur," replied the Frenchman, rather coldly.
10132{_}4773{_}He had just been reflecting that, after all, he did not want any favor from Vassili for the moment, and the manner of the latter was verging on the familiar.
10132{_}4774{_}"The woman--who--sold--me--the Charity League papers dined at my house in Paris--a fortnight ago," said Vassili, with a staccato tap on his companion's knee by way of emphasis to each word.
10132{_}4775{_}"Then, my friend, I cannot--congratulate--you--on the society--in--which you move," replied De Chauxville, mimicking his manner.
10132{_}4776{_}"Bah!
10132{_}4777{_}She was a princess!"
10132{_}4778{_}"A princess?"
10132{_}4779{_}"Yes, of your acquaintance, M. le Baron!
10132{_}4780{_}And she came to my house with her--eh--husband--the Prince Paul Howard Alexis."
10132{_}4781{_}This was news indeed.
10132{_}4782{_}De Chauxville leaned back and passed his slim white hand across his brow with a slow pressure, as if wiping some writing from a slate--as if his forehead bore the writing of his thoughts and he was wiping it away.
10132{_}4783{_}And the thoughts he thus concealed--who can count them?
10132{_}4784{_}For thoughts are the quickest and the longest and the saddest things of this life.
10132{_}4785{_}The first thought was that if he had known this three months earlier he could have made Etta marry him.
10132{_}4786{_}And that thought had a thousand branches.
10132{_}4787{_}With Etta for his wife he might have been a different man.
10132{_}4788{_}One can never tell what the effect of an acquired desire may be.
10132{_}4789{_}One can only judge by analogy, and it would seem that it is a frustrated desire that makes the majority of villains.
10132{_}4790{_}But the news coming, thus too late, only served an evil purpose.
10132{_}4791{_}For in that flash of thought Claude de Chauxville saw Paul's secrets given to him; Paul's wealth meted out to him; Paul in exile; Paul dead in Siberia, where death comes easily; Paul's widow Claude de Chauxville's wife.
10132{_}4792{_}He wiped all the thoughts away, and showed to Vassili a face that was as composed and impertinent as usual.
10132{_}4793{_}"You said 'her--eh--husband,'" he observed.
10132{_}4794{_}"Why?
10132{_}4795{_}Why did you add that little 'eh,' my friend?"
10132{_}4796{_}Vassili rose and walked to the door that led through into his bedroom from the salon in which they were sitting.
10132{_}4797{_}It was possible to enter the bedroom from another door and overhear any conversation that might be passing in the sitting-room.
10132{_}4798{_}The investigation was apparently satisfactory, for the Russian came back.
10132{_}4799{_}But he did not sit down.
10132{_}4800{_}Instead, he stood leaning against the tall china stove.
10132{_}4801{_}"Needless to tell you," he observed, "the antecedents of the--princess."
10132{_}4802{_}"Quite needless."
10132{_}4803{_}"Married seven years ago to Charles Sydney Bamborough," promptly giving the unnecessary information which was not wanted.
10132{_}4804{_}De Chauxville nodded.
10132{_}4805{_}"Where is Sydney Bamborough?"
10132{_}4806{_}asked Vassili, with his mask-like smile.
10132{_}4807{_}"Dead," replied the other quietly.
10132{_}4808{_}"Prove it."
10132{_}4809{_}De Chauxville looked up sharply.
10132{_}4810{_}The cigarette dropped from his fingers to the floor.
10132{_}4811{_}His face was yellow and drawn, with a singular tremble of the lips, which were twisted to one side.
10132{_}4812{_}"Good God!"
10132{_}4813{_}he whispered hoarsely.
10132{_}4814{_}There was only one thought in his mind--a sudden wild desire to rise up and stand by Etta against the whole world.
10132{_}4815{_}Verily we cannot tell what love may make of us, whither it may lead us.
10132{_}4816{_}We only know that it never leaves us as it found us.
10132{_}4817{_}Then, leaning quietly against the stove, Vassili stated his case.
10132{_}4818{_}"Rather more than a year ago," he said, "I received an offer of the papers connected with a great scheme in this country.
10132{_}4819{_}After certain enquiries had been made I accepted the offer.
10132{_}4820{_}I paid a fabulous price for the papers.
10132{_}4821{_}They were brought to me by a lady wearing a thick veil--a lady I had never seen before.
10132{_}4822{_}I asked no questions, and paid her the money.
10132{_}4823{_}It subsequently transpired that the papers had been stolen, as you perhaps know, from the house of Count Stepan Lanovitch--the house to which you happen to be going--at Thors.
10132{_}4824{_}Well, that is all ancient history.
10132{_}4825{_}It is to be supposed that the papers were stolen by Sydney Bamborough, who brought them here--probably to this hotel, where his wife was staying.
10132{_}4826{_}He handed her the papers, and she conveyed them to me in Paris.
10132{_}4827{_}But before she reached Petersburg they would have been missed by Stepan Lanovitch, who would naturally suspect the man who had been staying in his house, Bamborough--a man with a doubtful reputation in the diplomatic world, a professed doer of dirty jobs.
10132{_}4828{_}Foreseeing this, and knowing that the League was a big thing, with a few violent members on its books, Sydney Bamborough did not attempt to leave Russia by the western route.
10132{_}4829{_}He probably decided to go through Nijni, down the Volga, across the Caspian, and so on to Persia and India.
10132{_}4830{_}You follow me?"
10132{_}4831{_}"Perfectly!"
10132{_}4832{_}answered De Chauxville coldly.
10132{_}4833{_}"I have been here a week," went on the Russian spy, "making enquiries.
10132{_}4834{_}I have worked the whole affair out, link by link, till the evening when the husband and wife parted.
10132{_}4835{_}She went west with the papers.
10132{_}4836{_}Where did he go?"
10132{_}4837{_}De Chauxville picked up the cigarette, looked at it curiously, as at a relic--the relic of the moment of strongest emotion through which he had ever passed--and threw it into the ash-tray.
10132{_}4838{_}He did not speak, and after a moment Vassili went on, stating his case with lawyer-like clearness.
10132{_}4839{_}"A body was found on the steppe," he said; "the body of a middle-aged man dressed as a small commercial traveller would dress.
10132{_}4840{_}He had a little money in his pocket, but nothing to identify him.
10132{_}4841{_}He was buried here in Tver by the police, who received their information by an anonymous post-card posted in Tver.
10132{_}4842{_}The person who had found the body did not want to be implicated in any enquiry.
10132{_}4843{_}Now, who found the body?
10132{_}4844{_}Who was the dead man?
10132{_}4845{_}Mrs. Sydney Bamborough has assumed that the dead man was her husband; on the strength of that assumption she has become a princess.
10132{_}4846{_}A frail foundation upon which to build up her fortunes, eh?"
10132{_}4847{_}"How did she know that the body had been found?"
10132{_}4848{_}asked De Chauxville, perceiving the weak point in his companion's chain of argument.
10132{_}4849{_}"It was reported shortly in the local newspapers," replied Vassili, "and repeated in one or two continental journals, as the police were of opinion that the man was a foreigner.
10132{_}4850{_}Any one watching the newspapers would see it--otherwise the incident might pass unobserved."
10132{_}4851{_}"And you think," said De Chauxville, suppressing his excitement with an effort, "that the lady has risked every thing upon a supposition?"
10132{_}4852{_}"Knowing the lady, I do."
10132{_}4853{_}De Chauxville's dull eyes gleamed for a moment with an unwonted light.
10132{_}4854{_}All the civilization of the ages will not eradicate the primary instincts of men--and one of these, in good and bad alike, is to protect women.
10132{_}4855{_}The Frenchman bit the end of his cigarette, and angrily wiped the tobacco from his lips.
10132{_}4856{_}"She may have information of which you are ignorant," he suggested.
10132{_}4857{_}"Precisely.
10132{_}4858{_}It is that particular point which gives me trouble at the present moment.
10132{_}4859{_}It is that that I wish to discover."
10132{_}4860{_}De Chauxville looked up coolly.
10132{_}4861{_}He saw his advantage.
10132{_}4862{_}"Hence your sudden flow of communicativeness?"
10132{_}4863{_}he said.
10132{_}4864{_}Vassili nodded.
10132{_}4865{_}"You cannot find out for yourself, so you seek my help?"
10132{_}4866{_}went on the Frenchman.
10132{_}4867{_}Again the Russian nodded his head.
10132{_}4868{_}"And your price?"
10132{_}4869{_}said De Chauxville, drawing in his feet and leaning forward, apparently to study the pattern of the carpet.
10132{_}4870{_}The action concealed his face.
10132{_}4871{_}He was saving Etta, and he was ashamed of himself.
10132{_}4872{_}"When you have the information you may name your own price," said the Russian coldly.
10132{_}4873{_}There was a long silence.
10132{_}4874{_}Before speaking De Chauxville turned and took a glass of liqueur from the table.
10132{_}4875{_}His hand was not quite steady.
10132{_}4876{_}He raised the glass quickly and emptied it.
10132{_}4877{_}Then he rose and looked at his watch.
10132{_}4878{_}The silence was a compact.
10132{_}4879{_}"When the lady dined with you in Paris, did she recognize you?"
10132{_}4880{_}he asked.
10132{_}4881{_}"Yes; but she did not know that I recognized her."
10132{_}4882{_}For the moment they both overlooked Steinmetz.
10132{_}4883{_}De Chauxville stood reflecting.
10132{_}4884{_}"And your theory," he said, "respecting Sydney Bamborough--what is it?"
10132{_}4885{_}"If he got away to Nijni and the Volga, it is probable that he is in Eastern Siberia or in Persia at this moment.
10132{_}4886{_}He has not had time to get right across Asia yet."
10132{_}4887{_}De Chauxville moved toward the door.
10132{_}4888{_}With his fingers on the handle he paused again.
10132{_}4889{_}"I leave early to-morrow morning," he said.
10132{_}4890{_}Vassili nodded, or rather he bowed, in his grand way.
10132{_}4891{_}Then De Chauxville went out of the room.
10132{_}4892{_}They did not shake hands.
10132{_}4893{_}There is sometimes shame among thieves.
10132{_}4894{_}CHAPTER XXVII   IN THE WEB  "What I propose is that Catrina takes you for a drive, my dear baron, with her two ponies."
10132{_}4895{_}The countess had taken very good care to refrain from making this proposal to Catrina alone.
10132{_}4896{_}She was one of those mothers who rule their daughters by springing surprises upon them in a carefully selected company where the daughter is not free to reply.
10132{_}4897{_}De Chauxville bowed with outspread hands.
10132{_}4898{_}"If it will not bore mademoiselle," he replied.
10132{_}4899{_}The countess looked at her daughter with an unctuous smile, as if to urge her on to make the most of this opportunity.
10132{_}4900{_}It was one of the countess's chief troubles that she could not by hook or crook involve Catrina in any sort of a love intrigue.
10132{_}4901{_}She was the sort of mother who would have preferred to hear scandal about her daughter to hearing nothing.
10132{_}4902{_}"If it will not freeze monsieur," replied Catrina, with uncompromising honesty.
10132{_}4903{_}De Chauxville laughed in his frank way.
10132{_}4904{_}"I am not afraid of coldness--of the atmosphere, mademoiselle," he replied.
10132{_}4905{_}"I am most anxious to see your beautiful country.
10132{_}4906{_}It was quite dark during the last hour of my journey last night, and I had snow-sleepiness.
10132{_}4907{_}I saw nothing."
10132{_}4908{_}"You will see nothing but snow," said Catrina.
10132{_}4909{_}"Which is like the reserve of a young girl," added the Frenchman.
10132{_}4910{_}"It keeps warm that which is beneath it."
10132{_}4911{_}"You need not be afraid with Catrina," chimed in the countess, nodding and becking in a manner that clearly showed her assumption to herself of some vague compliment.
10132{_}4912{_}"She drives beautifully.
10132{_}4913{_}She is not nervous in that way.
10132{_}4914{_}I have never seen any one drive like her."
10132{_}4915{_}"I have no doubt," said De Chauxville, "that mademoiselle's hands are firm, despite their diminutiveness."
10132{_}4916{_}The countess was charmed--and showed it.
10132{_}4917{_}She frowned at Catrina, who remained grave and looked at the clock.
10132{_}4918{_}"When would you like to go?"
10132{_}4919{_}she asked De Chauxville, with that complete absence of affectation which the Russian, of all women of the world, alone have mastered in their conversation with men.
10132{_}4920{_}"Am I not at your service--now and always?"
10132{_}4921{_}responded the gallant baron.
10132{_}4922{_}"I hope not," replied Catrina quietly.
10132{_}4923{_}"There are occasions when I have no use for you.
10132{_}4924{_}Shall we say eleven o'clock?"
10132{_}4925{_}"With pleasure.
10132{_}4926{_}Then I will go and write my letters now," said the baron, quitting the room.
10132{_}4927{_}"A charming man!"
10132{_}4928{_}ejaculated the countess, before the door was well closed.
10132{_}4929{_}"A fool!"
10132{_}4930{_}corrected Catrina.
10132{_}4931{_}"I do not think you can say that, dear," sighed the countess, more in sorrow than in anger.
10132{_}4932{_}"A clever one," answered Catrina.
10132{_}4933{_}"There is a difference.
10132{_}4934{_}The clever ones are the worst."
10132{_}4935{_}The countess shrugged her shoulders hopelessly, and Catrina left the room.
10132{_}4936{_}She went upstairs to her own little den, where the piano stood.
10132{_}4937{_}It was the only room in the house that was not too warm, for here the window was occasionally opened--a proceeding which the countess considered scarcely short of criminal.
10132{_}4938{_}Catrina began to play, feverishly, nervously, with all the weird force of her nature.
10132{_}4939{_}She was like a very sick person seeking a desperate remedy--racing against time.
10132{_}4940{_}It was her habit to take her breaking heart thus to the great masters, to interpret their thoughts in their music, welding their melodies to the needs of her own sorrow.
10132{_}4941{_}She only had half an hour.
10132{_}4942{_}Of late music had failed her a little.
10132{_}4943{_}It had not given her the comfort she had usually extracted from solitude and the piano.
10132{_}4944{_}She was in a dangerous humor.
10132{_}4945{_}She was afraid of trusting herself to De Chauxville.
10132{_}4946{_}The time fled, and her humor did not change.
10132{_}4947{_}She was still playing when the door opened, and the countess stood before her flushed and angry, either or both being the effect of stairs upon emotion.
10132{_}4948{_}"Catrina!"
10132{_}4949{_}the elder lady exclaimed.
10132{_}4950{_}"The sleigh is at the door, and the count is waiting.
10132{_}4951{_}I cannot tell what you are thinking of.
10132{_}4952{_}It is not every-body who would be so attentive to you.
10132{_}4953{_}Just look at your hair.
10132{_}4954{_}Why can't you dress like other girls?"
10132{_}4955{_}"Because I am not made like other girls," replied Catrina--and who knows what bitterness of reproach there was in such an answer from daughter to mother?
10132{_}4956{_}"Hush, child," replied the countess, whose anger usually took the form of personal abuse.
10132{_}4957{_}"You are as the good God made you."
10132{_}4958{_}"Then the good God must have made me in the dark," cried Catrina, flinging out of the room.
10132{_}4959{_}"She will be down directly," said the Countess Lanovitch to De Chauxville, whom she found smoking a cigarette in the hall.
10132{_}4960{_}"She naturally--he!
10132{_}4961{_}he!--wishes to make a careful toilet."
10132{_}4962{_}De Chauxville bowed gravely, without committing himself to any observation, and offered her a cigarette, which she accepted.
10132{_}4963{_}Having achieved his purpose, he did not now propose to convey the impression that he admired Catrina.
10132{_}4964{_}In a few moments the girl appeared, drawing on her fur gloves.
10132{_}4965{_}Before the door was opened the countess discreetly retired to the enervating warmth of her own apartments.
10132{_}4966{_}Catrina gathered up the reins and gave a little cry, at which the ponies leaped forward, and in a whirl of driven snow the sleigh glided off between the pines.
10132{_}4967{_}At first there was no opportunity of conversation, for the ponies were fresh and troublesome.
10132{_}4968{_}The road over which they were passing had not been beaten down by the passage of previous sleighs, so that the powdery snow rose up like dust, and filled the eyes and mouth.
10132{_}4969{_}"It will be better presently," gasped Catrina, wrestling with her fractious little Tartar thoroughbreds, "when we get out on to the high-road."
10132{_}4970{_}De Chauxville sat quite still.
10132{_}4971{_}If he felt any misgiving as to her power of mastering her team he kept it to himself.
10132{_}4972{_}There was a subtle difference in his manner toward Catrina when they were alone together, a suggestion of camaraderie, of a common interest and a common desire, of which she was conscious without being able to put definite meaning to it.
10132{_}4973{_}It annoyed and alarmed her.
10132{_}4974{_}While giving her full attention to the management of the sleigh, she was beginning to dread the first words of this man, who was merely wielding a cheap power acquired in the shady course of his career.
10132{_}4975{_}There is nothing so disarming as the assumed air of intimate knowledge of one's private thoughts and actions.
10132{_}4976{_}De Chauxville assumed this air with a skill against which Catrina's dogged strength of character was incapable of battling.
10132{_}4977{_}His manner conveyed the impression that he knew more of Catrina's inward thoughts than any other living being, and she was simple enough to be frightened into the conclusion that she had betrayed herself to him.
10132{_}4978{_}There is no simpler method of discovering a secret than to ignore its existence.
10132{_}4979{_}It is possible that De Chauxville became aware of Catrina's sidelong glances of anxiety in his direction.
10132{_}4980{_}He may have divined that silence was more effective than speech.
10132{_}4981{_}He sat looking straight in front of him, as if too deeply absorbed in his own thoughts to take even a passing interest in the scenery.
10132{_}4982{_}"Why did you come here?"
10132{_}4983{_}asked Catrina suddenly.
10132{_}4984{_}De Chauxville seemed to awake from a revery.
10132{_}4985{_}He turned and looked at her in assumed surprise.
10132{_}4986{_}They were on the high-road now, where the snow was beaten down, so conversation was easy.
10132{_}4987{_}"But--to see you, mademoiselle."
10132{_}4988{_}"I am not _that_ sort of girl," answered Catrina coldly.
10132{_}4989{_}"I want the truth."
10132{_}4990{_}De Chauxville gave a short laugh and looked at her.
10132{_}4991{_}"Prophets and kings have sought the truth, mademoiselle, and have not found it," he said lightly.
10132{_}4992{_}Catrina made no answer to this.
10132{_}4993{_}Her ponies required considerable attention.
10132{_}4994{_}Also, there are some minds like large banking houses--not dealing in small change.
10132{_}4995{_}That which passes in or out of such minds has its own standard of importance.
10132{_}4996{_}Such people are not of much use in these days, when we like to touch things lightly, adorning a tale but pointing no moral.
10132{_}4997{_}"I would ask you to believe that your society was one incentive to make me accept the countess's kind hospitality," the Frenchman observed after a pause.
10132{_}4998{_}"And?"
10132{_}4999{_}De Chauxville looked at her.
10132{_}5000{_}He had not met many women of solid intellect.
10132{_}5001{_}"And?"
10132{_}5002{_}repeated Catrina.
10132{_}5003{_}"I have others, of course."
10132{_}5004{_}Catrina gave a little nod and waited.
10132{_}5005{_}"I wish to be near Alexis," added De Chauxville.
10132{_}5006{_}Catrina was staring straight in front of her.
10132{_}5007{_}Her face had acquired a habit of hardening at the mention of Paul's name.
10132{_}5008{_}It was stone-like now, and set.
10132{_}5009{_}Perhaps she might have forgiven him if he had loved her once, if only for a little while.
10132{_}5010{_}She might have forgiven him, if only for the remembrance of that little while.
10132{_}5011{_}But Paul had always been a man of set purpose, and such men are cruel.
10132{_}5012{_}Even for her sake, even for the sake of his own vanity, he had never pretended to love Catrina.
10132{_}5013{_}He had never mistaken gratified vanity for dawning love, as millions of men do.
10132{_}5014{_}Or perhaps he was without vanity.
10132{_}5015{_}Some few men are so constructed.
10132{_}5016{_}"Do you love him so?"
10132{_}5017{_}asked Catrina, with a grim smile distorting her strong face.
10132{_}5018{_}"As much as you, mademoiselle," replied De Chauxville.
10132{_}5019{_}Catrina started.
10132{_}5020{_}She was not sure that she hated Paul.
10132{_}5021{_}Toward Etta, there was no mistake in her feeling, and this was so strong that, like an electric current, there was enough of it to pass through the wife and reach the husband.
10132{_}5022{_}Passion, like character, does not grow in crowded places.
10132{_}5023{_}In great cities men are all more or less alike.
10132{_}5024{_}It is only in solitary abodes that strong natures grow up in their own way.
10132{_}5025{_}Catrina had grown to womanhood in one of the solitary places of the earth.
10132{_}5026{_}She had no facile axiom, no powerful precedent, to guide her every step through life.
10132{_}5027{_}The woman who was in daily contact with her was immeasurably beneath her in mental power, in force of character, in those possibilities of love or hatred which go to make a strong life for good or for evil.
10132{_}5028{_}By the side of her daughter the Countess Lanovitch was as the willow, swayed by every wind, in the neighborhood of the oak, crooked and still and strong.
10132{_}5029{_}"In Petersburg you pledged yourself to help me," said De Chauxville.
10132{_}5030{_}And although she knew that in the letter this was false, she did not contradict him.
10132{_}5031{_}"I came here to claim fulfilment of your promise."
10132{_}5032{_}The hard blue eyes beneath the fur cap stared straight in front of them.
10132{_}5033{_}Catrina seemed to be driving like one asleep, for she noted nothing by the roadside.
10132{_}5034{_}So far as eye could reach over the snow-clad plain, through the silent pines, these two were alone in a white, dead world of their own.
10132{_}5035{_}Catrina never drove with bells.
10132{_}5036{_}There was no sound beyond the high-pitched drone of the steel runners over the powdery snow.
10132{_}5037{_}They were alone; unseen, unheard save of that Ear that listens in the waste places of the world.
10132{_}5038{_}"What do you want me to do?"
10132{_}5039{_}she asked.
10132{_}5040{_}"Oh, not very much!"
10132{_}5041{_}answered De Chauxville--a cautious man, who knew a woman's humor.
10132{_}5042{_}Catrina driving a pair of ponies in the clear, sharp air of Central Russia, and Catrina playing the piano in the enervating, flower-scented atmosphere of a drawing-room, were two different women.
10132{_}5043{_}De Chauxville was not the man to mistake the one for the other.
10132{_}5044{_}"Not very much, mademoiselle," he answered.
10132{_}5045{_}"I should like Mme.
10132{_}5046{_}la Comtesse to invite the whole Osterno party to dine, and sleep, perhaps, if one may suggest it."
10132{_}5047{_}Catrina wanted this too.
10132{_}5048{_}She wanted to torture herself with the sight of Etta, beautiful, self-confident, carelessly cognizant of Paul's love.
10132{_}5049{_}She wanted to see Paul look at his wife with the open admiration which she had set down as something else than love--something immeasurably beneath love as Catrina understood that passion.
10132{_}5050{_}Her soul, brooding under a weight of misery, was ready to welcome any change, should it only mean a greater misery.
10132{_}5051{_}"I can manage that," she said, "if they will come.
10132{_}5052{_}It was a prearranged matter that there should be a bear-hunt in our forests."
10132{_}5053{_}"That will do," answered De Chauxville reflectively; "in a few days, perhaps, if it suits the countess."
10132{_}5054{_}Catrina made no reply.
10132{_}5055{_}After a pause she spoke again, in her strange, jerky way.
10132{_}5056{_}"What will you gain by it?"
10132{_}5057{_}she asked.
10132{_}5058{_}De Chauxville shrugged his shoulders.
10132{_}5059{_}"Who knows?"
10132{_}5060{_}he answered.
10132{_}5061{_}"There are many things I want to know; many questions which can be answered only by one's own observation.
10132{_}5062{_}I want to see them together.
10132{_}5063{_}Are they happy?"
10132{_}5064{_}Catrina's face hardened.
10132{_}5065{_}"If there is a God in heaven, and he hears our prayers, they ought not to be," she replied curtly.
10132{_}5066{_}"She looked happy enough in Petersburg," said the Frenchman, who never told the truth for its own sake.
10132{_}5067{_}Whenever he thought that Catrina's hatred needed stimulation he mentioned Etta's name.
10132{_}5068{_}"There are other questions in my mind," he went on, "some of which you can answer, mademoiselle, if you care to."
10132{_}5069{_}Catrina's face expressed no great willingness to oblige.
10132{_}5070{_}"The Charity League," said De Chauxville, looking at her keenly; "I have always had a feeling of curiosity respecting it.
10132{_}5071{_}Was, for instance, our friend the Prince Pavlo implicated in that unfortunate affair?"
10132{_}5072{_}Catrina flushed suddenly.
10132{_}5073{_}She did not take her eyes from the ponies.
10132{_}5074{_}She was conscious of the unwonted color in her cheeks, which was slowly dying away beneath her companion's relentless gaze.
10132{_}5075{_}"You need not trouble to reply, mademoiselle," said De Chauxville, with his dark smile; "I am answered."
10132{_}5076{_}Catrina pulled the ponies up with a jerk, and proceeded to turn their willing heads toward home.
10132{_}5077{_}She was alarmed and disturbed.
10132{_}5078{_}Nothing seemed to be safe from the curiosity of this man, no secret secure, no prevarication of the slightest avail.
10132{_}5079{_}"There are other questions in my mind," said De Chauxville quietly, "but not now.
10132{_}5080{_}Mademoiselle is no doubt tired."
10132{_}5081{_}He leaned back, and when at length he spoke it was to give utterance to the trite commonplace of which he made a conversational study.
10132{_}5082{_}CHAPTER XXVIII   IN THE CASTLE OF THORS  A week later Catrina, watching from the window of her own small room, saw Paul lift Etta from the sleigh, and the sight made her clench her hands until the knuckles shone like polished ivory.
10132{_}5083{_}She turned and looked at herself in the mirror.
10132{_}5084{_}No one knew how she had tried one dress after another since luncheon, alone in her two rooms, having sent her maid down stairs.
10132{_}5085{_}No one knew the bitterness in this girl's heart as she contemplated her own reflection.
10132{_}5086{_}She went slowly down stairs to the long, dimly lighted drawing-room.
10132{_}5087{_}As she entered she heard her mother's cackling voice.
10132{_}5088{_}"Yes, princess," the countess was saying, "it is a quaint old house; little more than a fortified farm, I know.
10132{_}5089{_}But my husband's family were always strange.
10132{_}5090{_}They seem always to have ignored the little comforts and elegancies of life."
10132{_}5091{_}"It is most interesting," answered Etta's voice, and Catrina stepped forward into the light.
10132{_}5092{_}Formal greetings were exchanged, and Catrina saw Etta look anxiously toward the door through which she had just come.
10132{_}5093{_}She thought that she was looking for her husband.
10132{_}5094{_}But it was Claude de Chauxville for whose appearance Etta was waiting.
10132{_}5095{_}Paul and Steinmetz entered at the same moment by another door, and Catrina, who was talking to Maggie in English, suddenly stopped.
10132{_}5096{_}"Ah, Catrina," said Paul, "we have broken new ground for you.
10132{_}5097{_}There was no track from here to Osterno through the forest.
10132{_}5098{_}I made one this afternoon, so you have no excuse for remaining away, now."
10132{_}5099{_}"Thank you," answered Catrina, withdrawing her cold hand hurriedly from his friendly grasp.
10132{_}5100{_}"Miss Delafield," went on Paul, "admires our country as much as you do."
10132{_}5101{_}"I was just telling mademoiselle," said Maggie, speaking French with an honest English accent.
10132{_}5102{_}Paul nodded, and left them together.
10132{_}5103{_}"Yes," the countess was saying at the other end of the gloomy room; "yes, we are greatly attached to Thors: Catrina, perhaps, more than I. I have some happy associations, and many sorrowful ones.
10132{_}5104{_}But then--mon Dieu!--how isolated we are!"
10132{_}5105{_}"It is rather far from--anywhere," acceded Etta, who was not attending, although she appeared to be interested.
10132{_}5106{_}"Far!
10132{_}5107{_}Princess, I often wonder how Paris and Thors can be in the same world!
10132{_}5108{_}Before our--our troubles we used to live in Paris a portion of the year.
10132{_}5109{_}At least I did, while my poor husband travelled about.
10132{_}5110{_}He had a hobby, you know, poor man!
10132{_}5111{_}Humanity was his hobby.
10132{_}5112{_}I have always found that men who seek to do good to their fellows are never thanked.
10132{_}5113{_}Have you noticed that?
10132{_}5114{_}The human race is not grateful en gros.
10132{_}5115{_}There is a little gratitude in the individual, but none in the race."
10132{_}5116{_}"None," answered Etta absently.
10132{_}5117{_}"It was so with the Charity League," went on the countess volubly.
10132{_}5118{_}She paused and looked round with her feeble eyes.
10132{_}5119{_}"We are all friends," she went on; "so it is safe to mention the Charity League, is it not?"
10132{_}5120{_}"No," answered Steinmetz from the fire-place; "no, madame.
10132{_}5121{_}There is only one friend to whom you may safely mention that."
10132{_}5122{_}"Ah!
10132{_}5123{_}Bad example!"
10132{_}5124{_}exclaimed the countess playfully.
10132{_}5125{_}"You are there!
10132{_}5126{_}I did not see you enter.
10132{_}5127{_}And who is that friend?"
10132{_}5128{_}"The fair lady who looks at you from your mirror," replied Steinmetz, with a face of stone.
10132{_}5129{_}The countess laughed and shook her cap to one side.
10132{_}5130{_}"Well," she said, "I can do no harm in talking of such things, as I know nothing of them.
10132{_}5131{_}My poor husband--my poor mistaken Stepan--placed no confidence in his wife.
10132{_}5132{_}And now he is in Siberia.
10132{_}5133{_}I believe he works in a bootmaker's shop.
10132{_}5134{_}I pity the people who wear the boots; but perhaps he only puts in the laces.
10132{_}5135{_}You hear, Paul?
10132{_}5136{_}He placed no confidence in his wife, and now he is in Siberia.
10132{_}5137{_}Let that be a warning to you--eh, princess?
10132{_}5138{_}I hope he tells you everything."
10132{_}5139{_}"Put not your trust in princesses," said Steinmetz from the hearth-rug, where he was still warming his hands, for he had driven Maggie over.
10132{_}5140{_}"It says so in the Bible."
10132{_}5141{_}"Princes, profane one!"
10132{_}5142{_}exclaimed the countess with a laugh--"princes, not princesses!"
10132{_}5143{_}"It may be so.
10132{_}5144{_}I bow to your superior literary attainments," replied Steinmetz, looking casually and significantly at a pile of yellow-backed foreign novels on a side-table.
10132{_}5145{_}"No," the countess went on, addressing her conversation to Etta; "no, my husband--figure to yourself, princess--told me nothing.
10132{_}5146{_}I never knew that he was implicated in this great scheme.
10132{_}5147{_}I do not know now who else was concerned in it.
10132{_}5148{_}It was all so sudden, so unexpected, so terrible.
10132{_}5149{_}It appears that he kept the papers in this very house--in that room through there.
10132{_}5150{_}It was his study--"  "My dear countess, silence!"
10132{_}5151{_}interrupted Steinmetz at this moment, breaking into the conversation in his masterful way and enabling Etta to get away.
10132{_}5152{_}Catrina, at the other end of the room, was listening, hard-eyed, breathless.
10132{_}5153{_}It was the sight of Catrina's face that made Steinmetz go forward.
10132{_}5154{_}He had not been looking at Catrina, but at Etta, who was perfect in her composure and steady self-control.
10132{_}5155{_}"Do you want to enter the boot trade also?"
10132{_}5156{_}asked Steinmetz cheerfully, in a lowered voice.
10132{_}5157{_}"Heaven forbid!"
10132{_}5158{_}cried the countess.
10132{_}5159{_}"Then let us talk of safer things."
10132{_}5160{_}The short twilight was already brooding over the land.
10132{_}5161{_}The room, lighted only by small square windows, grew darker and darker until Catrina rang for lamps.
10132{_}5162{_}"I hate a dark room," she said shortly to Maggie.
10132{_}5163{_}When De Chauxville came in, a few minutes later, Catrina was at the piano.
10132{_}5164{_}The room was brilliantly lighted, and on the table gleamed and glittered the silver tea-things.
10132{_}5165{_}The intermediate meal had been disposed of, but the samovar had been left alight, as is the habit at Russian afternoon teas.
10132{_}5166{_}Catrina looked up when the Frenchman entered, but did not cease playing.
10132{_}5167{_}"There is no need for introductions, I think," said the countess.
10132{_}5168{_}"We all know M. de Chauxville," replied Paul quietly, and the two men exchanged a glance.
10132{_}5169{_}De Chauxville shook hands with the new-comers, and, while the countess prepared tea for him, launched into a long description of the preparations for the bear-hunt of the following day.
10132{_}5170{_}He addressed his remarks exclusively to Paul, as between enthusiasts and fellow-sportsmen.
10132{_}5171{_}Gradually Paul thawed a little, and made one or two suggestions which betrayed a deep knowledge and a dawning interest.
10132{_}5172{_}"We shall only be three rifles," said De Chauxville, "Steinmetz, you, and I; and I must ask you to bear in mind the fact that I am no shot--a mere amateur, my dear prince.
10132{_}5173{_}The countess has been good enough to leave the whole matter in my hands.
10132{_}5174{_}I have seen the keepers, and I have arranged that they come to-night at eleven o'clock to see us and to report progress.
10132{_}5175{_}They know of three bears, and are attempting to ring them."
10132{_}5176{_}The Frenchman was really full of information and enthusiasm.
10132{_}5177{_}There were many details upon which he required Paul's advice, and the two men talked together with less constraint than they had hitherto done.
10132{_}5178{_}De Chauxville had picked up a vast deal of technical matter, and handled his little knowledge with a skill which bade fair to deprive it of its proverbial danger.
10132{_}5179{_}He presently left Steinmetz and the prince engaged in a controversy with the countess as to a meeting-place at the luncheon-hour.
10132{_}5180{_}Maggie and Catrina were at the piano.
10132{_}5181{_}Etta was looking at a book of photographs.
10132{_}5182{_}"A charming house, princess," said De Chauxville, in a voice that all could hear while the music happened to be soft.
10132{_}5183{_}But Catrina's music was more remarkable for strength than for softness.
10132{_}5184{_}"Charming," replied Etta.
10132{_}5185{_}The music rose into a swelling burst of harmonious chords.
10132{_}5186{_}"I must see you, princess," said De Chauxville.
10132{_}5187{_}Etta glanced across the room toward her husband and Steinmetz.
10132{_}5188{_}"Alone," added the Frenchman coolly.
10132{_}5189{_}Etta turned a page of the album and looked critically into a photograph.
10132{_}5190{_}"Must!"
10132{_}5191{_}she said, with a little frown.
10132{_}5192{_}"Must!"
10132{_}5193{_}repeated De Chauxville.
10132{_}5194{_}"A word I do not care about," said Etta, with raised eyebrows.
10132{_}5195{_}The music was soft again.
10132{_}5196{_}"It is ten years since I held a rifle," said De Chauxville.
10132{_}5197{_}"Ah, madame, you do not know the excitement.
10132{_}5198{_}I pity ladies, for they have no sport--no big game."
10132{_}5199{_}"Personally, monsieur," answered Etta, with a bright laugh, "I do not grudge you your big game.
10132{_}5200{_}Suppose you miss the bear, or whatever it may be?"
10132{_}5201{_}"Then," said De Chauxville, with a brave shrug of the shoulders, "it is the turn of the bear.
10132{_}5202{_}The excitement is his--the laugh is with him."
10132{_}5203{_}Catrina's foot was upon the loud pedal again.
10132{_}5204{_}"Nevertheless, madame," said De Chauxville, "I make so bold as to use the word.
10132{_}5205{_}You perhaps know me well enough to be aware that I am rarely bold unless my ground is sure."
10132{_}5206{_}"I should not boast of it," answered Etta; "there is nothing to be proud of.
10132{_}5207{_}It is easy enough to be bold if you are certain of victory."
10132{_}5208{_}"When defeat would be intolerable, even a certain victory requires care!
10132{_}5209{_}And I cannot afford to lose."
10132{_}5210{_}"Lose what?"
10132{_}5211{_}enquired Etta.
10132{_}5212{_}De Chauxville looked at her, but he did not answer.
10132{_}5213{_}The music was soft again.
10132{_}5214{_}"I suppose that at Osterno you set no value upon a bear-skin," he said after a pause.
10132{_}5215{_}"We have many," admitted Etta.
10132{_}5216{_}"But I love fur, or trophies of any description.
10132{_}5217{_}Paul has killed a great deal."
10132{_}5218{_}"Ah!"
10132{_}5219{_}"Yes," answered Etta, and the music rose again.
10132{_}5220{_}"I should like to know," she went on, "upon what assumption you make use of a word which does not often--annoy me."
10132{_}5221{_}"I have a good memory, madame.
10132{_}5222{_}Besides," he paused, looking round the room, "there are associations within these walls which stimulate the memory."
10132{_}5223{_}"What do you mean?"
10132{_}5224{_}asked Etta, in a hard voice.
10132{_}5225{_}The hand holding the album suddenly shook like a leaf in the wind.
10132{_}5226{_}De Chauxville had stood upright, his hand at his mustache, after the manner of a man whose small-talk is exhausted.
10132{_}5227{_}It would appear that he was wondering how he could gracefully get away from the princess to pay his devoirs elsewhere.
10132{_}5228{_}"I cannot tell you now," he answered; "Catrina is watching us across the piano.
10132{_}5229{_}You must beware, madame, of those cold blue eyes."
10132{_}5230{_}He moved away, going toward the piano, where Maggie was standing behind Catrina's chair.
10132{_}5231{_}He was like a woman, inasmuch as he could not keep away from his failures.
10132{_}5232{_}"Are you advanced, Miss Delafield?"
10132{_}5233{_}he asked, with his deferential little bow.
10132{_}5234{_}"Are you modern?"
10132{_}5235{_}"I am neither; I have no desire for even the cheapest form of notoriety.
10132{_}5236{_}Why do you ask?"
10132{_}5237{_}replied Maggie.
10132{_}5238{_}"I was merely wondering whether we were to count you among our rifles to-morrow.
10132{_}5239{_}One never knows what ladies will do next; not ladies--I apologize--women.
10132{_}5240{_}I suppose it is those who are not by birth ladies who aspire to the proud name of women.
10132{_}5241{_}The modern Woman--with a capital W--is not a lady--n'est ce pas?"
10132{_}5242{_}"She does not mind your abuse, monsieur," laughed Maggie.
10132{_}5243{_}"So long as you do not ignore her, she is happy.
10132{_}5244{_}But you may set your mind at rest as regards to-morrow.
10132{_}5245{_}I have never let off a gun in my life, and I am sensible enough not to begin on bears."
10132{_}5246{_}De Chauxville made a suitable reply, and remained by the piano talking to the two young ladies until Etta rose and came toward them.
10132{_}5247{_}He then crossed to the other side of the room and engaged Paul in the discussion of further plans for the morrow.
10132{_}5248{_}It was soon time to dress for dinner, and Etta was forced to forego the opportunity she sought to exchange a word alone with De Chauxville.
10132{_}5249{_}That astute gentleman carefully avoided allowing her this opportunity.
10132{_}5250{_}He knew the value of a little suspense.
10132{_}5251{_}During dinner and afterward, when at length the gentlemen came to the drawing-room, the conversation was of a sporting tendency.
10132{_}5252{_}Bears, bear-hunting, and bear stories held supreme sway.
10132{_}5253{_}More than once De Chauxvilie returned to this subject.
10132{_}5254{_}Twice he avoided Etta.
10132{_}5255{_}In some ways this man was courageous.
10132{_}5256{_}He delayed giving Etta her opportunity until there was a question of retiring to bed in view of the early start required by the next day's arrangements.
10132{_}5257{_}It had been finally settled that the three younger ladies should drive over to a woodman's cottage at the far end of the forest, where luncheon was to be served.
10132{_}5258{_}While this item of the programme was arranged De Chauxville looked straight at Etta across the table.
10132{_}5259{_}At length she had the chance afforded to her, deliberately, by De Chauxville.
10132{_}5260{_}"What did you mean?"
10132{_}5261{_}she asked at once.
10132{_}5262{_}"I have received information which, had I known it three months ago, would have made a difference in your life."
10132{_}5263{_}"What difference?"
10132{_}5264{_}"I should have been your husband, instead of that thick-headed giant."
10132{_}5265{_}Etta laughed, but her lips were for the moment colorless.
10132{_}5266{_}"When am I to see you alone?"
10132{_}5267{_}Etta shrugged her shoulders.
10132{_}5268{_}She had plenty of spirit.
10132{_}5269{_}"Please do not be dramatic or mysterious; I am tired.
10132{_}5270{_}Good-night."
10132{_}5271{_}She rose and concealed a simulated yawn.
10132{_}5272{_}De Chauxville looked at her with his sinister smile, and Etta suddenly saw the resemblance which Paul had noted between this man and the grinning mask of the lynx in the smoking-room at Osterno.
10132{_}5273{_}"When?"
10132{_}5274{_}repeated he.
10132{_}5275{_}Etta shrugged her shoulders.
10132{_}5276{_}"I wish to speak to you about the Charity League," said De Chauxville.
10132{_}5277{_}Etta's eyes dilated.
10132{_}5278{_}She made a step or two away from him, but she came back.
10132{_}5279{_}"I shall not go to the luncheon to-morrow, if you care to leave the hunt early."
10132{_}5280{_}De Chauxville bowed.
10132{_}5281{_}CHAPTER XXIX   ANGLO-RUSSIAN  At bedtime Catrina went to Maggie's room with her to see that she had all that she could desire.
10132{_}5282{_}A wood fire was burning brightly in the open French stove; the room was lighted by lamps.
10132{_}5283{_}It was warm and cheery.
10132{_}5284{_}A second door led to the little music-room which Catrina had made her own, and beyond was her bedroom.
10132{_}5285{_}Maggie had assured her hostess that she had every thing that she could wish, and that she did not desire the services of Catrina's maid.
10132{_}5286{_}But the Russian girl still lingered.
10132{_}5287{_}She was slow to make friends--not shy, but diffident and suspicious.
10132{_}5288{_}Her friendship once secured was a thing worth possessing.
10132{_}5289{_}She was inclined to bestow it upon this quiet, self-contained English girl.
10132{_}5290{_}In such matters the length of an acquaintance goes for nothing.
10132{_}5291{_}A long acquaintanceship does not necessarily mean friendship--one being the result of circumstance, the other of selection.
10132{_}5292{_}"The princess knows Russian?"
10132{_}5293{_}said Catrina suddenly.
10132{_}5294{_}She was standing near the dressing-table, where she had been absently attending to the candles.
10132{_}5295{_}She wheeled round and looked at Maggie, who was hospitably sitting on a low chair near the fire.
10132{_}5296{_}She was sorry for the loneliness of this girl's life.
10132{_}5297{_}She did not want her to go away just yet.
10132{_}5298{_}There was another chair by the fire, inviting Catrina to indulge in those maiden confidences which attach themselves to slippers and hair-brushings.
10132{_}5299{_}Maggie looked up with a smile which slowly ebbed away.
10132{_}5300{_}Catrina's remark was of the nature of a defiance.
10132{_}5301{_}Her half-diffident role of hostess was suddenly laid aside.
10132{_}5302{_}"No; she does not," answered the English girl.
10132{_}5303{_}Catrina came forward, standing over Maggie, looking down at her with eyes full of antagonism.
10132{_}5304{_}"Excuse me.
10132{_}5305{_}I saw her understand a remark I made to one of the servants.
10132{_}5306{_}She was not careful.
10132{_}5307{_}I saw it distinctly."
10132{_}5308{_}"I think you must be mistaken," answered Maggie quietly.
10132{_}5309{_}"She has been in Russia before for a few weeks; but she did not learn the language.
10132{_}5310{_}She told me so herself.
10132{_}5311{_}Why should she pretend not to know Russian, if she does?"
10132{_}5312{_}Catrina made no answer.
10132{_}5313{_}She sat heavily down in the vacant chair.
10132{_}5314{_}Her attitudes were uncouth and strong--a perpetual source of tribulation to the countess.
10132{_}5315{_}She sat with her elbow on her knee, staring into the fire.
10132{_}5316{_}"I did not mean to hate her; I did not want to," she said.
10132{_}5317{_}"If it had been you, I should not have hated you."
10132{_}5318{_}Maggie's clear eyes wavered for a moment.
10132{_}5319{_}A faint color rose to her face.
10132{_}5320{_}She leaned back so that the firelight did not reach her.
10132{_}5321{_}There was a silence, during which Maggie unclasped a bracelet with a little snap of the spring.
10132{_}5322{_}Catrina did not hear the sound.
10132{_}5323{_}She heard nothing.
10132{_}5324{_}She did not appear to be aware of her surroundings.
10132{_}5325{_}Maggie unclasped another bracelet noisily.
10132{_}5326{_}She was probably regretting her former kindness of manner.
10132{_}5327{_}Catrina had come too near.
10132{_}5328{_}"Are you not judging rather hastily?"
10132{_}5329{_}suggested Maggie, in a measured voice which heightened the contrast between the two.
10132{_}5330{_}"I find it takes some time to discover whether one likes or dislikes new acquaintances."
10132{_}5331{_}"Yes; but you English are so cold and deliberate.
10132{_}5332{_}You do not know what it is to hate--or to care."
10132{_}5333{_}"Perhaps we do," said Maggie; "but we say less about it."
10132{_}5334{_}Catrina turned and looked at her with a queer smile.
10132{_}5335{_}"Less!"
10132{_}5336{_}she laughed.
10132{_}5337{_}"Nothing--you say nothing.
10132{_}5338{_}Paul is the same.
10132{_}5339{_}I have seen.
10132{_}5340{_}I know.
10132{_}5341{_}You have said nothing since you came to Thors.
10132{_}5342{_}You have talked and laughed; you have given opinions; you have spoken of many things, but you have said nothing.
10132{_}5343{_}You are the same as Paul--one never knows.
10132{_}5344{_}I know nothing about you.
10132{_}5345{_}But I like you.
10132{_}5346{_}You are her cousin?"
10132{_}5347{_}"Yes."
10132{_}5348{_}"And I hate her!"
10132{_}5349{_}Maggie laughed.
10132{_}5350{_}She was quite steady and loyal.
10132{_}5351{_}"When you get to know her you will change, perhaps," she said.
10132{_}5352{_}"Perhaps I know her now better than you do!"
10132{_}5353{_}Maggie laughed in her cheery, practical way.
