10132{_}7366{_}We can only feel to a certain extent, only suffer up to a certain point.
10132{_}7367{_}"We must dress for dinner," said Steinmetz.
10132{_}7368{_}"Afterward--well, afterward we shall see."
10132{_}7369{_}"Yes," answered Paul.
10132{_}7370{_}And he did not go.
10132{_}7371{_}The two men stood looking at each other for a moment.
10132{_}7372{_}They had passed through much together--danger, excitement, and now they were dabbling in sorrow.
10132{_}7373{_}It would appear that this same sorrow runs like a river across the road of our life.
10132{_}7374{_}Some of us find the ford and plash through the shallows--shallow ourselves--while others flounder into deep water.
10132{_}7375{_}These are they who look right on to the greater events, and fail to note the trivial details of each little step.
10132{_}7376{_}Paul was wading through the deep water, and this good friend of his was not inclined to stand upon the bank.
10132{_}7377{_}It is while passing through this river that Fortune sends some of us a friend, who is ever afterward different from all others.
10132{_}7378{_}Paul stood looking down at the broad, heavy face of the man who loved him like a father.
10132{_}7379{_}It was not easy for him to speak.
10132{_}7380{_}He seemed to be making an effort.
10132{_}7381{_}"I do not want you to think," he said at last, "that it is as bad as it might have been.
10132{_}7382{_}It might have been worse--much worse--had I not made a mistake in regard to my own feelings when I married her.
10132{_}7383{_}I will try and do the right thing by her.
10132{_}7384{_}Only at present there does not seem to be much left, except you."
10132{_}7385{_}Steinmetz looked up with his quaintly resigned smile.
10132{_}7386{_}"Ah, yes," he said, "I am there always."
10132{_}7387{_}CHAPTER XXXIX   HUSBAND AND WIFE  Karl Steinmetz had shown the depth of his knowledge of men and women when he commented on that power of facing danger with an unruffled countenance which he was pleased to attribute to English ladies above all women.
10132{_}7388{_}During the evening he had full opportunity of verifying his own observations.
10132{_}7389{_}Etta came down to dinner smiling and imperturbable.
10132{_}7390{_}On the threshold of the drawing-room she exchanged a glance with Karl Steinmetz; and that was all.
10132{_}7391{_}At dinner it was Maggie and Paul who were silent.
10132{_}7392{_}Etta talked to Steinmetz--brightly, gayly, with a certain courage of a very high order; for she was desperate, and she did not show it.
10132{_}7393{_}At last the evening came to an end.
10132{_}7394{_}Maggie had sung two songs.
10132{_}7395{_}Steinmetz had performed on the piano with a marvellous touch.
10132{_}7396{_}All had played their parts with the brazen faces which Steinmetz, in his knowledge of many nations, assigned to the Anglo-Saxon race before others.
10132{_}7397{_}At last Etta rose to go to bed, with a little sharp sigh of great suspense.
10132{_}7398{_}It was coming.
10132{_}7399{_}She went up to her room, bidding Maggie good-night in the passage.
10132{_}7400{_}In a mechanical way she allowed the deft-handed maid to array her in a dressing gown--soft, silken, a dainty triumph in its way.
10132{_}7401{_}Then, almost impatiently, she sent the maid away when her hair was only half released.
10132{_}7402{_}She would brush it herself.
10132{_}7403{_}She was tired.
10132{_}7404{_}No, she wanted nothing more.
10132{_}7405{_}She sat down by the fire, brush in hand.
10132{_}7406{_}She could hardly breathe.
10132{_}7407{_}It was coming.
10132{_}7408{_}She heard Paul come to his dressing-room.
10132{_}7409{_}She heard his deep, quiet voice reply to some question of his valet's.
10132{_}7410{_}Then the word "Good-night" in the same quiet voice.
10132{_}7411{_}The valet had gone.
10132{_}7412{_}There was only the door now between her and--what?
10132{_}7413{_}Her fingers were at the throat of her dressing-gown.
10132{_}7414{_}The soft lace seemed to choke her.
10132{_}7415{_}Then Paul knocked at the door.
10132{_}7416{_}It was coming.
10132{_}7417{_}She opened her lips, but at first could make no sound.
10132{_}7418{_}"Come in!"
10132{_}7419{_}she said at length hoarsely.
10132{_}7420{_}She wondered whether he would kill her.
10132{_}7421{_}She wondered whether she was in love with her husband.
10132{_}7422{_}She had begun wondering that lately; she was wondering it when he came in.
10132{_}7423{_}He had changed his dress-coat for a silk-faced jacket, in which he was in the habit of working with Steinmetz in the quiet room after the household had gone to bed.
10132{_}7424{_}She looked up.
10132{_}7425{_}She dropped the brush, and ran toward him with a great rustle of her flowing silks.
10132{_}7426{_}"Oh, Paul, what is it?"
10132{_}7427{_}she cried.
10132{_}7428{_}She stopped short, not daring to touch him, before his cold, set face.
10132{_}7429{_}"Have you seen any one?"
10132{_}7430{_}she whispered.
10132{_}7431{_}"Only De Chauxville," he answered, "this afternoon."
10132{_}7432{_}"Indeed, Paul," she protested hastily, "it was nothing.
10132{_}7433{_}A message from Catrina Lanovitch.
10132{_}7434{_}It was only the usual visit of an acquaintance.
10132{_}7435{_}It would have been very strange if he had not called.
10132{_}7436{_}Do you think I could care for a man like that?"
10132{_}7437{_}"I never did think so until now," returned Paul steadily.
10132{_}7438{_}"Your excuses accuse you.
10132{_}7439{_}You may care for him.
10132{_}7440{_}I do not know; I--do--not--care."
10132{_}7441{_}She turned slowly and went back to her chair.
10132{_}7442{_}Mechanically she took up the brush, and shook back her beautiful hair.
10132{_}7443{_}"You mean you do not care for me," she said.
10132{_}7444{_}"Oh, Paul!
10132{_}7445{_}be careful."
10132{_}7446{_}Paul stood looking at her.
10132{_}7447{_}He was not a subtle-minded man at all.
10132{_}7448{_}He was not one of those who take it upon themselves to say that they understand women--using the word in an offensively general sense, as if women were situated midway between the human and the animal races.
10132{_}7449{_}He was old-fashioned enough to look upon women as higher and purer than men, while equally capable of thought and self-control.
10132{_}7450{_}He had, it must be remembered, no great taste for fictional literature.
10132{_}7451{_}He had not read the voluminous lucubrations of the modern woman writer.
10132{_}7452{_}He had not assisted at the nauseating spectacle of a woman morally turning herself inside out in three volumes and an interview.
10132{_}7453{_}No, this man respected women still; and he paid them an honor which, thank Heaven, most of them still deserve.
10132{_}7454{_}He treated them as men in the sense that he considered them to be under the same code of right and wrong, of good and evil.
10132{_}7455{_}He did not understand what Etta meant when she told him to be careful.
10132{_}7456{_}He did not know that the modern social code is like the Spanish grammar--there are so many exceptions that the rules are hardly worth noting.
10132{_}7457{_}And one of our most notorious modern exceptions is the married woman who is pleased to hold herself excused because outsiders tell her that her husband does not understand her.
10132{_}7458{_}"I do not think," said Paul judicially, "that you can have cared very much whether I loved you or not.
10132{_}7459{_}When you married me you knew that I was the promoter of the Charity League; I almost told you.
10132{_}7460{_}I told you so much that, with your knowledge, you must have been aware of the fact that I was heavily interested in the undertaking which you betrayed.
10132{_}7461{_}You married me without certain proof of your husband's death, such was your indecent haste to call yourself a princess.
10132{_}7462{_}And now I find, on your own confession, that you have a clandestine understanding with a man who tried to murder me only a week ago.
10132{_}7463{_}Is it not rather absurd to talk of caring?"
10132{_}7464{_}He stood looking down at her, cold and terrible in the white heat of his suppressed Northern anger.
10132{_}7465{_}The little clock on the mantel-piece, in a terrible hurry, ticked with all its might.
10132{_}7466{_}Time was speeding.
10132{_}7467{_}Every moment was against her.
10132{_}7468{_}And she could think of nothing to say simply because those things that she would have said to others would carry no weight with this man.
10132{_}7469{_}Etta was leaning forward in the luxurious chair, staring with haggard eyes into the fire.
10132{_}7470{_}The flames leaped up and gleamed on her pale face, in her deep eyes.
10132{_}7471{_}"I suppose," she said, without looking at him, "that you will not believe me when I tell you that I hate the man.
10132{_}7472{_}I knew nothing of what you refer to as happening last week; his attempt to murder you, I mean.
10132{_}7473{_}You are a prince, and all-powerful in your own province.
10132{_}7474{_}Can you not throw him into prison and keep him there?
10132{_}7475{_}Such things are done in Russia.
10132{_}7476{_}He is more dangerous than you think.
10132{_}7477{_}Please do it--please--"  Paul looked at her with hard, unresponsive eyes.
10132{_}7478{_}Lives depended on his answer.
10132{_}7479{_}"I did not come here to discuss Claude de Chauxville," he said, "but you, and our future."
10132{_}7480{_}Etta drew herself up as one under the lash, and waited with set teeth.
10132{_}7481{_}"I propose," he said, in a final voice which made it no proposition at all, "that you go home to England at once with--your cousin.
10132{_}7482{_}This country is not safe for you.
10132{_}7483{_}The house in London will be at your disposal.
10132{_}7484{_}I will make a suitable settlement on you, sufficient to live in accordance with your title and position.
10132{_}7485{_}I must ask you to remember that the name you bear has hitherto been an unsullied one.
10132{_}7486{_}We have been proud of our princesses--up to now.
10132{_}7487{_}In case of any trouble reaching you from outside sources connected with this country, I should like you to remember that you are under my protection and that of Steinmetz.
10132{_}7488{_}Either of us will be glad at any time to consider any appeal for assistance that you may think fit to make.
10132{_}7489{_}You will always be the Princess Howard Alexis."
10132{_}7490{_}Etta gave a sudden laugh.
10132{_}7491{_}"Oh, yes," she said, and her face was strangely red, "I shall still be the Princess Alexis."
10132{_}7492{_}"With sufficient money to keep up the position," he went on, with the cruel irony of a slow-spoken man.
10132{_}7493{_}A queer, twisted smile passed across Etta's face--the smile of one who is in agony and will not shriek.
10132{_}7494{_}"There are certain stipulations which I must make in self-defence," went on Paul.
10132{_}7495{_}"I must ask you to cease all communication of whatever nature with the Baron de Chauxville.
10132{_}7496{_}I am not jealous of him--now.
10132{_}7497{_}I do not know why."
10132{_}7498{_}He paused, as if wondering what the meaning of this might be.
10132{_}7499{_}Etta knew it.
10132{_}7500{_}The knowledge was part of her punishment.
10132{_}7501{_}"But," continued her husband.
10132{_}7502{_}"I am not going to sacrifice the name my mother bore to the vanity of a French coxcomb.
10132{_}7503{_}You will be kind enough to avoid all society where it is likely that you should meet him.
10132{_}7504{_}If you disregard my desires in this matter, I shall be compelled to take means to enforce them."
10132{_}7505{_}"What means?"
10132{_}7506{_}"I shall reduce your allowance."
10132{_}7507{_}Their eyes met, and perhaps that was the bitterest moment in Etta's life.
10132{_}7508{_}Dead things are better put out of sight at once.
10132{_}7509{_}Etta felt that Paul's dead love would grin at her in every sovereign of the allowance which was to be hers.
10132{_}7510{_}She would never get away from it; she could never shake off its memory.
10132{_}7511{_}"Am I to live alone?"
10132{_}7512{_}asked Etta, suddenly finding her voice.
10132{_}7513{_}"That is as you like," answered Paul, perhaps purposely misunderstanding her.
10132{_}7514{_}"You are at liberty to have any friend or companion you wish.
10132{_}7515{_}Perhaps--your cousin."
10132{_}7516{_}"Maggie?"
10132{_}7517{_}"Yes," answered Paul.
10132{_}7518{_}For the first time since he had entered the room his eyes were averted from Etta's face.
10132{_}7519{_}"She would not live with me," said the princess curtly.
10132{_}7520{_}Paul seemed to be reflecting.
10132{_}7521{_}When he next spoke it was in a kinder voice.
10132{_}7522{_}"You need not tell the circumstances which have given rise to this arrangement."
10132{_}7523{_}Etta shrugged her shoulders.
10132{_}7524{_}"That," went on Paul, "rests entirely with yourself.
10132{_}7525{_}You may be sure that I will tell no one.
10132{_}7526{_}I am not likely to discuss it with any one whomsoever."
10132{_}7527{_}Etta's stony eyes softened for a moment.
10132{_}7528{_}She seemed to be alternating between hatred of this man and love of him--a dangerous state for any woman.
10132{_}7529{_}It is possible that, if he had held his hand out to her, she would have been at his feet in a wild, incoherent passion of self-hatred and abasement.
10132{_}7530{_}Such moments as these turn our lives and determine them.
10132{_}7531{_}Paul knew nothing of the issue hanging on this moment, on the passing softness of her eyes.
10132{_}7532{_}He knew nothing of the danger in which this woman stood, of the temptation with which she was wrestling.
10132{_}7533{_}He went on in his blindness, went on being only just.
10132{_}7534{_}"If," he said, "you have any further questions to ask, I shall always be at your service.
10132{_}7535{_}For the next few days I shall be busy.
10132{_}7536{_}The peasants are in a state of discontent verging on rebellion.
10132{_}7537{_}We cannot at present arrange for your journey to Tver, but as soon as it is possible I will tell you."
10132{_}7538{_}He looked at the clock, and made an imperceptible movement toward the door.
10132{_}7539{_}Etta glanced up sharply.
10132{_}7540{_}She did not seem to be breathing.
10132{_}7541{_}"Is that all?"
10132{_}7542{_}she asked, in a dull voice.
10132{_}7543{_}There was a long silence, tense and throbbing, the great silence of the steppe.
10132{_}7544{_}"I think so," answered Paul at length.
10132{_}7545{_}"I have tried to be just."
10132{_}7546{_}"Then justice is very cruel."
10132{_}7547{_}"Not so cruel as the woman who for a few pounds sells the happiness of thousands of human beings.
10132{_}7548{_}Steinmetz advised me to speak to you.
10132{_}7549{_}He suggested the possibility of circumstances of which we are ignorant.
10132{_}7550{_}He said that you might be able to explain."
10132{_}7551{_}Silence.
10132{_}7552{_}"Can you explain?"
10132{_}7553{_}Silence.
10132{_}7554{_}Etta sat looking into the fire.
10132{_}7555{_}The little clock hurried on.
10132{_}7556{_}At length Etta drew a deep breath.
10132{_}7557{_}"You are the sort of man," she said, "who does not understand temptation.
10132{_}7558{_}You are strong.
10132{_}7559{_}The devil leaves the strong in peace.
10132{_}7560{_}You have found virtue easy because you have never wanted money.
10132{_}7561{_}Your position has always been assured.
10132{_}7562{_}Your name alone is a password through the world.
10132{_}7563{_}Your sort are always hard on women who--who--What have I done, after all?"
10132{_}7564{_}Some instinct bade her rise to her feet and stand before him--tall, beautiful, passionate, a woman in a thousand, a fit mate for such as he.
10132{_}7565{_}Her beautiful hair in burnished glory round her face gleamed in the firelight.
10132{_}7566{_}Her white fingers clenched, her arms thrown back, her breast panting beneath the lace, her proud face looking defiance into his--no one but a prince could have braved this princess.
10132{_}7567{_}"What have I done?"
10132{_}7568{_}she cried a second time.
10132{_}7569{_}"I have only fought for myself, and if I have won, so much the greater credit.
10132{_}7570{_}I am your wife.
10132{_}7571{_}I have done nothing the law can touch.
10132{_}7572{_}Thousands of women moving in our circle are not half so good as I am.
10132{_}7573{_}I swear before God I am----"  "Hush!"
10132{_}7574{_}he said, with upraised hand.
10132{_}7575{_}"I never doubted that."
10132{_}7576{_}"I will do any thing you wish," she went on, and in her humility she was very dangerous.
10132{_}7577{_}"I deceived you, I know.
10132{_}7578{_}But I sold the Charity League before I knew that you--that you thought of me.
10132{_}7579{_}When I married you I didn't love you.
10132{_}7580{_}I admit that.
10132{_}7581{_}But Paul--oh, Paul, if you were not so good you would understand."
10132{_}7582{_}Perhaps he did understand; for there was that in her eyes that made her meaning clear.
10132{_}7583{_}He was silent; standing before her in his great strength, his marvellous and cruel self-restraint.
10132{_}7584{_}"You will not forgive me?"
10132{_}7585{_}For a moment she leaned forward, peering into his face.
10132{_}7586{_}He seemed to be reflecting.
10132{_}7587{_}"Yes," he said at length, "I forgive you.
10132{_}7588{_}But if I cared for you, forgiveness would be impossible."
10132{_}7589{_}He went slowly toward the door.
10132{_}7590{_}Etta looked round the room with drawn eyes; their room--the room he had fitted up for his bride with the lavishness of a great wealth and a great love.
10132{_}7591{_}He paused, with his hand on the door.
10132{_}7592{_}"And," she said, with fiery cheeks, "does your forgiveness date from to-night?"
10132{_}7593{_}"Yes!"
10132{_}7594{_}He opened the door.
10132{_}7595{_}"Good-night!"
10132{_}7596{_}he said, and went out.
10132{_}7597{_}CHAPTER XL   STEPAN RETURNS  At daybreak the next morning Karl Steinmetz was awakened by the familiar cry of the wolf beneath his window.
10132{_}7598{_}He rose and dressed hastily.
10132{_}7599{_}The eastern sky was faintly pink; a rosy twilight moved among the pines.
10132{_}7600{_}He went down stairs and opened the little door at the back of the castle.
10132{_}7601{_}It was, of course, the starosta, shivering and bleached in the chilly dawn.
10132{_}7602{_}"They have watched my cottage, Excellency, all night.
10132{_}7603{_}It was only now that I could get away.
10132{_}7604{_}There are two strange sleighs outside Domensky's hut.
10132{_}7605{_}There are marks of many sleighs that have been and gone.
10132{_}7606{_}Excellency, it is unsafe for any one to venture outside the castle to-day.
10132{_}7607{_}You must send to Tver for the soldiers."
10132{_}7608{_}"The prince refuses to do that."
10132{_}7609{_}"But why, Excellency?
10132{_}7610{_}We shall be killed!"
10132{_}7611{_}"You do not know the effect of platoon firing on a closely packed mob, starost.
10132{_}7612{_}The prince does," replied Steinmetz, with his grim smile.
10132{_}7613{_}They spoke together in hushed voices for half an hour, while the daylight crept up the eastern sky.
10132{_}7614{_}Then the starosta stole away among the still larches, like the wolf whose cry he imitated so perfectly.
10132{_}7615{_}Steinmetz closed the door and went upstairs to his own room, his face grave and thoughtful, his tread heavy with the weight of anxiety.
10132{_}7616{_}The day passed as such days do.
10132{_}7617{_}Etta was not the woman to plead a conventional headache and remain hidden.
10132{_}7618{_}She came down to breakfast, and during that meal was boldly conversational.
10132{_}7619{_}"She has spirit," reflected Karl Steinmetz behind his quiet gray eyes.
10132{_}7620{_}He admired her for it, and helped her.
10132{_}7621{_}He threw back the ball of conversation with imperturbable good humor.
10132{_}7622{_}They were completely shut in.
10132{_}7623{_}No news from the outer world penetrated to the little party besieged within their own stone walls.
10132{_}7624{_}Maggie, fearless and innocent, announced her intention of snow-shoeing, but was dissuaded therefrom by Steinmetz with covert warnings.
10132{_}7625{_}During the morning each was occupied in individual affairs.
10132{_}7626{_}At luncheon time they met again.
10132{_}7627{_}Etta was now almost defiant.
10132{_}7628{_}She was on her mettle.
10132{_}7629{_}She was so near to loving Paul that a hatred of him welled up within her breast whenever he repelled her advances with uncompromising reticence.
10132{_}7630{_}They did not know--perhaps she hardly knew herself--that the opening of the side-door depended upon her humor.
10132{_}7631{_}In the afternoon Etta and Maggie sat, as was their wont, in the morning-room looking out over the cliff.
10132{_}7632{_}Of late their intercourse had been slightly strained.
10132{_}7633{_}They had never had much in common, although circumstances had thrown their lives together.
10132{_}7634{_}It is one of the ills to which women are heir that they have frequently to pass their whole lives in the society of persons with whom they have no real sympathy.
10132{_}7635{_}Both these women were conscious of the little rift within the lute, but such rifts are better treated with silence.
10132{_}7636{_}That which comes to interfere with a woman's friendship will not often bear discussion.
10132{_}7637{_}At dusk Steinmetz went out.
10132{_}7638{_}He had an appointment with the starosta.
10132{_}7639{_}Paul was sitting in his own room, making a pretence of work, about five o'clock, when Steinmetz came hurriedly to him.
10132{_}7640{_}"A new development," he said shortly.
10132{_}7641{_}"Come to my room."
10132{_}7642{_}Paul rose and followed him through the double doorway built in the thickness of the wall.
10132{_}7643{_}Steinmetz's large room was lighted only by a lamp standing on the table.
10132{_}7644{_}All the light was thrown on the desk by a large green shade, leaving the rest of the room in a semi-darkness.
10132{_}7645{_}At the far end of the room a man was standing in an expectant attitude.
10132{_}7646{_}There was something furtive about this intruder, and at the same time familiar to Paul, who peered at him through the gloom.
10132{_}7647{_}Then the man came hurriedly forward.
10132{_}7648{_}"Ah, Pavlo, Pavlo!"
10132{_}7649{_}he said in a deep, hollow voice.
10132{_}7650{_}"I could not expect you to know me."
10132{_}7651{_}He threw his arms around him, and embraced him after the simple manner of Russia.
10132{_}7652{_}Then he held him at arm's length.
10132{_}7653{_}"Stepan!"
10132{_}7654{_}said Paul.
10132{_}7655{_}"No, I did not know you."
10132{_}7656{_}Stepan Lanovitch was still holding him at arm's length, examining him with the large faint blue eyes which so often go with an exaggerated philanthropy.
10132{_}7657{_}"Old," he muttered, "old!
10132{_}7658{_}Ah, my poor Pavlo!
10132{_}7659{_}I heard in Kiew--you know how we outlaws hear such things--that you were in trouble, so I came to you."
10132{_}7660{_}Steinmetz in the background raised his patient eyebrows.
10132{_}7661{_}"There are two men in the world," went on the voluble Lanovitch, "who can manage the moujiks of Tver--you and I; so I came.
10132{_}7662{_}I will help you, Pavlo; I will stand by you.
10132{_}7663{_}Together we can assuredly quell this revolt."
10132{_}7664{_}Paul nodded, and allowed himself to be embraced a second time.
10132{_}7665{_}He had long known Stepan Lanovitch of Thors as one of the many who go about the world doing good with their eyes shut.
10132{_}7666{_}For the moment he had absolutely no use for this well-meaning blunderer.
10132{_}7667{_}"I am afraid," he said, "that it has got beyond control.
10132{_}7668{_}We cannot stamp it out now except by force, and I would rather not do that.
10132{_}7669{_}Our only hope is that it may burn itself out.
10132{_}7670{_}The talkers must get hoarse in time."
10132{_}7671{_}Lanovitch shook his head.
10132{_}7672{_}"They have been talking since the days of Ananias," he said, "and they are not hoarse yet.
10132{_}7673{_}I fear, Pavlo, there will never be peace in the world until the talkers are hoarse."
10132{_}7674{_}"How did you get here?"
10132{_}7675{_}asked Paul, who was always businesslike.
10132{_}7676{_}"I brought a pack on my back and sold cotton.
10132{_}7677{_}I made myself known to the starosta, and he communicated with good Karl here."
10132{_}7678{_}"Did you learn any thing in the village?"
10132{_}7679{_}asked Paul.
10132{_}7680{_}"No; they suspected me.
10132{_}7681{_}They would not talk.
10132{_}7682{_}But I understand them, Pavlo, these poor simple fools.
10132{_}7683{_}A pebble in the stream would turn the current of their convictions.
10132{_}7684{_}Tell them who is the Moscow doctor.
10132{_}7685{_}It is your only chance."
10132{_}7686{_}Steinmetz grunted acquiescence and walked wearily to the window.
10132{_}7687{_}This was only an old and futile argument of his own.
10132{_}7688{_}"And make it impossible for me to live another day among them," said Paul.
10132{_}7689{_}"Do you think St. Petersburg would countenance a prince who works among his moujiks?"
10132{_}7690{_}Stepan Lanovitch's pale blue eyes looked troubled.
10132{_}7691{_}Steinmetz shrugged his shoulders.
10132{_}7692{_}"They have brought it on themselves," he said.
10132{_}7693{_}"As much as a lamb brings the knife upon itself by growing up," replied Paul.
10132{_}7694{_}Lanovitch shook his white head with a tolerant little smile.
10132{_}7695{_}He loved these poor helpless peasants with a love as large as and a thousand times less practical than Paul's.
10132{_}7696{_}In the meantime Paul was thinking in his clear, direct way.
10132{_}7697{_}It was this man's habit in life and in thought to walk straight past the side issues.
10132{_}7698{_}"It is like you, Stepan," he said at length, "to come to us at this time.
10132{_}7699{_}We feel it, and we recognize the generosity of it, for Steinmetz and I know the danger you are running in coming back to this country.
10132{_}7700{_}But we cannot let you do it--No, do not protest.
10132{_}7701{_}It is quite out of the question.
10132{_}7702{_}We might quell the revolt; no doubt we should--the two of us together.
10132{_}7703{_}But what would happen afterward?
10132{_}7704{_}You would be sent back to Siberia, and I should probably follow you for harboring an escaped convict."
10132{_}7705{_}The face of the impulsive philanthropist dropped pathetically.
10132{_}7706{_}He had come to his friend's assistance on the spur of the moment.
10132{_}7707{_}He was destined, as some men are, to plunge about the world seeking to do good.
10132{_}7708{_}And it has been decreed that good must be done by stealth and after deliberation only.
10132{_}7709{_}He who does good on the spur of the moment usually sows a seed of dissension in the trench of time.
10132{_}7710{_}"Also," went on Paul, with that deliberate grasp of the situation which never failed to astonish the ready-witted Steinmetz; "also, you have other calls upon your energy.
10132{_}7711{_}You have other work to do."
10132{_}7712{_}Lanovitch's broad face lightened up; his benevolent brow beamed.
10132{_}7713{_}His capacity for work had brought him to the shoemaker's last in Tomsk.
10132{_}7714{_}It is a vice that grows with indulgence.
10132{_}7715{_}"It has pleased the Authorities," went on Paul, who was shy of religious turns of phrase, "to give us all our own troubles.
10132{_}7716{_}Mine--such as they are, Stepan--must be managed by myself.
10132{_}7717{_}Yours can be faced by no one but you.
10132{_}7718{_}You have come at the right moment.
10132{_}7719{_}You do not quite realize what your coming means to Catrina."
10132{_}7720{_}"Catrina!
10132{_}7721{_}Ah!"
10132{_}7722{_}The weak blue eyes looked into the strong face and read nothing there.
10132{_}7723{_}"I doubt," said Paul, "whether it is right for you to continue sacrificing Catrina for the sake of the little good that you are able to do.
10132{_}7724{_}You are hampered in your good work to such an extent that the result is very small, while the pain you give is very great."
10132{_}7725{_}"But is that so, Pavlo?
10132{_}7726{_}Is my child unhappy?"
10132{_}7727{_}"I fear so," replied Paul gravely, with his baffling self-restraint.
10132{_}7728{_}"She has not much in common with her mother, you understand."
10132{_}7729{_}"Ah, yes!"
10132{_}7730{_}"It is you to whom she is attached.
10132{_}7731{_}Sometimes it is so with children and parents.
10132{_}7732{_}One cannot tell why."
10132{_}7733{_}Steinmetz looked as if he could supply information upon the subject: but he remained silent, standing, as it were, in an acquiescent attitude.
10132{_}7734{_}"You have fought your fight," said Paul.
10132{_}7735{_}"A good fight, too.
10132{_}7736{_}You have struck your blow for the country.
10132{_}7737{_}You have sown your seed, but the harvest is not yet.
10132{_}7738{_}Now it is time to think of your own safety, of the happiness of your own child."
10132{_}7739{_}Stepan Lanovitch turned away and sat heavily down.
10132{_}7740{_}He leaned his two arms on the table, and his chin upon his clenched hands.
10132{_}7741{_}"Why not leave the country now; at all events for a few years?"
10132{_}7742{_}went on Paul, and when a man who is accustomed to command stoops to persuade, it is strong persuasion that he wields.
10132{_}7743{_}"You can take Catrina with you.
10132{_}7744{_}You will be assuring her happiness, which, at all events, is something tangible--a present harvest!
10132{_}7745{_}I will drive over to Thors now and bring her back.
10132{_}7746{_}You can leave to-night and go to America."
10132{_}7747{_}Stepan Lanovitch raised his head and looked hard into Paul's face.
10132{_}7748{_}"You wish it?"
10132{_}7749{_}"I think," answered Paul steadily, "that it is for Catrina's happiness."
10132{_}7750{_}Then Lanovitch rose up and took Paul's hand in his work-stained grip.
10132{_}7751{_}"Go, my son!
10132{_}7752{_}It will be a great happiness to me.
10132{_}7753{_}I will wait here," he said.
10132{_}7754{_}Paul went straight to the door.
10132{_}7755{_}He was a man with a capacity for prompt action, which seemed to rise to demand.
10132{_}7756{_}Steinmetz followed him out into the passage and took him by the arm.
10132{_}7757{_}"You cannot do it," he said.
10132{_}7758{_}"Yes, I can," replied Paul.
10132{_}7759{_}"I can find my way through the forest.
10132{_}7760{_}No one will venture to follow me there in the dark."
10132{_}7761{_}Steinmetz hesitated, shrugged his shoulders, and went back into the room.
10132{_}7762{_}The ladies at Thors were dressed for dinner--were, indeed, awaiting the announcement of that meal--when Paul broke in upon their solitude.
10132{_}7763{_}He did not pause to lay aside his furs, but went into the long, low room, withdrawing his seal gloves painfully, for it was freezing as it only can freeze in March.
10132{_}7764{_}The countess assailed him with many questions, more or less sensible, which he endured patiently until the servant had left the room.
10132{_}7765{_}Catrina, with flushed cheeks, stood looking at him, but said nothing.
10132{_}7766{_}Paul withdrew his gloves and submitted to the countess' futile tugs at his fur coat.
10132{_}7767{_}Then Catrina spoke.
10132{_}7768{_}"The Baron de Chauxville has left us," she said, without knowing exactly why.
10132{_}7769{_}For the moment Paul had forgotten Claude de Chauxville's existence.
10132{_}7770{_}"I have news for you," he said; and he gently pushed the chattering countess aside.
10132{_}7771{_}"Stepan Lanovitch is at Osterno.
10132{_}7772{_}He arrived to-night."
10132{_}7773{_}"Ah, they have set him free, poor man!
10132{_}7774{_}Does he wear chains on his ankles--is his hair long?
10132{_}7775{_}My poor Stepan!
10132{_}7776{_}Ah, but what a stupid man!"
10132{_}7777{_}The countess collapsed into a soft chair.
10132{_}7778{_}She chose a soft one, obviously.
10132{_}7779{_}It has to be recorded here that she did not receive the news with unmitigated joy.
10132{_}7780{_}"When he was in Siberia," she gasped, "one knew at all events where he was; and now, mon Dieu!
10132{_}7781{_}what an anxiety!"
10132{_}7782{_}"I have come over to see whether you will join him to-night and go with him to America," said Paul, looking at her.
10132{_}7783{_}"To--America--to-night!
10132{_}7784{_}My dear Paul, are you mad?
10132{_}7785{_}One cannot do such things as that.
10132{_}7786{_}America!
10132{_}7787{_}that is across the sea."
10132{_}7788{_}"Yes," answered Paul.
10132{_}7789{_}"And I am such a bad sailor.
10132{_}7790{_}Now, if it had been Paris----"  "But it cannot be," interrupted Paul.
10132{_}7791{_}"Will you join your father to-night?"
10132{_}7792{_}he added, turning to Catrina.
10132{_}7793{_}The girl was looking at him with something in her eyes that he did not care to meet.
10132{_}7794{_}"And go to America?"
10132{_}7795{_}she asked, in a lifeless voice.
10132{_}7796{_}Paul nodded.
10132{_}7797{_}Catrina turned suddenly away from him and walked to the fire, where she stood with her back toward him--a small, uncouth figure in black and green, the lamplight gleaming on her wonderful hair.
10132{_}7798{_}She turned suddenly again, and, coming back, stood looking into his face.
10132{_}7799{_}"I will go," she said.
10132{_}7800{_}"You think it best?"
10132{_}7801{_}"Yes," he answered; "I think it best."
10132{_}7802{_}She drew a sharp breath and was about to speak when the countess interrupted her.
10132{_}7803{_}"What!"
10132{_}7804{_}she cried.
10132{_}7805{_}"You are going away to-night like this, without any luggage!
10132{_}7806{_}And pray what is to become of me?"
10132{_}7807{_}"You can join them in America," said Paul, in his quietest tone.
10132{_}7808{_}"Or you can live in Paris, at last."
10132{_}7809{_}CHAPTER XLI   DUTY  It was not now a very cold night.
10132{_}7810{_}There were fleecy clouds thrown like puffs of smoke against the western sky.
10132{_}7811{_}The moon, on the wane,--a small crescent lying on its back,--was lowering toward the horizon.
10132{_}7812{_}The thermometer had risen since sunset, as it often does in March.
10132{_}7813{_}There was a suggestion of spring in the air.
10132{_}7814{_}It seemed that at last the long winter was drawing to a close; that the iron grip of frost was relaxing.
10132{_}7815{_}Paul went out and inspected the harness by the light of a stable lantern held in the mittened hand of a yemschick.
10132{_}7816{_}He had reasons of his own for absenting himself while Catrina bade her mother farewell.
10132{_}7817{_}He was rather afraid of these women.
10132{_}7818{_}The harness inspected, he began reckoning how many hours of moonlight might still be vouchsafed to him.
10132{_}7819{_}The stableman, seeing the direction of his gaze, began to talk of the weather and the possibilities of snow in the near future.
10132{_}7820{_}They conversed in low voices together.
10132{_}7821{_}Presently the door opened and Catrina came quickly out, followed by a servant carrying a small hand-bag.
10132{_}7822{_}Paul could not see Catrina's face.
10132{_}7823{_}She was veiled and furred to the eyelids.
10132{_}7824{_}Without a word the girl took her seat in the sleigh, and the servant prepared the bear-skin rugs.
10132{_}7825{_}Paul gathered up the reins and took his place beside her.
10132{_}7826{_}A few moments were required to draw up the rugs and fasten them with straps; then Paul gave the word and the horses leaped forward.
10132{_}7827{_}As they sped down the avenue Catrina turned and looked her last on Thors.
10132{_}7828{_}Before long Paul wheeled into the trackless forest.
10132{_}7829{_}He had come very carefully, steering chiefly by the moon and stars, with occasional assistance from a bend of the winding river.
10132{_}7830{_}At times he had taken to the ice, following the course of the stream for a few miles.
10132{_}7831{_}No snow had fallen; it would be easy to return on his own track.
10132{_}7832{_}Through this part of the forest no road was cut.
10132{_}7833{_}For nearly half an hour they drove in silence.
10132{_}7834{_}Only the whistle of the iron-bound runners on the powdery snow, the creak of the warming leather on the horses, the regular breathing of the team, broke the stillness of the forest.
10132{_}7835{_}Paul hoped against hope that Catrina was asleep.
10132{_}7836{_}She sat by his side, her arm touching his sleeve, her weight thrown against him at such times as the sleigh bumped over a fallen tree or some inequality of the ground.
10132{_}7837{_}He could not help wondering what thoughts there were behind her silence.
10132{_}7838{_}Steinmetz's good-natured banter had come back to his memory, during the last few days, in a new light.
10132{_}7839{_}"Paul," said the woman at his side quite suddenly, breaking the silence of the great forest where they had grown to life and sorrow almost side by side.
10132{_}7840{_}"Yes."
10132{_}7841{_}"I want to know how this all came about.
10132{_}7842{_}It is not my father's doing.
10132{_}7843{_}There is something quick, and practical, and wise which suggests you and Herr Steinmetz.
10132{_}7844{_}I suspect that you have done this--you and he--for our happiness."
10132{_}7845{_}"No," answered Paul; "it was mere accident.
10132{_}7846{_}Your father heard of our trouble in Kiew.
10132{_}7847{_}You know him--always impulsive and reckless.
10132{_}7848{_}He never thinks of the danger.
10132{_}7849{_}He came to help us."
10132{_}7850{_}Catrina smiled wanly.
10132{_}7851{_}"But it _is_ for our happiness, is it not, Paul?
10132{_}7852{_}You know that it is--that is why you have done it.
10132{_}7853{_}I have not had time yet to realize what I am doing, all that is going to happen.
10132{_}7854{_}But if it is your doing, I think I shall be content to abide by the result."
10132{_}7855{_}"It is not my doing," replied Paul, who did not like her wistful tone.
10132{_}7856{_}"It is the outcome of circumstances.
10132{_}7857{_}Circumstances have been ruling us all lately.
10132{_}7858{_}We seem to have no time to consider, but only to do that which seems best for the moment."
10132{_}7859{_}"And it is best that I should go to America with my father?"
10132{_}7860{_}Her voice was composed and quiet.
10132{_}7861{_}In the dim light he could not see her white lips; indeed, he never looked.
10132{_}7862{_}"It seems so to me, undoubtedly," he said.
10132{_}7863{_}"In doing this, so far as we can see at present, it seems certain that you are saving your father from Siberia.
10132{_}7864{_}You know what he is; he never thinks of his own safety.
10132{_}7865{_}He ought never to have come here to-night.
10132{_}7866{_}If he remains in Russia, it is an absolute certainty that he will sooner or later be rearrested.
10132{_}7867{_}He is one of those good people who require saving from themselves."
10132{_}7868{_}Catrina nodded.
10132{_}7869{_}At times duty is the kedge-anchor of happiness.
10132{_}7870{_}The girl was dimly aware that she was holding to this.
10132{_}7871{_}She was simple and unsophisticated enough to consider Paul's opinion infallible.
10132{_}7872{_}At the great cross-roads of life we are apt to ask the way of any body who happens to be near.
10132{_}7873{_}Catrina might perhaps have made a worse choice of counsel, for Paul was honest.
10132{_}7874{_}"As you put it," she said, "it is clearly my duty.
10132{_}7875{_}There is a sort of consolation in that, however painful it may be at the time.
10132{_}7876{_}I suppose it is consolatory to look back and think that at all events one did one's duty."
10132{_}7877{_}"I don't know," answered Paul simply; "I suppose so."
10132{_}7878{_}Looking back was not included in his method of life, which was rather characterized by a large faith and a forward pressure.
10132{_}7879{_}Whenever there was question of considering life as an abstract, he drew within his shell with a manlike shyness.
10132{_}7880{_}He had no generalities ready for each emergency.
10132{_}7881{_}"Would father have gone alone?"
10132{_}7882{_}she asked, with a very human thrill of hope in her voice.
10132{_}7883{_}"No," answered Paul steadily, "I think not.
10132{_}7884{_}But you can ask him."
10132{_}7885{_}They had never been so distant as they were at this moment--so cold, such mere acquaintances.
10132{_}7886{_}And they had played together in one nursery.
10132{_}7887{_}"Of course, if that is the case," said the girl, "my duty is quite clear."
10132{_}7888{_}"It required some persuasion to make him consent to go, even with you," said Paul.
10132{_}7889{_}A rough piece of going--for there was no road--debarred further conversation at this time.
10132{_}7890{_}The sleigh rolled and bumped over one fallen tree after another.
10132{_}7891{_}Paul, with his feet stretched out, wedged firmly into the sleigh, encouraged the tired horses with rein and voice.
10132{_}7892{_}Catrina was compelled to steady herself with both hands on the bar of the apron; for the apron of a Russian sleigh is a heavy piece of leather stretched on a wooden bar.
10132{_}7893{_}"Then you think my duty is quite clear?"
10132{_}7894{_}repeated the girl at length.
10132{_}7895{_}Paul did not answer at once.
10132{_}7896{_}"I am sure of it," he said.
10132{_}7897{_}And there the question ended.
10132{_}7898{_}Catrina Lanovitch, who had never been ruled by those about her, shaped her whole life unquestioningly upon an opinion.
10132{_}7899{_}They did not speak for some time, and then it was the girl who broke the silence.
10132{_}7900{_}"I have a confession to make and a favor to ask," she said bluntly.
10132{_}7901{_}Paul's attitude denoted attention, but he said nothing.
10132{_}7902{_}"It is about the Baron de Chauxville," she said.
10132{_}7903{_}"Ah!"
10132{_}7904{_}"I am a coward," she went on.
10132{_}7905{_}"I did not know it before.
10132{_}7906{_}It is rather humiliating.
10132{_}7907{_}I have been trying for some weeks to tell you something, but I am horribly afraid of it.
10132{_}7908{_}I am afraid you will despise me.
10132{_}7909{_}I have been a fool--worse, perhaps.
10132{_}7910{_}I never knew that Claude de Chauxville was the sort of person he is.
10132{_}7911{_}I allowed him to find out things about me which he never should have known--my own private affairs, I mean.
10132{_}7912{_}Then I became frightened, and he tried to make use of me.
10132{_}7913{_}I think he makes use of every-body.
10132{_}7914{_}_You_ know what he is."
10132{_}7915{_}"Yes," answered Paul, "I know."
10132{_}7916{_}"He hates you," she went on.
10132{_}7917{_}"I do not want to make mischief, but I suppose he wanted to marry the princess.
10132{_}7918{_}His vanity was wounded because she preferred you, and he wanted to be avenged upon you.
10132{_}7919{_}Wounds to the vanity never heal.
10132{_}7920{_}I do not know how he did it, Paul, but he made me help him in his schemes.
10132{_}7921{_}I could have prevented you from going to the bear hunt, for I suspected him then.
10132{_}7922{_}I could have prevented my mother from inviting him to Thors.
10132{_}7923{_}I could have put a thousand difficulties in his way, but I did not.
10132{_}7924{_}I helped him.
10132{_}7925{_}I told him about the people and who were the worst--who had been influenced by the Nihilists and who would not work.
10132{_}7926{_}I allowed him to stay on here and carry out his plan.
10132{_}7927{_}All this trouble among the peasants is his handiwork.
10132{_}7928{_}He has organized a regular rising against you.
10132{_}7929{_}He is horribly clever.
10132{_}7930{_}He left us yesterday, but I am convinced that he is in the neighborhood still."
10132{_}7931{_}She stopped and reflected.
10132{_}7932{_}There was something wanting in the story, which she could not supply.
10132{_}7933{_}It was a motive.
10132{_}7934{_}A half-confession is almost an impossibility.
10132{_}7935{_}When we speak of ourselves it must be all or nothing--preferably, nothing.
10132{_}7936{_}"I do not know why I did it," she said.
10132{_}7937{_}"It was a sort of period I went through.
10132{_}7938{_}I cannot explain."
10132{_}7939{_}He did not ask her to do so.
10132{_}7940{_}They were singularly like brother and sister in their mental attitude.
10132{_}7941{_}They had driven through twenty miles of forest which belonged to one or other of them.
10132{_}7942{_}Each was touched by the intangible, inexplicable dignity that belongs to the possession of great lands--to the inheritance of a great name.
10132{_}7943{_}"That is the confession," she said.
10132{_}7944{_}He gave a little laugh.
10132{_}7945{_}"If none of us had worse than that upon our consciences," he answered, "there would be little harm in the world, De Chauxville's schemes have only hurried on a crisis which was foreordained.
10132{_}7946{_}The progress of humanity cannot be stayed.
10132{_}7947{_}They have tried to stay it in this country.
10132{_}7948{_}They will go on trying until the crash comes.
10132{_}7949{_}What is the favor you have to ask?"
10132{_}7950{_}"You must leave Osterno," she urged earnestly; "it is unsafe to delay even a few hours.
10132{_}7951{_}M. de Chauxville said there would be no danger.
10132{_}7952{_}I believed him then, but I do not now.
10132{_}7953{_}Besides, I know the peasants.
10132{_}7954{_}They are hard to rouse, but once excited they are uncontrollable.
10132{_}7955{_}They are afraid of nothing.
10132{_}7956{_}You must get away to-night."
10132{_}7957{_}Paul made no answer.
10132{_}7958{_}She turned slowly in her seat and looked into his face by the light of the waning moon.
10132{_}7959{_}"Do you mean that you will not go?"
10132{_}7960{_}He met her glance with his grave, slow smile.
10132{_}7961{_}"There is no question of going," he answered.
10132{_}7962{_}"You must know that."
10132{_}7963{_}She did not attempt to persuade.
10132{_}7964{_}Perhaps there was something in his voice which she as a Russian understood--a ring of that which we call pig-headedness in others.
10132{_}7965{_}"It must be splendid to be a man," she said suddenly, in a ringing voice.
10132{_}7966{_}"One feeling in me made me ask you the favor, while another was a sense of gladness at your certain refusal.
10132{_}7967{_}I wish I was a man.
10132{_}7968{_}I envy you.
10132{_}7969{_}You do not know how I envy you, Paul."
10132{_}7970{_}Paul gave a quiet laugh--such a laugh as one hears in the trenches after the low hum of a passing ball.
10132{_}7971{_}"If it is danger you want, you will have more than I in the next week," he answered.
10132{_}7972{_}"Steinmetz and I knew that you were the only woman in Russia who could get your father safely out of the country.
10132{_}7973{_}That is why I came for you."
10132{_}7974{_}The girl did not answer at once.
10132{_}7975{_}They were driving on the road again now, and the sleigh was running smoothly.
10132{_}7976{_}"I suppose," she said reflectively at length, "that the secret of the enormous influence you exercise over all who come in contact with you is that you drag the best out of every one--the best that is in them."
10132{_}7977{_}Paul did not answer.
10132{_}7978{_}"What is that light?"
10132{_}7979{_}she asked suddenly, laying her hand on the thick fur of his sleeve.
10132{_}7980{_}She was not nervous, but very watchful.
10132{_}7981{_}"There--straight in front."
10132{_}7982{_}"It is the sleigh," replied Paul, "with your father and Steinmetz.
10132{_}7983{_}I arranged that they should meet us at the cross-roads.
10132{_}7984{_}You must be at the Volga before daylight.
10132{_}7985{_}Send the horses on to Tver.
10132{_}7986{_}I have given you Minna and The Warrior; they can do the journey with one hour's rest, but you must drive them."
10132{_}7987{_}Catrina had swayed forward against the bar of the apron in a strange way, for the road was quite smooth.
10132{_}7988{_}She placed her gloved hands on the bar and held herself upright with a peculiar effort.
10132{_}7989{_}"What?"
10132{_}7990{_}said Paul.
10132{_}7991{_}For she had made an inarticulate sound.
10132{_}7992{_}"Nothing," she answered.
10132{_}7993{_}Then, after a pause, "I did not know that we were to go so soon.
10132{_}7994{_}That was all."
10132{_}7995{_}CHAPTER XLII   THE STORM BURSTS  The large drawing-room was brilliantly lighted.
10132{_}7996{_}Another weary day had dragged to its close.
10132{_}7997{_}It was the Tuesday evening--the last Tuesday in March five years ago.
10132{_}7998{_}The starosta had not been near the castle all day.
10132{_}7999{_}Steinmetz and Paul had never lost sight of the ladies since breakfast time.
10132{_}8000{_}They had not ventured out of doors.
10132{_}8001{_}There was in the atmosphere a sense of foreboding--the stillness of a crisis.
10132{_}8002{_}Etta had been defiant and silent--a dangerous humor--all day.
10132{_}8003{_}Maggie had watched Paul's face with steadfast, quiet eyes full of courage, but she knew now that there was danger.
10132{_}8004{_}The conversation at breakfast and luncheon had been maintained by Steinmetz--always collected and a little humorous.
10132{_}8005{_}It was now dinner time.
10132{_}8006{_}The whole castle was brilliantly lighted, as if for a great assembly of guests.
10132{_}8007{_}During the last week a fuller state--a greater ceremony--had been observed by Paul's orders, and Steinmetz had thought more than once of that historical event which appealed to his admiration most--the Indian Mutiny.
10132{_}8008{_}Maggie was in the drawing-room alone.
10132{_}8009{_}She was leaning one hand and arm on the mantel-piece, looking thoughtfully into the fire.
10132{_}8010{_}The rustle of silk made her turn her head.
10132{_}8011{_}It was Etta, beautifully dressed, with a white face and eyes dull with suspense.
10132{_}8012{_}"I think it is warmer to-night," said Maggie, urged by a sudden necessity of speech, hampered by a sudden chill at the heart.
10132{_}8013{_}"Yes," answered Etta.
10132{_}8014{_}And she shivered.
10132{_}8015{_}For a moment there was a little silence and Etta looked at the clock.
10132{_}8016{_}It was ten minutes to seven.
10132{_}8017{_}A high wind was blowing, the first of the equinoctial gales heralding the spring.
10132{_}8018{_}The sound of the wind in the great chimney was like the moaning of high rigging at sea.
10132{_}8019{_}The door opened and Steinmetz came in.
10132{_}8020{_}Etta's face hardened, her lips closed with a snap.
10132{_}8021{_}Steinmetz looked at her and at Maggie.
10132{_}8022{_}For once he seemed to have no pleasantry ready for use.
10132{_}8023{_}He walked toward a table where some books and newspapers lay in pleasant profusion.
10132{_}8024{_}He was standing there when Paul came into the room.
10132{_}8025{_}The prince glanced at Maggie.
10132{_}8026{_}He saw where his wife stood, but he did not look at her.
10132{_}8027{_}Steinmetz was writing something on half a sheet of notepaper, in pencil.
10132{_}8028{_}He pushed it across the table toward Paul, who drew it nearer to him.
10132{_}8029{_}"Are you armed?"
10132{_}8030{_}were the written words.
10132{_}8031{_}Paul crushed the paper in the hollow of his hand and threw it into the fire, where it burned away.
10132{_}8032{_}He also glanced at the clock.
10132{_}8033{_}It was five minutes to seven.
10132{_}8034{_}Suddenly the door was thrown open and a manservant rushed in--pale, confused, terror-stricken.
10132{_}8035{_}He was a giant footman in the gorgeous livery of the Alexis.
10132{_}8036{_}"Excellency," he stammered in Russian, "the castle is surrounded--they will kill us--they will burn us out----"  He stopped abashed before Paul's pointing finger and stony face.
10132{_}8037{_}"Leave the room!"
10132{_}8038{_}said Paul.
10132{_}8039{_}"You forget yourself."
10132{_}8040{_}Through the open door-way to which Paul pointed peered the ashen faces of other servants huddled together like sheep.
10132{_}8041{_}"Leave the room!"
10132{_}8042{_}repeated Paul, and the man obeyed him, walking to the door unsteadily with quivering chin.
10132{_}8043{_}On the threshold he paused.
10132{_}8044{_}Paul stood pointing to the door.
10132{_}8045{_}He had a poise of the head--some sudden awakening of the blood that had coursed in the veins of hereditary potentates.
10132{_}8046{_}Maggie looked at him; she had never known him like this.
10132{_}8047{_}She had known the man, she had never encountered the prince.
10132{_}8048{_}The big clock over the castle boomed out the hour, and at the same instant there arose a roar like the voice of the surf on a Malabar shore.
10132{_}8049{_}There was a crashing of glass almost in the room itself.
10132{_}8050{_}Already Steinmetz was drawing the curtains closer over the windows in order to prevent the light from filtering through the interstices of the closed shutters.
10132{_}8051{_}"Only stones," he said to Paul, with his grim smile; "it might have been bullets."
10132{_}8052{_}As if in corroboration of his suggestion the sharp ring of more than one fire-arm rang out above the dull roar of many voices.
10132{_}8053{_}Steinmetz crossed the room to where Etta was standing, white-lipped, by the fire.
10132{_}8054{_}Her clenched hand was gripping Maggie's wrist.
10132{_}8055{_}She was half hidden behind her cousin.
10132{_}8056{_}Maggie was looking at Paul.
10132{_}8057{_}Etta was obviously conscious of Steinmetz's gaze and approach.
10132{_}8058{_}"I asked you before to tell me all you knew," he said.
10132{_}8059{_}"You refused.
10132{_}8060{_}Will you do it now?"
10132{_}8061{_}Etta met his glance for a moment, shrugged her shoulders, and turned her back on him.
10132{_}8062{_}Paul was standing in the open door-way with his back turned toward them--alone.
10132{_}8063{_}The palace had never looked so vast as it did at that moment--brilliantly lighted, gorgeous, empty.
10132{_}8064{_}Through the hail of blows on the stout doors, the rattle of stones at the windows, the prince could hear yells of execration and the wild laughter that is bred of destruction.
10132{_}8065{_}He turned and entered the room.
10132{_}8066{_}His face was gray and terrible.
10132{_}8067{_}"They have no chance," he said, "of effecting an entrance by force; the lower windows are barred.
10132{_}8068{_}They have no ladders, Steinmetz and I have seen to that.
10132{_}8069{_}We have been expecting this for some days."
10132{_}8070{_}He turned toward Steinmetz as if seeking confirmation.
10132{_}8071{_}The din was increasing.
10132{_}8072{_}When the German spoke he had to shout.
10132{_}8073{_}"We can beat them back if we like.
10132{_}8074{_}We can shoot them down from the windows.
10132{_}8075{_}But"--he paused, shrugged his shoulders, and laughed--"what will you!
10132{_}8076{_}This prince will not shoot his father's serfs."
10132{_}8077{_}"We must leave you," went on Paul.
10132{_}8078{_}"We must beware of treachery.
10132{_}8079{_}Whatever happens, we shall not leave the house.
10132{_}8080{_}If the worst comes, we make our last stand in this room.
10132{_}8081{_}Whatever happens, stay here till we come."
10132{_}8082{_}He left the room, followed by Steinmetz.
10132{_}8083{_}There were only three doors in the impregnable stone walls; the great entrance, a side door for use in times of deep snow, and the small concealed entrance by which the starosta was in the habit of reaching his masters.
10132{_}8084{_}For a moment the two men stood at the head of the stairs listening to the wild commotion.
10132{_}8085{_}They were turning to descend the state stairs when a piercing shriek, immediately drowned by a yell of triumph, broke the silence of the interior of the castle.
10132{_}8086{_}There was a momentary stillness, followed by another shriek.
10132{_}8087{_}"They are in!"
10132{_}8088{_}said Steinmetz.
10132{_}8089{_}"The side door."
10132{_}8090{_}And the two men looked at each other with wide eyes full of knowledge.
10132{_}8091{_}As they ran to the foot of the broad staircase the tramp of scuffling feet, the roar of angry voices, came through the passages from the back of curtained doorways.
10132{_}8092{_}The servants' quarters seemed to be pandemonium.
10132{_}8093{_}The sounds approached.
10132{_}8094{_}"Half-way up!"
10132{_}8095{_}said Paul, and they ran half-way up the broad staircase side by side.
10132{_}8096{_}There they stood and waited.
10132{_}8097{_}In a moment the baize doors were burst open, and a scuffling mass of men and women poured into the hall--a very sewer of humanity.
10132{_}8098{_}A yell of execration signalized their recognition of the prince.
10132{_}8099{_}"They are mad!"
10132{_}8100{_}said Steinmetz, as the crowd surged forward toward the stairs with waving arms and the dull gleam of steel; with wild faces turned upward, wild mouths bellowing hatred and murder.
10132{_}8101{_}"It is a chance--it may stop them!"
10132{_}8102{_}said Steinmetz.
10132{_}8103{_}His arm was outstretched steadily.
10132{_}8104{_}A loud report, a little puff of smoke shooting upward to the gilded ceiling, and for one brief moment the crowd stood still, watching one of their ringleaders, who was turning and twisting on his side half a dozen steps from the bottom.
10132{_}8105{_}The man writhed in silence with his hand to his breast, and the crowd stood aghast.
10132{_}8106{_}He held up his hand and gazed at it with a queer stupefaction.
10132{_}8107{_}The blood dripped from his fingers.
10132{_}8108{_}Then his chin went up as if some one was gripping the back of his neck.
10132{_}8109{_}He turned over slowly and rolled to the bottom of the stairs.
10132{_}8110{_}Then Paul raised his voice.
10132{_}8111{_}"Listen to me!"
10132{_}8112{_}he said.
10132{_}8113{_}But he got no farther, for some one shot at him from the background, over the frantic heads of the others, and missed him.
10132{_}8114{_}The bullet lodged in the wall at the head of the stairs, in the jamb of the gorgeous door-way.
10132{_}8115{_}It is there to-day.
10132{_}8116{_}There was a yell of hatred, and an ugly charge toward the stairs; but the sight of the two revolvers held them there--motionless for a few moments.
10132{_}8117{_}Those in front pushed back, while the shouters in the safe background urged them forward by word and gesture.
10132{_}8118{_}Two men holding a hundred in check!
10132{_}8119{_}But one of the two was a prince, which makes all the difference, and will continue to make that difference, despite halfpenny journalism, until the end of the world.
10132{_}8120{_}"What do you want?"
10132{_}8121{_}cried Paul.
10132{_}8122{_}"Oh, I will wait!"
10132{_}8123{_}he shouted, in the next pause.
10132{_}8124{_}"There is plenty of time--when you are tired of shouting."
10132{_}8125{_}Several of them proceeded to tell him what they wanted.
10132{_}8126{_}An old story, too stale for repetition here.
10132{_}8127{_}Paul recognized in the din of many voices the tinkling arguments of the professional agitator all the world over--the cry of "Equality!
10132{_}8128{_}Equality!"
10132{_}8129{_}when men are obviously created unequal.
10132{_}8130{_}"Look out!"
10132{_}8131{_}said Paul; "I believe they are going to make a rush."
10132{_}8132{_}All the while the foremost men were edging toward the stairs, while the densely packed throng at the back were struggling among themselves.
10132{_}8133{_}In the passages behind, some were yelling and screaming with a wild intonation which Steinmetz recognized.
10132{_}8134{_}He had been through the Commune.
10132{_}8135{_}"Those fellows at the back have been killing some one," he said; "I can tell by their voices.
10132{_}8136{_}They are drunk with the sight of blood."
10132{_}8137{_}Some new orator gained the ears of the rabble at this moment, and the ill-kempt heads swayed from side to side.
10132{_}8138{_}"It is useless," he cried, "telling him what you want.
10132{_}8139{_}He will not give it you.
10132{_}8140{_}Go and take it!
10132{_}8141{_}Go and take it, little fathers; that is the only way!"
10132{_}8142{_}Steinmetz raised his hand and peered down into the crowd, looking for the man of eloquence, and the voice was hushed.
10132{_}8143{_}At this moment, however, the yelling increased, and through the door-way leading to the servants' quarters came a stream of men--bloodstained, ragged, torn.
10132{_}8144{_}They were waving arms and implements above their heads.
10132{_}8145{_}"Down with the aristocrats!
10132{_}8146{_}kill them--kill them!"
10132{_}8147{_}they were shrieking.
10132{_}8148{_}A little volley of fire-arms further excited them.
10132{_}8149{_}But vodka is not a good thing to shoot upon, and Paul stood untouched, waiting, as he had said, until they were tired of shouting.
10132{_}8150{_}"Now," yelled Steinmetz to him in English, "we must go.
10132{_}8151{_}We can make a stand at the head of the stairs, then the door-way, then----" He shrugged his shoulders.
10132{_}8152{_}"Then--the end," he added, as they moved up the stairs step by step, backward.
10132{_}8153{_}"My very good friend," he went on, "at the door we must begin to shoot them down.
10132{_}8154{_}It is our only chance.
10132{_}8155{_}It is, moreover, our duty toward the ladies."
10132{_}8156{_}"There is one alternative," answered Paul.
10132{_}8157{_}"The Moscow Doctor?"
10132{_}8158{_}"Yes."
10132{_}8159{_}"They may turn," said Paul; "they are just in that humor."
10132{_}8160{_}The new-comers were the most dangerous.
10132{_}8161{_}They were forcing their way to the front.
10132{_}8162{_}There was no doubt that, as soon as they could penetrate the densely packed mob, they would charge up the stairs, even in face of a heavy fire.
10132{_}8163{_}The reek of vodka was borne up in the heated atmosphere, mingled with the nauseating odor of filthy clothing.
10132{_}8164{_}"Go," said Steinmetz, "and put on your doctor's clothes.
10132{_}8165{_}I can keep them back for a few minutes."
10132{_}8166{_}There was no time to be lost.
10132{_}8167{_}Paul slipped away, leaving Steinmetz alone at the summit of the state stairway, standing grimly, revolver in hand.
10132{_}8168{_}In the drawing-room Paul found Maggie, alone.
10132{_}8169{_}"Where is Etta?"
10132{_}8170{_}he asked.
10132{_}8171{_}"She left the room some time ago."
10132{_}8172{_}"But I told her to stay," said Paul.
10132{_}8173{_}To this Maggie made no answer.
10132{_}8174{_}She was looking at him with an anxious scrutiny.
10132{_}8175{_}"Did they shoot at you?"
10132{_}8176{_}she asked.
10132{_}8177{_}"Yes; but not straight," he answered, with a little laugh, as he hurried on.
10132{_}8178{_}In a few moments he was back in the drawing-room, a different man, in the rough, stained clothes of the Moscow Doctor.
10132{_}8179{_}The din on the stairs was louder.
10132{_}8180{_}Steinmetz was almost in the door-way.
10132{_}8181{_}He was shooting economically, picking his men.
10132{_}8182{_}With an effort Paul dragged one or two heavy pieces of furniture across the room, in the form of a rough barricade.
10132{_}8183{_}He pointed to the hearthrug where Maggie was to stand.
10132{_}8184{_}"Ready!"
10132{_}8185{_}he shouted to Steinmetz.
10132{_}8186{_}"Come!"
10132{_}8187{_}The German ran in, and Paul closed the barricade.
10132{_}8188{_}The rabble poured in at the open door, screaming and shouting.
10132{_}8189{_}Bloodstained, ragged, wild with the madness of murder, they crowded to the barricade.
10132{_}8190{_}There they stopped, gazing stupidly at Paul.
10132{_}8191{_}"The Moscow Doctor--the Moscow Doctor!"
10132{_}8192{_}passed from lip to lip.
10132{_}8193{_}It was the women who shouted it the loudest.
10132{_}8194{_}Like the wind through a forest it swept out of the room and down the stairs.
10132{_}8195{_}Those crowding up pushed on and uttered the words as they came.
10132{_}8196{_}The room was packed with them.
10132{_}8197{_}"Yes!"
10132{_}8198{_}shouted Steinmetz, at the top of his great voice, "and the prince!"
10132{_}8199{_}He knew the note to strike, and struck with a sure hand.
10132{_}8200{_}The barricade was torn aside, and the people swept forward, falling on their knees, grovelling at Paul's feet, kissing the hem of his garment, seizing his strong hands in theirs.
10132{_}8201{_}It was a mighty harvest.
10132{_}8202{_}That which is sown in the people's hearts bears a thousandfold at last.
10132{_}8203{_}"Get them out of the place--open the big doors," said Paul to Steinmetz.
10132{_}8204{_}He stood cold and grave among them.
10132{_}8205{_}Some of them were already sneaking toward the door--the ringleaders, the talkers from the towns--mindful of their own necks in this change of feeling.
10132{_}8206{_}Steinmetz hustled them out, bidding them take their dead with them.
10132{_}8207{_}Some of the servants reappeared, peeping, white-faced, behind curtains.
10132{_}8208{_}When the last villager had crossed the threshold, these ran forward to close and bar the great doors.
10132{_}8209{_}"No," said Paul, from the head of the stairs, "leave them open."
10132{_}8210{_}So the great doors stood defiantly open.
10132{_}8211{_}The lights of the state staircase flared out over the village as the peasants crept crest-fallen to their cottages.
10132{_}8212{_}They glanced up shamefacedly, but they had no word to say.
10132{_}8213{_}Steinmetz, in the drawing-room, looked at Paul with his resigned semi-humorous shrug of the shoulders.
10132{_}8214{_}"Touch-and-go, mein lieber!"
10132{_}8215{_}he said.
10132{_}8216{_}"Yes; an end of Russia for us," answered the prince.
10132{_}8217{_}He moved toward the door leading through to the old castle.
10132{_}8218{_}"I am going to look for Etta," he said.
10132{_}8219{_}"And I," said Steinmetz, going to the other entrance, "am going to see who opened the side door."
10132{_}8220{_}CHAPTER XLIII   BEHIND THE VEIL  "Will you come with me?"
10132{_}8221{_}said Paul to Maggie.
10132{_}8222{_}"I will send the servants to put this room to rights."
10132{_}8223{_}Maggie followed him out of the room, and together they went through the passages, calling Etta and looking for her.
10132{_}8224{_}There was an air of gloom and chilliness in the rooms of the old castle.
10132{_}8225{_}The outline of the great stones, dimly discernible through the wall-paper, was singularly suggestive of a fortress thinly disguised.
10132{_}8226{_}"I suppose," said Paul, "that Etta lost her nerve."
10132{_}8227{_}"Yes," answered Maggie doubtfully; "I think it was that."
10132{_}8228{_}Paul went on.
10132{_}8229{_}He carried a lamp in one steady hand.
10132{_}8230{_}"We shall probably find her in one of these rooms," he said.
10132{_}8231{_}"It is so easy to lose one's self among the passages and staircases."
10132{_}8232{_}They passed on through the great smoking-room, with its hunting trophies.
10132{_}8233{_}The lynx, with its face of Claude de Chauxville, grinned at them darkly from its pedestal.
10132{_}8234{_}Half-way down the stairs leading to the side door they met Steinmetz coming hastily up.
10132{_}8235{_}His face was white and drawn with horror.
10132{_}8236{_}"You must not go down here," he said, in a husky voice, barring the passage with his arm.
10132{_}8237{_}"Why not?"
10132{_}8238{_}"Go up again!"
10132{_}8239{_}said Steinmetz breathlessly.
10132{_}8240{_}"You must not go down here."
10132{_}8241{_}Paul laid his hand on the broad arm stretched across the stairway.
10132{_}8242{_}For a moment it almost appeared to be a physical struggle, then Steinmetz stepped aside.
10132{_}8243{_}"I beg of you," he said, "not to go down."
10132{_}8244{_}And Paul went on, followed by Steinmetz, and behind them, Maggie.
10132{_}8245{_}At the foot of the stairs a broader passage led to the side door, and from this other passages opened into the servants' quarters, and communicated through the kitchens with the modern building.
10132{_}8246{_}It was evident that the door leading to the grassy slope at the back of the castle was open, for a cold wind blew up the stairs and made the lamps flicker.
10132{_}8247{_}At the end of the passage Paul stopped.
10132{_}8248{_}Steinmetz was a little behind him, holding Maggie back.
10132{_}8249{_}The two lamps lighted up the passage and showed the white form of the Princess Etta lying huddled up against the wall.
10132{_}8250{_}The face was hidden, but there was no mistaking the beautiful dress and hair.
10132{_}8251{_}It could only be Etta.
10132{_}8252{_}Paul stooped down and looked at her, but he did not touch her.
10132{_}8253{_}He went a few paces forward and closed the door.
10132{_}8254{_}Beyond Etta a black form lay across the passage, all trodden underfoot and dishevelled.
10132{_}8255{_}Paul held the lamp down, and through the mud and blood Claude de Chauxville's clear-cut features were outlined.
10132{_}8256{_}Death is always unmistakable, though it be shown by nothing more than a heap of muddy clothes.
10132{_}8257{_}Claude de Chauxville was lying across the passage.
10132{_}8258{_}He had been trodden underfoot by the stream of maddened peasants who had entered by this door which had been opened for them, whom Steinmetz had checked at the foot of the stairs by shooting their ringleader.
10132{_}8259{_}De Chauxville's scalp was torn away by a blow, probably given with a spade or some blunt instrument.
10132{_}8260{_}His hand, all muddy and bloodstained, still held a revolver.
10132{_}8261{_}The other hand was stretched out toward Etta, who lay across his feet, crouching against the wall.
10132{_}8262{_}Death had found and left her in an attitude of fear, shielding her bowed head from a blow with her upraised hands.
10132{_}8263{_}Her loosened hair fell in a long wave of gold down to the bloodstained hand outstretched toward her.
10132{_}8264{_}She was kneeling in De Chauxville's blood, which stained the stone floor of the passage.
10132{_}8265{_}Paul leaned forward and laid his fingers on the bare arm, just below a bracelet which gleamed in the lamplight.
10132{_}8266{_}She was quite dead.
10132{_}8267{_}He held a lamp close to her.
10132{_}8268{_}There was no mark or scratch upon her arm or shoulder.
10132{_}8269{_}The blow which had torn her hair down had killed her without any disfigurement.
10132{_}8270{_}The silken skirt of her dress, which lay across the passage, was trampled and stained by the tread of a hundred feet.
10132{_}8271{_}Then Paul went to Claude de Chauxville.
10132{_}8272{_}He stooped down and slipped his skilled fingers inside the torn and mud-stained clothing.
10132{_}8273{_}Here also was death.
10132{_}8274{_}Paul stood upright and looked at them as they lay, silent, motionless, with their tale untold.
10132{_}8275{_}Maggie and Steinmetz stood watching him.
10132{_}8276{_}He went to the door, which was of solid oak four inches thick, and examined the fastenings.
10132{_}8277{_}There had been no damage done to bolt, or lock, or hinge.
10132{_}8278{_}The door had been opened from the inside.
10132{_}8279{_}He looked slowly round, measuring the distances.
10132{_}8280{_}"What is the meaning of it?"
10132{_}8281{_}he said at length to Steinmetz, in a dull voice.
10132{_}8282{_}Maggie winced at the sound of it.
10132{_}8283{_}Steinmetz did not answer at once, but hesitated--after the manner of a man weighing words which will never be forgotten by their hearers.
10132{_}8284{_}"It seems to me," he said, with a slow, wise charity, the best of its kind, "quite clear that De Chauxville died in trying to save her--the rest must be only guesswork."
10132{_}8285{_}Maggie had come forward and was standing beside him.
10132{_}8286{_}"And in guessing let us be charitable--is it not so?"
10132{_}8287{_}he said, turning to her, with a twist of his humorous lips.
10132{_}8288{_}"I suppose," he went on, after a little pause, "that Claude de Chauxville has been at the bottom of all our trouble.
10132{_}8289{_}All his life he has been one of the stormy petrels of diplomacy.
10132{_}8290{_}Wherever he has gone trouble has followed later.
10132{_}8291{_}By some means he obtained sufficient mastery over the princess to compel her to obey his orders.
10132{_}8292{_}The means he employed were threats.
10132{_}8293{_}He had it in his power to make mischief, and in such affairs a woman is so helpless that we may well forgive that which she may do in a moment of panic.
10132{_}8294{_}I imagine that he frightened the poor lady into obedience to his command that she should open this door.
10132{_}8295{_}Before dinner, when we were all in the drawing-room, I noted a little mark of dust on the white silk skirt of her dress.
10132{_}8296{_}At the time I thought only that her maid had been careless.
10132{_}8297{_}Perhaps you noticed it, mademoiselle?
10132{_}8298{_}Ladies note such things."
10132{_}8299{_}He turned to Maggie, who nodded her head.
10132{_}8300{_}"That," he went on, "was the dust of these old passages.
10132{_}8301{_}She had been down here.
10132{_}8302{_}She had opened this door."
10132{_}8303{_}He spread out his hands in deprecation.
10132{_}8304{_}In his quaint Germanic way he held one hand out over the two motionless forms in mute prayer that they might be forgiven.
10132{_}8305{_}"We all have our faults," he said.
10132{_}8306{_}"Who are we to judge each other?
10132{_}8307{_}If we understood all, we might pardon.
10132{_}8308{_}The two strongest human motives are ambition and fear.
10132{_}8309{_}She was ruled by both.
10132{_}8310{_}I myself have seen her under the influence of sudden panic.
10132{_}8311{_}I have noted the working of her great ambition.
10132{_}8312{_}She was probably deceived at every turn by that man, who was a scoundrel.
10132{_}8313{_}He is dead, and death is understood to wipe out all debts.
10132{_}8314{_}If I were a better man than I am, I might speak well of him.
10132{_}8315{_}But--ach Gott!
10132{_}8316{_}that man was a scoundrel!
10132{_}8317{_}I think the good God will judge between them and forgive that poor woman.
10132{_}8318{_}She must have repented of her action when she heard the clatter of the rioters all round the castle.
10132{_}8319{_}I am sure she did that.
10132{_}8320{_}I am sure she came down here to shut the door, and found Claude de Chauxville here.
10132{_}8321{_}They were probably talking together when the poor mad fools who killed them came round to this side of the castle and found them.
10132{_}8322{_}They recognized her as the princess.
10132{_}8323{_}They probably mistook him for the prince.
10132{_}8324{_}It is what men call a series of coincidences.
10132{_}8325{_}I wonder what God calls it?"
10132{_}8326{_}He broke off, and, stooping down, he drew the lapel of the Frenchman's cloak gently over the marred face.
10132{_}8327{_}"And let us remember," he said, "that he tried to save her.
10132{_}8328{_}Some lives are so.
10132{_}8329{_}At the very end a little reparation is made.
10132{_}8330{_}In life he was her evil genius.
10132{_}8331{_}When he died they trampled him underfoot in order to reach her.
10132{_}8332{_}Mademoiselle, will you come?"
10132{_}8333{_}He took Maggie by the arm and led her gently away.
10132{_}8334{_}She was shaking all over, but his hand was steady and wholly kind.
10132{_}8335{_}He led her up the narrow stairs to her own room.
10132{_}8336{_}In the little boudoir the fire was burning brightly; the lamps were lighted, just as the maid had left them at the first alarm.
10132{_}8337{_}Maggie sat down, and quite suddenly she burst into tears.
10132{_}8338{_}Steinmetz did not leave her.
10132{_}8339{_}He stood beside her, gently stroking her shoulder with his stout fingers.
10132{_}8340{_}He said nothing, but the gray mustache only half concealed his lips, which were twisted with a little smile full of tenderness and sympathy.
10132{_}8341{_}Maggie was the first to speak.
10132{_}8342{_}"I am all right now," she said.
10132{_}8343{_}"Please do not wait any longer, and do not think me a very weak-minded person.
10132{_}8344{_}Poor Etta!"
10132{_}8345{_}Steinmetz moved away toward the door.
10132{_}8346{_}"Yes," he said; "poor Etta!
10132{_}8347{_}It is often those who get on in the world who need the world's pity most."
10132{_}8348{_}At the door he stopped.
10132{_}8349{_}"To-morrow," he said, "I will take you home to England.
10132{_}8350{_}Is that agreeable to you, mademoiselle?"
10132{_}8351{_}She smiled at him sadly through her tears.
10132{_}8352{_}"Yes, I should like that," she said.
10132{_}8353{_}"This country is horrible.
10132{_}8354{_}You are very kind to me."
10132{_}8355{_}Steinmetz went down stairs and found Paul at the door talking to a young officer, who slowly dismounted and lounged into the hall, conscious of his brilliant uniform--of his own physical capacity to show off any uniform to full advantage.
10132{_}8356{_}He was a lieutenant in a Cossack regiment, and as he bowed to Steinmetz, whom Paul introduced, he swung off his high astrakhan cap with a flourish, showing a fair boyish face.
10132{_}8357{_}"Yes," he continued to Paul in English; "the general sent me over with a sotnia of men, and pretty hungry you will find them.
10132{_}8358{_}We have covered the whole distance since daybreak.
10132{_}8359{_}A report reached the old gentleman that the whole countryside was about to rise against you."
10132{_}8360{_}"Who spread the report?"
10132{_}8361{_}asked Steinmetz.
10132{_}8362{_}"I believe it originated down at the wharfs.
10132{_}8363{_}It has been traced to an old man and his daughter,--a sort of pedler, I think, who took a passage down the river,--but where they heard the rumor I don't know."
10132{_}8364{_}Paul and Steinmetz carefully avoided looking at each other.
10132{_}8365{_}They knew that Catrina and Stepan Lanovitch had sent back assistance.
10132{_}8366{_}"Of course," said Paul, "I am very glad to see you, but I am equally glad to inform you that you are not wanted.
10132{_}8367{_}Steinmetz will tell you all about it, and when you are ready for dinner it will be ready for you.
10132{_}8368{_}I will give instructions that the men be cared for."
10132{_}8369{_}"Thanks.
10132{_}8370{_}The funny thing is that I am instructed, with your approval, to put the place under martial law and take charge."
10132{_}8371{_}"That will not be necessary, thanks," answered Paul, going out of the open door to speak to the wild-looking Cossacks sent for his protection.
10132{_}8372{_}In Russia, as in other countries where life is cheaply held, the death formalities are small.
10132{_}8373{_}It is only in England, where we are so careful for the individual and so careless of the type, that we have to pay for dying, and leave a mass of red-tape formalities for our friends.
10132{_}8374{_}While the young officer was changing his uniform for the evening finery which his servant's forethought had provided, Paul and Steinmetz hurriedly arranged what story of the evening should be given to the world.
10132{_}8375{_}Knowing the country as they did, they were enabled to tell a true tale, which was yet devoid of that small personal interest that gossips love.
10132{_}8376{_}And all the world ever knew was that the Princess Howard Alexis was killed by the revolted peasants while attempting to escape by a side door, and that the Baron Claude de Chauxville, who was staying in the neighborhood, met his death in attempting to save her from the fury of the mob.
10132{_}8377{_}On the recommendation of Karl Steinmetz, Paul placed the castle and village under martial law, and there and then gave the command to the young Cossack officer, pending further instructions from his general, commanding at Tver.
10132{_}8378{_}The officer dined with Steinmetz, and under the careful treatment of that diplomatist inaugurated a reign of military autocracy, which varied pleasingly between strict discipline and boyish neglect.
10132{_}8379{_}Before the master of the situation had slept off the effect of his hundred-mile ride and a heavy dinner, the next morning Steinmetz and Maggie were ready to start on their journey to England.
